TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Paths and Operations API Reference
DESCRIPTION: Defines the structure and key elements for `paths` and `operations` in OpenAPI 3.0 specifications. Includes details on path templating, supported HTTP methods, and common operation properties like `summary`, `description`, `tags`, `externalDocs`, `parameters`, and `responses`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Paths:
  Definition: Endpoints (resources), e.g., /users, /reports/summary/
  Location: Global `paths` section of the API specification
  Relative to: API server URL (`<server-url>/path`)
  Optional Properties:
    summary: Short description for the path
    description: Longer, multi-line description (supports Markdown)
  Path Templating:
    Syntax: Curly braces `{}` to mark path parameters, e.g., `/users/{id}`

Operations:
  Definition: HTTP methods used to manipulate paths
  Supported Methods: `get`, `post`, `put`, `patch`, `delete`, `head`, `options`, `trace`
  Uniqueness: A unique operation is a combination of a path and an HTTP method.
  Optional Properties:
    summary: Short description of what an operation does
    description: Longer, multi-line description (supports Markdown)
    tags: Used to group operations logically
    externalDocs: References an external resource for additional documentation
    parameters:
      Types: Path, query string, headers, cookies
      Details: See 'Describing Parameters' documentation
    requestBody:
      Purpose: Define data transmitted to the server (for POST, PUT, PATCH)
      Details: See 'Describing Request Body' documentation
    responses: Defines possible responses for the operation
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Referencing Components with $ref
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates the syntax for referencing a defined component, specifically a schema, using the `$ref` keyword with the path format '#/components/<type>/<name>'.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/components.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
$ref: "#/components/schemas/User"
```

TITLE: Detailed OpenAPI Operation with Parameters and Response Schema
DESCRIPTION: Provides a comprehensive example of an OpenAPI operation, including `tags`, `summary`, `description`, `operationId`, `parameters` (path parameter `id`), `responses` with content type and schema `$ref`, and `externalDocs`. It also defines a `User` schema in the `components` section.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{id}:
    get:
      tags:
        - Users
      summary: Gets a user by ID.
      description: >
        A detailed description of the operation.
        Use markdown for rich text representation,
        such as **bold**, *italic*, and [links](https://swagger.io).
      operationId: getUserById
      parameters:
        - name: id
          in: path
          description: User ID
          required: true
          schema:
            type: integer
            format: int64
      responses:
        "200":
          description: Successful operation
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"
      externalDocs:
        description: Learn more about user operations provided by this API.
        url: http://api.example.com/docs/user-operations/

components:
  schemas:
    User:
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
          format: int64
        name:
          type: string
      required:
        - id
        - name
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define a Basic OpenAPI 3.0 Specification
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates the fundamental structure of an OpenAPI 3.0 definition, including API metadata (`info`), server configurations (`servers`), and a basic path definition (`paths`) for a `/users` endpoint with a GET operation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/basic-structure.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
info:
  title: Sample API
  description: Optional multiline or single-line description in [CommonMark](http://commonmark.org/help/) or HTML.
  version: 0.1.9

servers:
  - url: http://api.example.com/v1
    description: Optional server description, e.g. Main (production) server
  - url: http://staging-api.example.com
    description: Optional server description, e.g. Internal staging server for testing

paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Returns a list of users.
      description: Optional extended description in CommonMark or HTML.
      responses:
        "200": # status code
          description: A JSON array of user names
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                type: array
                items:
                  type: string
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define Reusable OpenAPI 3.0 Schemas, Parameters, and Responses
DESCRIPTION: This YAML example demonstrates the structure of the `components` object in OpenAPI 3.0, showcasing how to define reusable data `schemas`, operation `parameters`, and API `responses`. These definitions can be referenced throughout the API specification to ensure consistency and reduce redundancy.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/components.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
components:
  #-------------------------------
  # Reusable schemas (data models)
  #-------------------------------
  schemas:
    User: # Can be referenced as '#/components/schemas/User'
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
          format: int64
        name:
          type: string

    Error: # Can be referenced as '#/components/schemas/Error'
      type: object
      properties:
        code:
          type: integer
        message:
          type: string

  #-------------------------------
  # Reusable operation parameters
  #-------------------------------
  parameters:
    offsetParam: # Can be referenced via '#/components/parameters/offsetParam'
      name: offset
      in: query
      description: Number of items to skip before returning the results.
      required: false
      schema:
        type: integer
        format: int32
        minimum: 0
        default: 0

    limitParam: # Can be referenced as '#/components/parameters/limitParam'
      name: limit
      in: query
      description: Maximum number of items to return.
      required: false
      schema:
        type: integer
        format: int32
        minimum: 1
        maximum: 100
        default: 20

  #-------------------------------
  # Reusable responses
  #-------------------------------
  responses:
    404NotFound: # Can be referenced as '#/components/responses/404NotFound'
      description: The specified resource was not found.

    ImageResponse: # Can be referenced as '#/components/responses/ImageResponse'
      description: An image.
      content:
        image/*:
          schema:
            type: string
            format: binary

    GenericError: # Can be referenced as '#/components/responses/GenericError'
      description: An error occurred.
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            $ref: "#/components/schemas/Error"
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Components Section Full Structure
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet provides a comprehensive overview of the `components` section in OpenAPI, listing all available subsections such as `schemas`, `parameters`, `securitySchemes`, and `responses`, which serve as containers for reusable API definitions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/components.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  # Reusable schemas (data models)
  schemas: ...

  # Reusable path, query, header and cookie parameters
  parameters: ...

  # Security scheme definitions (see Authentication)
  securitySchemes: ...

  # Reusable request bodies
  requestBodies: ...

  # Reusable responses, such as 401 Unauthorized or 400 Bad Request
  responses: ...

  # Reusable response headers
  headers: ...

  # Reusable examples
  examples: ...

  # Reusable links
  links: ...

  # Reusable callbacks
  callbacks: ...
```

TITLE: Reuse Schema for Multiple Media Types in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to reuse a common schema definition for multiple media types in an OpenAPI specification. By defining a schema object in the `components/schemas` section, it can be referenced using `$ref` across different media types, promoting reusability and reducing redundancy.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /employees:
    get:
      responses:
        "200": # Response
          description: OK
          content: # Response body
            application/json: # Media type
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/Employee" # Reference to object definition
            application/xml: # Media type
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/Employee" # Reference to object definition
components:
  schemas:
    Employee: # Object definition
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
        name:
          type: string
        fullTime:
          type: boolean
```

TITLE: Define OpenAPI 3.0 Request Body with `oneOf` Schema
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 YAML snippet demonstrates how to use the `oneOf` keyword within a request body schema. It specifies that the incoming JSON payload for the `/pets` PATCH operation must conform to exactly one of the referenced schemas, either `Cat` or `Dog`, ensuring type-specific validation for updates.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/oneof-anyof-allof-not.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
paths:
  /pets:
    patch:
      requestBody:
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              oneOf:
                - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Cat"
                - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Dog"
      responses:
        "200":
          description: Updated

components:
  schemas:
    Dog:
      type: object
      properties:
        bark:
          type: boolean
        breed:
          type: string
          enum: [Dingo, Husky, Retriever, Shepherd]
    Cat:
      type: object
      properties:
        hunts:
          type: boolean
        age:
          type: integer
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Paths After Component Refactoring
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates how to refactor an OpenAPI specification by moving the common 'User' object definition into the global `components/schemas` section and referencing it using `$ref`, thereby eliminating duplication.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/components.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{userId}:
    get:
      summary: Get a user by ID
      parameters: ...
      responses:
        "200":
          description: A single user.
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Get all users
      responses:
        "200":
          description: A list of users.
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                type: array
                items:
                  $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"

components:
  schemas:
    User:
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
        name:
          type: string
```

TITLE: Defining a Reusable User Schema
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define a reusable 'User' schema object within the 'components/schemas' section of an OpenAPI specification, available in both JSON and YAML formats.

  schemas:

          type: integer

          type: string

TITLE: OpenAPI Nullability with `nullable: true`
DESCRIPTION: Explains how OpenAPI 3.0 handles null values using `nullable: true` instead of an explicit `null` type. It provides examples of correct and incorrect usage and notes that `null` is distinct from an empty string.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
# Correct
type: integer
nullable: true

# Incorrect
type: null

# Incorrect as well
type:
  - integer
  - null
```

TITLE: Defining and Reusing Common Responses and Schemas in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This comprehensive OpenAPI 3.0 YAML example demonstrates how to define reusable HTTP responses (e.g., 401 Unauthorized, 404 Not Found) and their associated schemas (e.g., `Error`, `ArrayOfUsers`, `User`) within the global `components` object. These definitions are then referenced using `$ref` at the operation level, promoting consistency and reducing redundancy across multiple API endpoints like `/users` and `/users/{id}`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Gets a list of users.
      response:
        "200":
          description: OK
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/ArrayOfUsers"
        "401":
          $ref: "#/components/responses/Unauthorized" # <-----
  /users/{id}:
    get:
      summary: Gets a user by ID.
      response:
        "200":
          description: OK
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"
        "401":
          $ref: "#/components/responses/Unauthorized" # <-----
        "404":
          $ref: "#/components/responses/NotFound" # <-----

# Descriptions of common components
components:
  responses:
    NotFound:
      description: The specified resource was not found
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            $ref: "#/components/schemas/Error"
    Unauthorized:
      description: Unauthorized
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            $ref: "#/components/schemas/Error"

  schemas:
    # Schema for error response body
    Error:
      type: object
      properties:
        code:
          type: string
        message:
          type: string
      required:
        - code
        - message
```

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Security Description Keywords and Process
DESCRIPTION: This section explains the two primary keywords used to describe security in OpenAPI 3.0: `securitySchemes` for defining supported schemes and `security` for applying them. It outlines the two-step process: first defining schemes globally, then applying them either globally or to specific operations, detailing the purpose, location, and properties of each keyword.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
OpenAPI 3.0 Security Description Keywords:
- `securitySchemes`:
    - Purpose: Define all security schemes supported by the API.
    - Location: Global `components/securitySchemes` section.
    - Properties:
        - `type`:
            - `http`: Basic, Bearer, other HTTP schemes
            - `apiKey`: API keys, cookie authentication
            - `oauth2`: OAuth 2
            - `openIdConnect`: OpenID Connect Discovery
- `security`:
    - Purpose: Apply specific security schemes to the API or individual operations.
    - Location: Root level (global) or operation level.
    - Behavior: Global application unless overridden on operation level.
    - Syntax:
        - `- scheme name: []` (for schemes without scopes)
        - `- scheme name: [scope1, scope2]` (for schemes with scopes, e.g., OAuth2)
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define JSON Response Media Type in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define a JSON media type for a 200 OK response in OpenAPI 3.0, including schema definition for object properties (id, name, fullTime) and a sample example. This snippet shows the structure under `paths`, `responses`, `content`, and `schema`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /employees:
    get:
      summary: Returns a list of employees.
      responses:
        "200": # Response
          description: OK
          content: # Response body
            application/json: # Media type
              schema: # Must-have
                type: object # Data type
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                  name:
                    type: string
                  fullTime:
                    type: boolean
                example: # Sample data
                  id: 1
                  name: Jessica Right
                  fullTime: true
```

TITLE: Specify Alternate Request Body Schemas with oneOf/anyOf in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 YAML snippet demonstrates how to use `oneOf` within a request body's schema to allow for alternate data structures. It specifies that the `application/json` request body can conform to one of several predefined schemas (e.g., `Cat`, `Dog`, `Hamster`), providing flexibility for polymorphic data.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
requestBody:
  description: A JSON object containing pet information
  content:
    application/json:
      schema:
        oneOf:
          - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Cat"
          - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Dog"
          - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Hamster"
```

TITLE: Server Templating for Multiple Environments (Prod, Dev, Staging)
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to use an `environment` variable to define different server environments (production, development, staging) with a default production server.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/api-host-and-base-path.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
servers:
  - url: https://{environment}.example.com/v2
    variables:
      environment:
        default: api    # Production server
        enum:
          - api         # Production server
          - api.dev     # Development server
          - api.staging # Staging server
```

TITLE: Distinguishing oneOf from anyOf in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates the critical difference between `oneOf` and `anyOf`. While `anyOf` allows matching one or more subschemas, `oneOf` strictly requires matching *exactly one*. The example shows a body that is invalid for `oneOf` because it matches multiple schemas.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/oneof-anyof-allof-not.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: JSON
CODE:
```
{ "nickname": "Fido", "pet_type": "Dog", "age": 4 }
```

TITLE: Define OpenAPI Info Object for API Metadata
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to define the `info` object in an OpenAPI 3.0 specification. It includes essential API metadata such as the application title, API version, description, terms of service, contact information, and license details. The `title` and `version` fields are mandatory, while others like `description`, `termsOfService`, `contact`, and `license` are optional but recommended for comprehensive API documentation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/api-general-info.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
info:
  # You application title. Required.
  title: Sample Pet Store App

  # API version. You can use semantic versioning like 1.0.0,
  # or an arbitrary string like 0.99-beta. Required.
  version: 1.0.0

  # API description. Arbitrary text in CommonMark or HTML.
  description: This is a sample server for a pet store.

  # Link to the page that describes the terms of service.
  # Must be in the URL format.
  termsOfService: http://example.com/terms/

  # Contact information: name, email, URL.
  contact:
    name: API Support
    email: support@example.com
    url: http://example.com/support

  # Name of the license and a URL to the license description.
  license:
    name: Apache 2.0
    url: http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0.html

# Link to the external documentation (if any).
# Code or documentation generation tools can use description as the text of the link.
externalDocs:
  description: Find out more
  url: http://example.com
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define Various Security Schemes in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to define various security schemes within the `components/securitySchemes` section of an OpenAPI 3.0 specification. It includes examples for HTTP Basic, HTTP Bearer, API Key, OpenID Connect, and OAuth 2 with scopes, illustrating the `type`, `scheme`, `in`, `name`, `openIdConnectUrl`, and `flows` properties for each.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    BasicAuth:
      type: http
      scheme: basic

    BearerAuth:
      type: http
      scheme: bearer

    ApiKeyAuth:
      type: apiKey
      in: header
      name: X-API-Key

    OpenID:
      type: openIdConnect
      openIdConnectUrl: https://example.com/.well-known/openid-configuration

    OAuth2:
      type: oauth2
      flows:
        authorizationCode:
          authorizationUrl: https://example.com/oauth/authorize
          tokenUrl: https://example.com/oauth/token
          scopes:
            read: Grants read access
            write: Grants write access
            admin: Grants access to admin operations
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Media Type Concepts and Structure
DESCRIPTION: Explains the concept of media types in OpenAPI 3.0, their role in defining request/response body data, and how they are specified using the `content` keyword within response definitions. It also references RFC 6838 for media type naming conventions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Media Type Definition in OpenAPI 3.0:
  - Concept: Format of request or response body data (e.g., JSON, XML, images).
  - Location: Specified within request and response definitions.
  - Structure (within a response):
    responses:
      "{HTTP_CODE}":
        description: "..."
        content:
          "{media_type_name}":
            schema: # Required
              type: "..."
              properties: # For object types
                ...
            example: # Optional
              ...
  - Keywords:
    - content: Defines the response body, containing one or more media types.
    - schema: Defines the data type of the message body for a specific media type.
    - example: Provides sample data for the media type.
  - Media Type Naming:
    - Compliance: RFC 6838
    - Examples:
      - Standard: application/json, application/xml, text/plain, image/png
      - Vendor-specific: application/vnd.mycompany.myapp.v2+json, image/vnd.djvu
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: $ref Syntax Examples for Various Reference Types
DESCRIPTION: Provides a comprehensive list of $ref syntax examples, illustrating how to construct references for local, remote, and URL-based definitions in OpenAPI specifications.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/using-ref.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
$ref: '#/definitions/myElement'
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
$ref: 'document.json'
```

CODE:
```
$ref: 'document.json#/myElement'
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
$ref: '../document.json#/myElement'
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
$ref: '../another-folder/document.json#/myElement'
```

CODE:
```

```

CODE:

```

```

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 OAuth 2.0 Flows Object Properties
DESCRIPTION: Details the properties available for each OAuth 2.0 flow type (`authorizationCode`, `implicit`, `password`, `clientCredentials`) within an OpenAPI 3.0 security scheme definition, including `authorizationUrl`, `tokenUrl`, `refreshUrl`, and `scopes`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Flows Object Properties:
  authorizationUrl:
    Description: The authorization URL to use for this flow. Can be relative to the API server URL.
    Applies to: authorizationCode, implicit
  tokenUrl:
    Description: The token URL to use for this flow. Can be relative to the API server URL.
    Applies to: authorizationCode, password, clientCredentials
  refreshUrl:
    Description: Optional. The URL to be used for obtaining refresh tokens. Can be relative to the API server URL.
    Applies to: authorizationCode, implicit, password, clientCredentials
  scopes:
    Description: The available scopes for the OAuth2 security scheme. A map between the scope name and a short description for it.
    Applies to: authorizationCode, implicit, password, clientCredentials
```

TITLE: Add Discriminator for Object Type Detection in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows how to use the `discriminator` keyword with `oneOf` or `anyOf` to help API consumers identify the specific object type in a polymorphic response. The `propertyName` points to a field (e.g., `objectType`) within the schema that contains the actual type name, aiding in code generation and data validation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/inheritance-and-polymorphism.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  responses:
    sampleObjectResponse:
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            oneOf:
              - $ref: '#/components/schemas/simpleObject'
              - $ref: '#/components/schemas/complexObject'
            discriminator:
              propertyName: objectType
  …
  schemas:
    simpleObject:
      type: object
      required:
        - objectType
      properties:
        objectType:
          type: string
      …
    complexObject:
      type: object
      required:
        - objectType
      properties:
        objectType:
          type: string
      …
```

TITLE: Defining HTTP and HTTPS Servers Using Protocol Templating
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to use a `protocol` variable to define both HTTP and HTTPS servers within a single `servers` entry, with HTTPS set as the default.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/api-host-and-base-path.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
servers:
  - url: '{protocol}://api.example.com'
    variables:
      protocol:
        enum:
          - http
          - https
        default: https
```

TITLE: Define Multiple Request Body Examples in OpenAPI (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates the use of the `examples` (plural) property to define multiple request body examples. It shows inline examples (`value`), external examples (`externalValue`), and referenced examples (`$ref`) from `components.examples`. Each example can include optional `summary` and `description` for documentation purposes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
requestBody:
  content:
    application/json:
      schema:
        $ref: '#/components/schemas/Pet'
      examples:

        dog:  # <--- example name
          summary: An example of a dog
          value:
            # vv Actual payload goes here vv
            name: Fluffy
            petType: dog

        cat:  # <--- example name
          summary: An example of a cat
          externalValue: http://api.example.com/examples/cat.json   # cat.json contains {"name": "Tiger", "petType": "cat"}

        hamster:  # <--- example name
          $ref: '#/components/examples/hamster'

  components:
    examples:
      hamster:  # <--- example name
        summary: An example of a hamster
        value:
          # vv Actual payload goes here vv
          name: Ginger
          petType: hamster
```

TITLE: OpenAPI allOf Keyword for Schema Extension and Polymorphism
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how `allOf` combines a base `Pet` schema with type-specific properties for `Dog` and `Cat`. It uses `oneOf` and `discriminator` to enable polymorphic request body validation, ensuring the data conforms to all combined subschemas.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/oneof-anyof-allof-not.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /pets:
    patch:
      requestBody:
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              oneOf:
                - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Cat"
                - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Dog"
              discriminator:
                propertyName: pet_type
      responses:
        "200":
          description: Updated

components:
  schemas:
    Pet:
      type: object
      required:
        - pet_type
      properties:
        pet_type:
          type: string
      discriminator:
        propertyName: pet_type

    Dog: # "Dog" is a value for the pet_type property (the discriminator value)
      allOf: # Combines the main `Pet` schema with `Dog`-specific properties
        - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Pet"
        - type: object
          # all other properties specific to a `Dog`
          properties:
            bark:
              type: boolean
            breed:
              type: string
              enum: [Dingo, Husky, Retriever, Shepherd]

    Cat: # "Cat" is a value for the pet_type property (the discriminator value)
      allOf: # Combines the main `Pet` schema with `Cat`-specific properties
        - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Pet"
        - type: object
          # all other properties specific to a `Cat`
          properties:
            hunts:
              type: boolean
            age:
              type: integer
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI 2.0 to 3.0 Security Changes Summary
DESCRIPTION: This section summarizes key changes in security definition between OpenAPI 2.0 and 3.0. It covers renaming of `securityDefinitions` to `securitySchemes`, changes in `type: basic` to `type: http` with `scheme: basic`, introduction of `type: http` as an umbrella, support for API keys `in: cookie`, addition of `type: openIdConnect`, and updates to OAuth 2 flows and their naming conventions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
OpenAPI 2.0 to 3.0 Security Changes:
- `securityDefinitions` renamed to `securitySchemes` and moved to `components`.
- `type: basic` replaced with `type: http` and `scheme: basic`.
- New `type: http` is an umbrella type for all HTTP security schemes.
- API keys can now be sent `in: cookie`.
- Added support for OpenID Connect Discovery (`type: openIdConnect`).
- OAuth 2 security schemes can define multiple `flows`.
- OAuth 2 flows renamed: `accessCode` to `authorizationCode`, `application` to `clientCredentials`.
```

```

    -o /local/out/go
```

TITLE: Complete OpenAPI Example with Linked Operations for User Management
DESCRIPTION: This comprehensive OpenAPI 3.0 example demonstrates how to link a `createUser` POST operation to a `getUser` GET operation. It shows how the `id` returned from the `createUser` response body is automatically passed as the `userId` path parameter to the `getUser` operation using a runtime expression (`$response.body#/id`), illustrating a common workflow for API discoverability.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
info:
  version: 0.0.0
  title: Links example

paths:
  /users:
    post:
      summary: Creates a user and returns the user ID
      operationId: createUser
      requestBody:
        required: true
        description: A JSON object that contains the user name and age.
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"
      responses:
        "201":
          description: Created
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                type: object
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                    format: int64
                    description: ID of the created user.
          # -----------------------------------------------------
          # Links
          # -----------------------------------------------------
          links:
            GetUserByUserId: # <---- arbitrary name for the link
              operationId: getUser
              # or
              # operationRef: '#/paths/~1users~1{userId}/get'
              parameters:
                userId: "$response.body#/id"

              description: >
                The `id` value returned in the response can be used as
                the `userId` parameter in `GET /users/{userId}`.
          # -----------------------------------------------------

  /users/{userId}:
    get:
      summary: Gets a user by ID
      operationId: getUser
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: userId
          required: true
          schema:
            type: integer
            format: int64
      responses:
        "200":
          description: A User object
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"

components:
  schemas:
    User:
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
          format: int64
          readOnly: true
        name:
          type: string
```

TITLE: OpenAPI 2.0 Paths and Operations API Reference
DESCRIPTION: This reference outlines the core structure for defining API paths and operations within OpenAPI Specification v2.0. It details the `paths` object, its nested HTTP method operations, and key properties such as `summary`, `description`, `operationId`, `parameters`, `responses`, and `externalDocs`, along with the `definitions` section for reusable schemas.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
OpenAPI 2.0 Specification:
  paths:
    description: Defines API endpoints (resources) and their operations.
    type: object
    properties:
      /{path_template}:
        description: An API endpoint, potentially with path parameters (e.g., /users/{id}).
        type: object
        properties:
          get | post | put | patch | delete | head | options:
            description: An HTTP method (operation) for the path.
            type: object
            properties:
              summary: string (short summary)
              description: string (detailed description, supports GFM)
              operationId: string (unique ID for code generation)
              tags: array<string> (for grouping in UI)
              produces: array<string> (MIME types produced)
              parameters:
                type: array<object>
                description: List of parameters for the operation.
                items:
                  name: string
                  in: string (path, query, header, formData, body)
                  description: string
                  type: string (e.g., integer, string)
                  required: boolean
              responses:
                type: object
                description: Map of HTTP status codes to responses.
                properties:
                  {status_code}:
                    description: string
                    schema: object (reference to #/definitions/User or inline schema)
              externalDocs:
                type: object
                properties:
                  url: string
                  description: string
  definitions:
    description: Reusable data type definitions.
    type: object
    properties:
      {definition_name}:
        type: object
        properties:
          type: string
          properties: object (key-value pairs of property name to schema)
          required: array<string>
```

TITLE: Example: Pagination with Cursors Using OpenAPI Links
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how a cursor value returned in a paginated API response (e.g., from GET /items?limit=100) can be used as a parameter for a subsequent request (GET /items?cursor=Q1MjAwNz&limit=100) to retrieve the next set of data, demonstrating link usage for pagination.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
GET /items?limit=100

  ⇩

{
  "metadata": {
    "previous": null,
    "next": "Q1MjAwNz",
    "count": 10
  },
  ...
}

  ⇩

GET /items?cursor=Q1MjAwNz&limit=100
```

TITLE: Defining Global Bearer Authentication in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 YAML snippet demonstrates how to define a Bearer authentication security scheme (`type: http`, `scheme: bearer`) under `components/securitySchemes` and then apply it globally to all API operations using the `security` keyword. The `bearerFormat` is optional and provides documentation hints.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/bearer-authentication.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
---
# 1) Define the security scheme type (HTTP bearer)
components:
  securitySchemes:
    bearerAuth: # arbitrary name for the security scheme
      type: http
      scheme: bearer
      bearerFormat: JWT # optional, arbitrary value for documentation purposes

# 2) Apply the security globally to all operations
security:
  - bearerAuth: [] # use the same name as above
```

TITLE: Reference Nested Objects with $ref in OpenAPI YAML
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows how to define nested objects using `$ref` to reference separate schemas, promoting reusability and modularity in OpenAPI definitions. The `User` schema references a `ContactInfo` schema, making the API definition cleaner and more maintainable by avoiding deep nesting.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_22

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    User:
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
        name:
          type: string
        contact_info:
          $ref: "#/components/schemas/ContactInfo"

    ContactInfo:
      type: object
      properties:
        email:
          type: string
          format: email
        phone:
          type: string
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Mixed-Type Arrays with `oneOf`
DESCRIPTION: Explains how to define arrays containing items of different types in OpenAPI using the `oneOf` keyword within the `items` schema. It demonstrates using `oneOf` with inline subschemas and with schema references, and also shows how to define an array of arbitrary types.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_15

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
# ["foo", 5, -2, "bar"]
type: array
items:
  oneOf:
    - type: string
    - type: integer
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
# Array of Cats and Dogs
type: array
items:
  oneOf:
    - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Cat"
    - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Dog"
```

type: array
items: {}
```

CODE:
```
# Incorrect
items:
  - type: string
  - type: integer

# Incorrect as well
items:
  type:
    - string
    - integer
```

TITLE: Swagger Codegen Version Compatibility with OpenAPI Specification
DESCRIPTION: This table details the compatibility of various Swagger Codegen versions with different versions of the OpenAPI Specification (formerly Swagger Specification), including release dates and notes for each version.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/compatibility.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC

TITLE: Define File Upload with Additional Data via Multipart Form in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to define a file upload alongside other form data using the `multipart/form-data` media type in OpenAPI 3.0. The schema defines an object with properties for `orderId`, `userId`, and the `fileName` (a binary string). The HTTP request example shows how these parts are structured in a multipart payload.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/file-upload.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
requestBody:
  content:
    multipart/form-data:
      schema:
        type: object
        properties:
          orderId:
            type: integer
          userId:
            type: integer
          fileName:
            type: string
            format: binary
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
POST /upload
Host: example.com
Content-Length: 2740
Content-Type: multipart/form-data; boundary=abcde12345

--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="orderId"

1195
--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="userId"

545
--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="fileName"; filename="attachment.txt"
Content-Type: text/plain

[file content goes there]
--abcde12345--
```

TITLE: Referencing a Schema in an API Response
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to use the $ref keyword to reference a previously defined 'User' schema within a 200 OK API response, demonstrating reusability in both JSON and YAML.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/using-ref.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: JSON
CODE:
```
"responses":
  {
    "200":
      {
        "description": "The response",
        "schema": { "$ref": "#/components/schemas/user" },
      },
  }
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
responses:
  "200":
    description: The response
    schema:
      $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"
```

TITLE: Configure OpenAPI OAuth 2.0 with Multiple Flows
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to define an OAuth 2.0 security scheme that supports multiple authorization flows (e.g., Implicit and Password) within a single OpenAPI `securitySchemes` component, allowing clients to choose any supported flow.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    oAuth2:
      type: oauth2
      description: For more information, see https://developers.getbase.com/docs/rest/articles/oauth2/requests
      flows:
        implicit:
          authorizationUrl: https://api.getbase.com/oauth2/authorize
          scopes:
            read: Grant read-only access to all your data except for the account and user info
            write: Grant write-only access to all your data except for the account and user info
            profile: Grant read-only access to the account and user info only
        password:
          tokenUrl: https://api.getbase.com/oauth2/token
          scopes:
            read: Grant read-only access to all your data except for the account and user info
            write: Grant write-only access to all your data except for the account and user info
            profile: Grant read-only access to the account and user info only
```

TITLE: Define Enum for Query Parameter in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to define an `enum` for a query parameter named `sort` within an OpenAPI 3.0 path definition. It restricts the `sort` parameter's values to either `asc` or `desc`, ensuring valid input for sorting operations.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/enums.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /items:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: sort
          description: Sort order
          schema:
            type: string
            enum: [asc, desc]
```

TITLE: Defining and Applying API Keys Globally in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define an API key security scheme (`ApiKeyAuth`) in the `components/securitySchemes` section and then apply it globally to all API operations using the `security` section in OpenAPI 3.0. It specifies the key type, location (header, query, or cookie), and the actual name of the key.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/api-keys.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
---
# 1) Define the key name and location
components:
  securitySchemes:
    ApiKeyAuth: # arbitrary name for the security scheme
      type: apiKey
      in: header # can be "header", "query" or "cookie"
      name: X-API-KEY # name of the header, query parameter or cookie

# 2) Apply the API key globally to all operations
security:
  - ApiKeyAuth: [] # use the same name as under securitySchemes
```

TITLE: Implement Polymorphic Responses with oneOf or anyOf in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to define polymorphic responses in OpenAPI 3.0 using the `oneOf` keyword. It allows an API response payload to conform to one of several alternative schemas, such as `simpleObject` or `complexObject`, providing flexibility in data representation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/inheritance-and-polymorphism.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  responses:
    sampleObjectResponse:
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            oneOf:
              - $ref: '#/components/schemas/simpleObject'
              - $ref: '#/components/schemas/complexObject'
  …
components:
  schemas:
    simpleObject:
      …
    complexObject:
      …
```

servers:
  - url: http://api.example.com/v1

  - url: http://staging-api.example.com
    description: Optional server description, e.g. Internal staging server for testing
```

TITLE: Define Schema Composition using allOf in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to use the `allOf` keyword in OpenAPI 3.0 to compose schemas. It shows how `ExtendedErrorModel` inherits properties from `BasicErrorModel` and adds its own, illustrating how to reuse common property sets across different models.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/inheritance-and-polymorphism.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    BasicErrorModel:
      type: object
      required:
        - message
        - code
      properties:
        message:
          type: string
        code:
          type: integer
          minimum: 100
          maximum: 600
    ExtendedErrorModel:
      allOf: # Combines the BasicErrorModel and the inline model
        - $ref: "#/components/schemas/BasicErrorModel"
        - type: object
          required:
            - rootCause
          properties:
            rootCause:
              type: string
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define and Reuse Global Parameters with $ref in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to define common parameters (like pagination parameters 'offset' and 'limit') in a global 'parameters' section. These definitions can then be easily reused across different paths and operations using the '$ref' keyword, promoting consistency and reducing redundancy.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_23

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
parameters:
  offsetParam: # <-- Arbitrary name for the definition that will be used to refer to it.
    # Not necessarily the same as the parameter name.
    in: query
    name: offset
    required: false
    type: integer
    minimum: 0
    description: The number of items to skip before starting to collect the result set.
  limitParam:
    in: query
    name: limit
    required: false
    type: integer
    minimum: 1
    maximum: 50
    default: 20
    description: The numbers of items to return.
paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Gets a list of users.
      parameters:
        - $ref: "#/parameters/offsetParam"
        - $ref: "#/parameters/limitParam"
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
  /teams:
    get:
      summary: Gets a list of teams.
      parameters:
        - $ref: "#/parameters/offsetParam"
        - $ref: "#/parameters/limitParam"
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Load SwaggerUI and Editor via Unpkg in HTML for Multi-Spec Support
DESCRIPTION: This HTML example illustrates how to integrate SwaggerUI and SwaggerEditor directly from unpkg.com without a build process. It includes the necessary CSS and JavaScript bundles, initializes SwaggerUI with a default API definition, and incorporates various editor plugins for multi-spec support.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_26

LANGUAGE: html
CODE:
```
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html >
  <head>
    <meta charset="utf-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1" />
    <meta name="theme-color" content="#000000" />
    <meta name="description" content="SwaggerUIMultifold" />
    <link rel="stylesheet" href="//unpkg.com/swagger-editor@5.0.0-alpha.86/dist/swagger-editor.css" />
  </head>
  <body style="margin:0; padding:0;">
    <section id="swagger-ui"></section>

    <script src="//unpkg.com/swagger-ui-dist@5.11.0/swagger-ui-bundle.js"></script>
    <script src="//unpkg.com/swagger-ui-dist@5.11.0/swagger-ui-standalone-preset.js"></script>
    <script>
      ui = SwaggerUIBundle({});
      // expose SwaggerUI React globally for SwaggerEditor to use
      window.React = ui.React;
    </script>
    <script src="//unpkg.com/swagger-editor@5.0.0-alpha.86/dist/umd/swagger-editor.js"></script>
    <script>
      SwaggerUIBundle({
        url: 'https://petstore3.swagger.io/api/v3/openapi.json',
        dom_id: '#swagger-ui',
        presets: [
          SwaggerUIBundle.presets.apis,
          SwaggerUIStandalonePreset,
        ],
        plugins: [
          SwaggerEditor.plugins.EditorContentType,
          SwaggerEditor.plugins.EditorPreviewAsyncAPI,
          SwaggerEditor.plugins.EditorPreviewApiDesignSystems,
          SwaggerEditor.plugins.SwaggerUIAdapter,
          SwaggerUIBundle.plugins.DownloadUrl,
        ],
        layout: 'StandaloneLayout',
      });
    </script>
  </body>
</html>
```

TITLE: Specify Required Object Properties in OpenAPI YAML
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to mark properties as required within an OpenAPI object schema using the `required` keyword. It's crucial to note that `required` is an object-level attribute, not a property-level one, ensuring proper validation for the entire object.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_19

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
type: object
properties:
  id:
    type: integer
  username:
    type: string
  name:
    type: string
required:
  - id
  - username
```

TITLE: Define Request Body with Multiple Media Types in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 YAML snippet demonstrates how to define a request body for a POST operation on `/pets`. It specifies different schemas for various media types such as `application/json`, `application/xml`, `application/x-www-form-urlencoded`, and `text/plain`, and marks the request body as required.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /pets:
    post:
      summary: Add a new pet

      requestBody:
        description: Optional description in *Markdown*
        required: true
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/Pet"
          application/xml:
            schema:
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/Pet"
          application/x-www-form-urlencoded:
            schema:
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/PetForm"
          text/plain:
            schema:
              type: string

      responses:
        "201":
          description: Created
```

TITLE: Define Single Media Type with Example in OpenAPI Response
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates the basic structure for defining a single media type for an API response in OpenAPI, including its schema and an optional example. It illustrates how the `content` keyword specifies the media type, and `schema` defines the data structure, with `example` providing sample data.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /employees:
    get:
      summary: Returns a list of employees.
      responses:
        "200": # Response
          description: OK
          content: # Response body
            application/json: # Media type
              schema: # Must-have
                type: object # Data type
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                  name:
                    type: string
                  fullTime:
                    type: boolean
                example: # Sample data
                  id: 1
                  name: Jessica Right
                  fullTime: true
```

TITLE: Overriding Server URLs in OpenAPI Definitions
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to override the global `servers` array at different levels within an OpenAPI definition. You can specify a different base URL for an entire path (e.g., `/files`) or for a specific operation (e.g., `GET /ping`), which is useful for specialized endpoints or deprecated APIs.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/api-host-and-base-path.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
servers:
  - url: https://api.example.com/v1

paths:
  /files:
    description: File upload and download operations
    servers:
      - url: https://files.example.com
        description: Override base path for all operations with the /files path
    ...

/ping:
    get:
      servers:
        - url: https://echo.example.com
          description: Override base path for the GET /ping operation
```

TITLE: Referencing Shared Schemas for Multiple Media Types in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to reuse a single schema definition across multiple media types within an OpenAPI response. This is achieved by defining the schema in the 'components' section and referencing it using '$ref', promoting reusability and consistency.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /employees:
    get:
      responses:
        "200": # Response
          description: OK
          content: # Response body
            application/json: # Media type
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/Employee" # Reference to object definition
            application/xml: # Media type
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/Employee" # Reference to object definition
components:
  schemas:
    Employee: # Object definition
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
        name:
          type: string
        fullTime:
          type: boolean
```

TITLE: Applying Bearer Authentication to Specific Operations

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /something:
    get:
      security:
        - bearerAuth: []
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Request Body Example (Schema Child)
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to add a single example for a request body when the `example` keyword is a child of the `schema` definition. This is typical when the schema is defined inline. The example demonstrates a `POST /users` endpoint with an `id` and `name` example for the user object.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    post:
      summary: Adds a new user
      requestBody:
        content:
          application/json:
            schema: # Request body contents
              type: object
              properties:
                id:
                  type: integer
                name:
                  type: string
              example: # Sample object
                id: 10
                name: Jessica Smith
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Example: Creating a User and Using the Returned ID in OpenAPI Links
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how the ID returned from a POST /users operation can be used as input for subsequent GET, PATCH, or DELETE operations on the same user, illustrating the concept of OpenAPI links.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
POST /users HTTP/1.1
Host: example.com
Content-Type: application/json

{
  "name": "Alex",
  "age": 27
}

which returns the ID of the created user:

HTTP/1.1 201 Created
Content-Type: application/json

{
  "id": 305
}
```

TITLE: Correct: Defining Query Parameters in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates the correct method for defining query parameters in OpenAPI using the 'parameters' section with 'in: query', ensuring proper validation, documentation, and adherence to the specification.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: role
          schema:
            type: string
            enum: [user, poweruser, admin]
          required: true
```

TITLE: Initialize Swagger UI with Swagger Editor Plugins
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript code snippet demonstrates how to import and initialize Swagger UI along with a comprehensive set of plugins from the 'swagger-editor' library. It configures Swagger UI to load an OpenAPI definition from a specified URL, render it within a designated DOM element, and integrate various editor functionalities such as modals, dialogs, dropdowns, versioning, different editor types (Monaco, textarea), content handling, and preview options. The setup uses a 'StandaloneLayout' for the UI.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_29

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
import SwaggerUI from 'swagger-ui';

import DialogsPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/dialogs';

import EditorMonacoPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-monaco';
import EditorMonacoLanguageApiDOMPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-monaco-language-apidom';
import EditorContentReadOnlyPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-content-read-only';
import EditorContentOriginPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-content-origin';
import EditorContentTypePlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-content-type';
import EditorContentPersistencePlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-content-persistence';
import EditorContentFixturesPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-content-fixtures';
import EditorPreviewPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview';
import EditorPreviewSwaggerUIPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-swagger-ui';
import EditorPreviewAsyncAPIPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-asyncapi';
import EditorPreviewApiDesignSystemsPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-api-design-systems';
import TopBarPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/top-bar';
import SplashScreenPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/splash-screen';
import LayoutPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/layout';
import EditorSafeRenderPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-safe-render';

SwaggerUI({
  url: 'https://petstore.swagger.io/v2/swagger.json',
  dom_id: '#swagger-editor',
  plugins: [
    ModalsPlugin,
    DialogsPlugin,
    DropdownMenuPlugin,
    DropzonePlugin,
    VersionsPlugin,
    EditorTextareaPlugin,
    EditorMonacoPlugin,
    EditorMonacoLanguageApiDOMPlugin,
    EditorContentReadOnlyPlugin,
    EditorContentOriginPlugin,
    EditorContentTypePlugin,
    EditorContentPersistencePlugin,
    EditorContentFixturesPlugin,
    EditorPreviewPlugin,
    EditorPreviewSwaggerUIPlugin,
    EditorPreviewAsyncAPIPlugin,
    EditorPreviewApiDesignSystemsPlugin,
    TopBarPlugin,
    SplashScreenPlugin,
    LayoutPlugin,
    EditorSafeRenderPlugin
  ],
  layout: 'StandaloneLayout'

TITLE: Define a String-to-Object Dictionary Schema in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 schema illustrates how to define a dictionary where keys are strings and values are complex objects. The `additionalProperties` keyword specifies an inline object schema with `code` (integer) and `text` (string) properties.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/dictionaries.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
type: object
additionalProperties:
  type: object
  properties:
    code:
      type: integer
    text:
      type: string
```

TITLE: Example of Invalid JSON for `oneOf` Schema (Multiple Matches)
DESCRIPTION: This JSON object is invalid for the `oneOf` schema because it is valid against *both* the `Cat` and `Dog` schemas. The `oneOf` keyword strictly requires validity against exactly one subschema, making this object incorrect despite conforming to individual schemas.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/oneof-anyof-allof-not.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
{ "bark": true, "hunts": true, "breed": "Husky", "age": 3 }
```

TITLE: Define Required Path Parameter in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI YAML snippet shows how to define a path parameter, 'userId', as required by explicitly setting 'required: true'. Path parameters are inherently required in OpenAPI, and this definition documents that constraint along with a descriptive explanation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: path
    name: userId
    schema:
      type: integer
    required: true # <----------
    description: Numeric ID of the user to get.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define Read-Only and Write-Only Object Properties in OpenAPI YAML
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows how to use `readOnly` and `writeOnly` keywords for object properties in OpenAPI. `readOnly` properties are included in responses but not requests, while `writeOnly` properties are sent in requests but not responses, useful for distinguishing GET and POST/PUT/PATCH data.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_20

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
type: object
properties:
  id:
    # Returned by GET, not used in POST/PUT/PATCH
    type: integer
    readOnly: true
  username:
    type: string
  password:
    # Used in POST/PUT/PATCH, not returned by GET
    type: string
    writeOnly: true
```

```

TITLE: Defining a Basic Path Parameter in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to define a basic path parameter (`userId`) for a GET operation in OpenAPI 3.0. It specifies the parameter's location (`in: path`), name, data type (`schema: type: integer`), and marks it as required with a description.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{userId}:
    get:
      summary: Get a user by ID
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: userId
          schema:
            type: integer
          required: true
          description: Numeric ID of the user to get
```

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Security Schemes Overview
DESCRIPTION: This section provides an overview of the security schemes supported by OpenAPI 3.0, including HTTP authentication (Basic, Bearer, other RFC 7235 schemes), API keys (in headers, query, cookies), OAuth 2, and OpenID Connect Discovery. It explains the concept of 'security scheme' and lists the available types.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
OpenAPI 3.0 Security Schemes:
- HTTP authentication schemes (use Authorization header):
    - Basic
    - Bearer
    - Other HTTP schemes (RFC 7235, HTTP Authentication Scheme Registry)
- API keys:
    - In headers, query string, or cookies
    - Cookie authentication
- OAuth 2
- OpenID Connect Discovery
```

TITLE: Integrate SwaggerEditor into a React Application
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript snippet demonstrates how to embed SwaggerEditor into a React component. It initializes the editor with a remote YAML specification and configures `MonacoEnvironment` to correctly locate worker files relative to the application's base URL, ensuring proper functionality.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
import React from 'react';
import ReactDOM from 'react-dom';
import SwaggerEditor from 'swagger-editor';
import 'swagger-editor/swagger-editor.css';

const url = "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/asyncapi/spec/v2.2.0/examples/streetlights-kafka.yml";

const MyApp = () => (
  <div>
    <h1>SwaggerEditor Integration</h1>
    <SwaggerEditor url={url} />
  </div>
);

self.MonacoEnvironment = {
  /**
   * We're building into the dist/ folder. When application starts on
   * URL=https://example.com then SwaggerEditor will look for
   * `apidom.worker.js` on https://example.com/dist/apidom.worker.js and
   * `editor.worker` on https://example.com/dist/editor.worker.js.
   */
  baseUrl: `${document.baseURI || location.href}dist/`,
}

ReactDOM.render(<MyApp />, document.getElementById('swagger-editor'));
```

TITLE: Define API Paths and Operations
DESCRIPTION: This example shows how to define an API path (`/users`) and an HTTP GET operation within the `paths` section. It includes a summary, an extended description, and a `200` response definition with content type and schema.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/basic-structure.md#_snippet_4

CODE:

paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Returns a list of users.
      description: Optional extended description in CommonMark or HTML
      responses:
        "200":
          description: A JSON array of user names
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                type: array
                items:
                  type: string
```

TITLE: Define Multiple File Uploads via Multipart Form in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates how to define the upload of an arbitrary number of files using the `multipart/form-data` media type in OpenAPI 3.0. The `filename` property is defined as an array of binary strings. The corresponding HTTP request shows how multiple files are included as separate parts within the multipart payload.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/file-upload.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
requestBody:
  content:
    multipart/form-data:
      schema:
        type: object
        properties:
          filename:
            type: array
            items:
              type: string
              format: binary
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
POST /upload
Host: example.com
Content-Length: 2740
Content-Type: multipart/form-data; boundary=abcde12345

--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="fileName"; filename="file1.txt"
Content-Type: text/plain

[file content goes there]
--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="fileName"; filename="file2.png"
Content-Type: image/png

[file content goes there]
--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="fileName"; filename="file3.jpg"
Content-Type: image/jpeg

[file content goes there]
--abcde12345--
```

TITLE: Swagger UI Core Configuration Parameters
DESCRIPTION: Details the core configuration parameters for Swagger UI, including their Docker variable equivalents, types, default values, and descriptions. Parameters are grouped by category and sorted alphabetically.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/configuration.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameters:
  configUrl:
    Docker Variable: CONFIG_URL
    Type: String
    Description: URL to fetch external configuration document from.
  dom_id:
    Docker Variable: DOM_ID
    Type: String, REQUIRED if domNode is not provided.
    Description: The ID of a DOM element inside which SwaggerUI will put its user interface.
  domNode:
    Docker Variable: Unavailable
    Type: Element, REQUIRED if dom_id is not provided.
    Description: The HTML DOM element inside which SwaggerUI will put its user interface. Overrides dom_id.
  spec:
    Docker Variable: SPEC
    Type: Object={}
    Description: A JavaScript object describing the OpenAPI definition. When used, the url parameter will not be parsed. This is useful for testing manually-generated definitions without hosting them.
  url:
    Docker Variable: URL
    Type: String
    Description: The URL pointing to API definition (normally swagger.json or swagger.yaml). Will be ignored if urls or spec is used.
  urls:
    Docker Variable: URLS
    Type: Array
    Description: An array of API definition objects ([{url: "<url1>", name: "<name1>"},{url: "<url2>", name: "<name2>"}]) used by Topbar plugin. When used and Topbar plugin is enabled, the url parameter will not be parsed. Names and URLs must be unique among all items in this array, since they're used as identifiers.
  urls.primaryName:
    Docker Variable: URLS_PRIMARY_NAME
    Type: String
    Description: When using urls, you can use this subparameter. If the value matches the name of a spec provided in urls, that spec will be displayed when Swagger UI loads, instead of defaulting to the first spec in urls.
  queryConfigEnabled:
    Docker Variable: QUERY_CONFIG_ENABLED
    Type: Boolean=false
    Description: Enables overriding configuration parameters via URL search params.
```

TITLE: Defining a Reusable 401 Unauthorized Response for API Keys in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to define a reusable 401 'Unauthorized' response in the `components/responses` section and reference it from operation-level responses in OpenAPI 3.0. This response includes a description and an optional `WWW-Authenticate` header.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/api-keys.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /something:
    get:
      ...
      responses:
        ...
        '401':
            $ref: "#/components/responses/UnauthorizedError"
    post:
      ...
      responses:
        ...
        '401':
          $ref: "#/components/responses/UnauthorizedError"

components:
  responses:
    UnauthorizedError:
      description: API key is missing or invalid
      headers:
        WWW_Authenticate:
          schema:
            type: string
```

TITLE: Defining and Referencing a Reusable 401 Unauthorized Response
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 YAML example shows how to define a common 401 'Unauthorized' error response under `components/responses` for reusability. It then demonstrates how to reference this shared response from multiple API operations (e.g., GET and POST for `/something`) using the `$ref` keyword, ensuring consistent error handling documentation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/bearer-authentication.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /something:
    get:
      ...
      responses:
        '401':
          $ref: '#/components/responses/UnauthorizedError'
        ...
    post:
      ...
      responses:
        '401':
          $ref: '#/components/responses/UnauthorizedError'
        ...

components:
  responses:
    UnauthorizedError:
      description: Access token is missing or invalid
```

TITLE: Reuse Request Body Definitions in OpenAPI (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define reusable request bodies in the global `components.requestBodies` section and reference them using `$ref` in multiple API operations (e.g., `post` and `put`). This promotes reusability and consistency across the API specification.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /pets:
    post:
      summary: Add a new pet
      requestBody:
        $ref: '#/components/requestBodies/PetBody'

  /pets/{petId}
    put:
      summary: Update a pet
      parameters: [ ... ]
      requestBody:
        $ref: '#/components/requestBodies/PetBody'

components:
  requestBodies:
    PetBody:
      description: A JSON object containing pet information
      required: true
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            $ref: '#/components/schemas/Pet'
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Schema for Multipart Request Body
DESCRIPTION: Defines the structure of a multipart request body in OpenAPI 3.0 using `multipart/form-data`. It specifies individual request parts as properties within the schema, demonstrating how to include string values, JSON objects, and binary data (like images).
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/multipart-requests.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
requestBody:
  content:
    multipart/form-data: # Media type
      schema: # Request payload
        type: object
        properties: # Request parts
          id: # Part 1 (string value)
            type: string
            format: uuid
          address: # Part2 (object)
            type: object
            properties:
              street:
                type: string
              city:
                type: string
          profileImage: # Part 3 (an image)
            type: string
            format: binary
```

TITLE: Restrict Parameter Values with Enum in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to restrict a parameter to a fixed set of values by adding the `enum` keyword to the parameter’s `schema`. The enum values must be of the same type as the parameter data type. The example defines a `status` query parameter that can only be 'available', 'pending', or 'sold'.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_17

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: status
    schema:
      type: string
      enum:
        - available
        - pending
        - sold
```

TITLE: Defining Global Security Requirements with Scopes in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to define global security requirements in an OpenAPI specification. It shows the application of specific scopes for OAuth2 (`scope1`, `scope2`) and OpenID Connect (`scopeA`, `scopeB`), while indicating that `BasicAuth` does not use scopes with an empty array. This configuration applies to all API calls unless overridden at the operation level.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
security:
  - OAuth2:
      - scope1
      - scope2
  - OpenId:
      - scopeA
      - scopeB
  - BasicAuth: []
```

TITLE: Generate Java API Client using Swagger Codegen Online Service
DESCRIPTION: This `curl` command demonstrates how to send an HTTP POST request to the Swagger Codegen online generator's `/api/generate` endpoint. It specifies an OpenAPI `specURL`, the target language (`java`), and the generation type (`CLIENT`) to produce a Java API client. The service responds with a zipped file containing the generated code.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/online-generators.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
curl -X POST \
  https://generator3.swagger.io/api/generate \
  -H 'content-type: application/json' \
  -d '{
  "specURL" : "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/OAI/OpenAPI-Specification/master/examples/v3.0/petstore.yaml",
  "lang" : "java",
  "type" : "CLIENT",
  "codegenVersion" : "V3"
}'
```

TITLE: Run Swagger Generator Docker Image with Environment Variables and Volumes
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to pull and run the `swaggerapi/swagger-generator-v3` Docker image. ```

docker run -e "HIDDEN_OPTIONS_PATH=/hiddenOptions.yaml" -e "JAVA_MEM=1024m" -e "HTTP_PORT=80" -p 80:80 --name swagger-generator-v3  -v /tmp:/jetty_home/lib/shared swaggerapi/swagger-generator-v3

docker run -e "HIDDEN_OPTIONS_PATH=/hiddenOptions.yaml" -e "JAVA_MEM=1024m" -e "HTTP_PORT=80" -p 80:80 --name swagger-generator-v3 -v /my/custom:/jetty_home/lib/shared swaggerapi/swagger-generator-v3
```

TITLE: Defining a Required Path Parameter with Constraints in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This YAML example details the definition of a required path parameter (`id`) for the `/users/{id}` endpoint in OpenAPI 3.0. It specifies the parameter's location, name, required status, integer type, and a minimum value constraint.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{id}:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: id # Note the name is the same as in the path
          required: true
          schema:
            type: integer
            minimum: 1
          description: The user ID
```
