TITLE: Reusing Common Responses Across API Operations in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to define common API responses (e.g., 'NotFound', 'Unauthorized') in a global 'responses' section and then reference them using '$ref' from individual API operations. This strategy promotes reusability, reduces redundancy, and ensures consistency in response documentation across the API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_11

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Gets a list of users.
      response:
        200:
          description: OK
          schema:
            $ref: "#/definitions/ArrayOfUsers"
        401:
          $ref: "#/responses/Unauthorized"
  /users/{id}:
    get:
      summary: Gets a user by ID.
      response:
        200:
          description: OK
          schema:
            $ref: "#/definitions/User"
        401:
          $ref: "#/responses/Unauthorized"
        404:
          $ref: "#/responses/NotFound"
# Descriptions of common responses
responses:
  NotFound:
    description: The specified resource was not found
    schema:
      $ref: "#/definitions/Error"
  Unauthorized:
    description: Unauthorized
    schema:
      $ref: "#/definitions/Error"
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define OpenAPI Path and Query Parameters with RFC 6570 Styles
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet defines an OpenAPI path `/users{id}` with a path parameter `id` using `matrix` style and `explode: true`, and a query parameter `metadata` using default `form` style. It demonstrates how `style` and `explode` keywords influence URI serialization.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/serialization.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
paths:
  # /users;id=3;id=4?metadata=true
  /users{id}:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: id
          required: true
          schema:
            type: array
            items:
              type: integer
            minItems: 1
          style: matrix
          explode: true
        - in: query
          name: metadata
          schema:
            type: boolean
          # Using the default serialization for query parameters:
          # style=form, explode=false, allowReserved=false
      responses:
        '200':
          description: A list of users
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Configure Global OpenID Connect Security in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define an `openIdConnect` security scheme in `components/securitySchemes` with its discovery URL and then apply it globally to all API operations in the `security` section, specifying required scopes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/openid-connect-discovery.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
---
# 1) Define the security scheme type and attributes
components:
  securitySchemes:
    openId: # <--- Arbitrary name for the security scheme. Used to refer to it from elsewhere.
      type: openIdConnect
      openIdConnectUrl: https://example.com/.well-known/openid-configuration

# 2) Apply security globally to all operations
security:
  - openId: # <--- Use the same name as specified in securitySchemes
      - pets_read
      - pets_write
      - admin
```

TITLE: Requiring Multiple API Keys Simultaneously in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to enforce the simultaneous use of multiple API keys for authentication. By listing `apiKey1` and `apiKey2` within the same security requirement object, both keys must be present in the request.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
security:
  - apiKey1: []
    apiKey2: []
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Parameter Examples (Multiple)
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to provide multiple example values for an OpenAPI parameter using the `examples` keyword. Each example has a distinct key name, a `value`, and an optional `summary`. This example shows a `limit` query parameter with `zero` and `max` examples.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: limit
    schema:
      type: integer
      maximum: 50
    examples: # Multiple examples
      zero: # Distinct name
        value: 0 # Example value
        summary: A sample limit value # Optional description
      max: # Distinct name
        value: 50 # Example value
        summary: A sample limit value # Optional description
```

TITLE: Define Multiple Media Types for API Responses in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to specify different media types (e.g., `application/json`, `application/xml`) for an API response in an OpenAPI specification. It shows how to define separate schemas for each media type under the `content` keyword for a given response code.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /employees:
    get:
      summary: Returns a list of employees.
      responses:
        "200": # Response
          description: OK
          content: # Response body
            application/json: # One of media types
              schema:
                type: object
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                  name:
                    type: string
                  fullTime:
                    type: boolean
            application/xml: # Another media types
              schema:
                type: object
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                  name:
                    type: string
                  fullTime:
                    type: boolean
```

```
parameters:

    name: status
    schema:
      type: string
      enum: [approved, pending, closed, new]
      example: approved # Example of a parameter value
```

TITLE: Configure OAuth 2.0 with initOAuth in JavaScript
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to call the `initOAuth` method on a SwaggerUI instance to configure OAuth 2.0 authorization. This example shows a typical setup with various parameters, including client ID, client secret, application name, scopes, and advanced security options.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/oauth2.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const ui = SwaggerUI({...})

// Method can be called in any place after calling constructor SwaggerUIBundle
ui.initOAuth({
    clientId: "your-client-id",
    clientSecret: "your-client-secret-if-required",
    realm: "your-realms",
    appName: "your-app-name",
    scopeSeparator: " ",
    scopes: "openid profile",
    additionalQueryStringParams: {test: "hello"},
    useBasicAuthenticationWithAccessCodeGrant: true,
    usePkceWithAuthorizationCodeGrant: true
  })
```

TITLE: Defining Multiple API Keys with Logical AND in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define and apply multiple API keys (e.g., `apiKey` and `appId`) that must both be present for authorization (logical AND) by listing them within the same array item under the `security` section in OpenAPI 3.0.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/api-keys.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    apiKey:
      type: apiKey
      in: header
      name: X-API-KEY
    appId:
      type: apiKey
      in: header
      name: X-APP-ID

security:
  - apiKey: []
    appId: [] # <-- no leading dash (-)
```

TITLE: Define Array Query Parameter with Size and Uniqueness Constraints in OpenAPI/Swagger
DESCRIPTION: Defines an array query parameter `color` with `minItems`, `maxItems`, `uniqueItems`, and `enum` constraints for its items. This ensures the array has 1-5 unique string values from a predefined list.

- in: query
  name: color
  required: false
  type: array
  minItems: 1
  maxItems: 5
  uniqueItems: true
  items:
    type: string
    enum:
      [
        black,
        white,
        gray,
        red,
        pink,
        orange,
        yellow,
        green,
        blue,
        purple,
        brown,
      ]
```

TITLE: Server URL Templating with Multiple Variables
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to use variables within a server URL for dynamic values like customer IDs and ports. Variables require a `default` value and can have an `enum` for restricted choices.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/api-host-and-base-path.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
servers:
  - url: https://{customerId}.saas-app.com:{port}/v2
    variables:
      customerId:
        default: demo
        description: Customer ID assigned by the service provider
      port:
        enum:
          - '443'
          - '8443'
        default: '443'
```

TITLE: Configure OpenAPI OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code Flow
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to define the OAuth 2.0 Authorization Code flow within an OpenAPI `securitySchemes` component. This flow uses `authorizationUrl`, `tokenUrl`, and optional `refreshUrl`, as shown with a Slack API example.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    oAuth2AuthCode:
      type: oauth2
      description: For more information, see https://api.slack.com/docs/oauth
      flows:
        authorizationCode:
          authorizationUrl: https://slack.com/oauth/authorize
          tokenUrl: https://slack.com/api/oauth.access
          scopes:
            users:read: Read user information
            users:write: Modify user information
            im:read: Read messages
            im:write: Write messages
            im:history: Access the message archive
            search:read: Search messages, files, and so on
            # etc.
```

XMLHttpRequest cannot load http://sad.server.com/v2/api-docs. No 'Access-Control-Allow-Origin' header is present on the requested resource. Origin 'null' is therefore not allowed access.

TITLE: Define Direct File Upload in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates how to define a direct file upload in an OpenAPI 3.0 specification. The corresponding HTTP request shows a simple POST with the file as the body.

CODE:
```
requestBody:
  content:
    image/png:
      schema:
        type: string
        format: binary
```

CODE:

POST /upload
Host: example.com
Content-Length: 808
Content-Type: image/png

[file content goes there]
```

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Path Parameter Serialization Examples
DESCRIPTION: This table illustrates how path parameters are serialized based on different `style` (simple, label, matrix) and `explode` (true/false) combinations in OpenAPI 3.0, showing the resulting URI for primitive, array, and object values.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/serialization.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Path Parameters Serialization Table:
| style     | explode  | URI template   | Primitive value id = 5 | Array id = [3, 4, 5]   | Object id = {"role": "admin", "firstName": "Alex"} |
| --------- | -------- | -------------- | ---------------------- | ---------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- |
| simple *  | false *  | /users/{id}    | /users/5               | /users/3,4,5           | /users/role,admin,firstName,Alex                   |
| simple    | true     | /users/{id*}   | /users/5               | /users/3,4,5           | /users/role=admin,firstName=Alex                   |
| label     | false    | /users/{.id}   | /users/.5              | /users/.3,4,5          | /users/.role,admin,firstName,Alex                  |
| label     | true     | /users/{.id*}  | /users/.5              | /users/.3.4.5          | /users/.role=admin.firstName=Alex                  |
| matrix    | false    | /users/{;id}   | /users/;id=5           | /users/;id=3,4,5       | /users/;id=role,admin,firstName,Alex               |
| matrix    | true     | /users/{;id*}  | /users/;id=5           | /users/;id=3;id=4;id=5 | /users/;role=admin;firstName=Alex                  |
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: initOAuth Method Properties for OAuth 2.0 Configuration
DESCRIPTION: Details the configurable properties for the `initOAuth` method, which is used to set up OAuth 2.0 authorization in Swagger UI. Each property controls a specific aspect of the OAuth flow, from client identification to security enhancements.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/oauth2.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
initOAuth(config: object)

config properties:
- clientId: string (required)
  Default clientId.
- clientSecret: string (optional)
  Default clientSecret. ⚠️ Never use this parameter in your production environment. It exposes crucial security information. This feature is intended for dev/test environments only. ⚠️
- realm: string (optional)
  realm query parameter (for oauth1) added to `authorizationUrl` and `tokenUrl`.
- appName: string (optional)
  application name, displayed in authorization popup.
- scopeSeparator: string (optional)
  scope separator for passing scopes, encoded before calling, default value is a space (encoded value `%20`).
- scopes: string[] | string (optional)
  string array or scope separator (i.e. space) separated string of initially selected oauth scopes, default is empty array.
- additionalQueryStringParams: object (optional)
  Additional query parameters added to `authorizationUrl` and `tokenUrl`.
- useBasicAuthenticationWithAccessCodeGrant: boolean (default: false)
  Only activated for the `accessCode` flow. During the `authorization_code` request to the `tokenUrl`, pass the Client Password using the HTTP Basic Authentication scheme.
- usePkceWithAuthorizationCodeGrant: boolean (default: false)
  Only applies to `Authorization Code` flows. Proof Key for Code Exchange brings enhanced security for OAuth public clients. Note: This option does not hide the client secret input because neither PKCE nor client secrets are replacements for each other.
```

TITLE: Describing Global Basic Authentication in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define Basic authentication globally in an OpenAPI 3.0 specification using `components/securitySchemes` to define the `http` type with `basic` scheme, and the `security` section to apply it to the entire API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/basic-authentication.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
---
components:
  securitySchemes:
    basicAuth: # <-- arbitrary name for the security scheme
      type: http
      scheme: basic

security:
  - basicAuth: [] # <-- use the same name here
```

TITLE: Incorrect YAML for Mixed Types in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates an incorrect way to define mixed data types in OpenAPI. Using a list for the `type` keyword is not valid in OpenAPI, even though it is valid in JSON Schema. Instead, `oneOf` or `anyOf` should be used.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
type:
  - string
  - integer
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Definition for Webhook Subscription Endpoint
DESCRIPTION: Defines the `/subscribe` POST operation in OpenAPI 3.0. It specifies the `requestBody` schema for the `callbackUrl` (as a string with `uri` format) and the expected `201` response indicating successful webhook creation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/callbacks.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
info:
  version: 0.0.0
  title: test

paths:
  /subscribe:
    post:
      summary: Subscribe to a webhook
      requestBody:
        required: true
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              type: object
              properties:
                callbackUrl: # Callback URL
                  type: string
                  format: uri
                  example: https://myserver.com/send/callback/here
              required:
                - callbackUrl
      responses:
        "201":
          description: Webhook created
```

TITLE: Overriding Global Security in OpenAPI Operations
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to apply security settings at the operation level within an OpenAPI `paths` definition. It shows how to specify a particular OAuth2 scope (`admin`) for `/billing_info` and how to explicitly disable security (`[]`) for the `/ping` endpoint, overriding any global security configurations.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /billing_info:
    get:
      summary: Gets the account billing info
      security:
        - OAuth2: [admin] # Use OAuth with a different scope
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
        "401":
          description: Not authenticated
        "403":
          description: Access token does not have the required scope

  /ping:
    get:
      summary: Checks if the server is running
      security: [] # No security
      responses:
        "200":
          description: Server is up and running
        default:
          description: Something is wrong
```

TITLE: OpenAPI $ref Sibling Element Ignorance Example
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates how properties like `description` and `default` are ignored when placed as siblings to a `$ref` in an OpenAPI schema. The `DateWithExample` schema, despite defining these properties, will resolve identically to the `Date` schema it references.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/using-ref.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    Date:
      type: string
      format: date

    DateWithExample:
      $ref: "#/components/schemas/Date"
      description: Date schema extended with a `default` value... Or not?
      default: 2000-01-01
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI Serialization Keyword to URI Template Modifier Mapping
DESCRIPTION: This API documentation table maps OpenAPI serialization keywords (`style`, `explode`, `allowReserved`) to their corresponding URI Template modifiers as defined by RFC 6570. It serves as a reference for understanding how OpenAPI parameters are serialized into URIs.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/serialization.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Keyword: style: simple, URI Template Modifier: none
Keyword: style: label, URI Template Modifier: . prefix
Keyword: style: matrix, URI Template Modifier: ; prefix
Keyword: style: form, URI Template Modifier: ? or & prefix (depending on the parameter position in the query string)
Keyword: style: pipeDelimited, URI Template Modifier: ? or & prefix (depending on the parameter position in the query string) – but using pipes | instead of commas, to join the array values
Keyword: style: spaceDelimited, URI Template Modifier: ? or & prefix (depending on the parameter position in the query string) – but using spaces instead of commas , to join the array values
Keyword: explode: false, URI Template Modifier: none
Keyword: explode: true, URI Template Modifier: * suffix
Keyword: allowReserved: false, URI Template Modifier: none
Keyword: allowReserved: true, URI Template Modifier: + prefix
```

TITLE: Defining Array Examples in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates various ways to define examples for arrays in OpenAPI specifications, including examples for individual array items, simple arrays, and arrays containing complex objects.

components:
  schemas:
    ArrayOfInt:
      type: array
      items:
        type: integer
        format: int64
        example: 1
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:

      type: array

        type: integer
        format: int64
      example: [1, 2, 3]
```

CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    ArrayOfUsers:
      type: array

        type: object

            type: integer

            type: string

        - id: 10
          name: Jessica Smith
        - id: 20
          name: Ron Stewart

TITLE: Swagger UI Display Configuration Parameters
DESCRIPTION: Detailed documentation for parameters that control the visual presentation and interactive features of Swagger UI. Each parameter defines a specific aspect of the UI's behavior, from how models are expanded to how operations are sorted and filtered.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/configuration.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: deepLinking
  Type: Boolean
  Default: false
  Docker Variable: DEEP_LINKING
  Description: If set to true, enables deep linking for tags and operations. See the Deep Linking documentation for more information.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: displayOperationId
  Type: Boolean
  Default: false
  Docker Variable: DISPLAY_OPERATION_ID
  Description: Controls the display of operationId in operations list. The default is false.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: defaultModelsExpandDepth
  Type: Number
  Default: 1
  Docker Variable: DEFAULT_MODELS_EXPAND_DEPTH
  Description: The default expansion depth for models (set to -1 completely hide the models).
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: defaultModelExpandDepth
  Type: Number
  Default: 1
  Docker Variable: DEFAULT_MODEL_EXPAND_DEPTH
  Description: The default expansion depth for the model on the model-example section.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: defaultModelRendering
  Type: String
  Default: ["example"*, "model"]
  Docker Variable: DEFAULT_MODEL_RENDERING
  Description: Controls how the model is shown when the API is first rendered. (The user can always switch the rendering for a given model by clicking the 'Model' and 'Example Value' links.)
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: displayRequestDuration
  Type: Boolean
  Default: false
  Docker Variable: DISPLAY_REQUEST_DURATION
  Description: Controls the display of the request duration (in milliseconds) for "Try it out" requests.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: docExpansion
  Type: String
  Default: ["list"*, "full", "none"]
  Docker Variable: DOC_EXPANSION
  Description: Controls the default expansion setting for the operations and tags. It can be 'list' (expands only the tags), 'full' (expands the tags and operations) or 'none' (expands nothing).
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: filter
  Type: Boolean OR String
  Default: false
  Docker Variable: FILTER
  Description: If set, enables filtering. The top bar will show an edit box that you can use to filter the tagged operations that are shown. Can be Boolean to enable or disable, or a string, in which case filtering will be enabled using that string as the filter expression. Filtering is case sensitive matching the filter expression anywhere inside the tag.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: maxDisplayedTags
  Type: Number
  Default: (show all operations)
  Docker Variable: MAX_DISPLAYED_TAGS
  Description: If set, limits the number of tagged operations displayed to at most this many. The default is to show all operations.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: operationsSorter
  Type: Function OR String
  Default: (server order)
  Description: Applies a sort to the operation list of each API. It can be 'alpha' (sort by paths alphanumerically), 'method' (sort by HTTP method) or a function (see Array.prototype.sort() to know how sort function works). Default is the order returned by the server unchanged.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: showExtensions
  Type: Boolean
  Default: false
  Docker Variable: SHOW_EXTENSIONS
  Description: Controls the display of vendor extension (x-) fields and values for Operations, Parameters, Responses, and Schema.
```

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: showCommonExtensions
  Type: Boolean
  Default: false
  Docker Variable: SHOW_COMMON_EXTENSIONS
  Description: Controls the display of extensions
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Definition for Callback Subscription and Unsubscription
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI (Swagger) YAML snippet defines API endpoints for managing callback subscriptions. It includes a '/subscribe' endpoint with parameters for callback URL and event, returning a 'subscriberId'. It also demonstrates how to link this ID to an '/unsubscribe' operation, allowing clients to remove their subscription. The example also shows how to define 'callbacks' within an operation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/callbacks.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
paths:
/subscribe:
  description: Add a subscriber
  post:
    parameters:
      - name: callbackUrl
        in: query
        required: true
        schema:
          type: string
          format: uri
      - name: event
        in: query
        required: true
        schema:
          type: string
    responses:
      '201':
        description: Added
        content:
          application/json:
            type: object
            properties:
              subscriberId:
                type: string
                example: AAA-123-BBB-456
    links:  # Link the returned id with the unsubscribe operation
      unsubscribeOp:
        operationId: unsubscribeOperation
            parameters:
              Id: $response.body#/subscriberId
    callbacks:
      myEvent:
        '{$request.query.callbackUrl}?event={$request.query.event}':
          post:
            requestBody:
              content:
                application/json:
                  example:
                    message: Some event
            responses:
              '200':
                description: OK

/unsubscribe:
  post:
    operationId: unsubscribeOperation
    parameters:
      - name: Id
        in: query
        required: true
        schema:
          type: string
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI Runtime Expression Syntax Reference
DESCRIPTION: A comprehensive list of runtime expressions available in OpenAPI, detailing their purpose and how they extract values from requests and responses. These expressions refer to the current operation where links are defined. The evaluated expression typically has the same type as the referenced value, and if an expression cannot be evaluated, no parameter value is passed to the target operation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Expression: $url
Description: The full request URL, including the query string.

Expression: $method
Description: Request HTTP method, such as GET or POST.

Expression: $request.query._param_name_
Description: The value of the specified query parameter. The parameter must be defined in the operation’s parameters section, otherwise, it cannot be evaluated. Parameter names are case-sensitive.

Expression: $request.path._param_name_
Description: The value of the specified path parameter. The parameter must be defined in the operation’s parameters section, otherwise, it cannot be evaluated. Parameter names are case-sensitive.

Expression: $request.header._header_name_
Description: The value of the specified request header. This header must be defined in the operation’s parameters section, otherwise, it cannot be evaluated. Header names are case-insensitive.

Expression: $request.body
Description: The entire request body.

Expression: $request.body_#/foo/bar_
Description: A portion of the request body specified by a JSON Pointer.

Expression: $statusCode
Description: HTTP status code of the response. For example, 200 or 404.

Expression: $response.header._header_name_
Description: The complete value of the specified response header, as a string. Header names are case-insensitive. The header does not need to be defined in the response’s headers section.

Expression: $response.body
Description: The entire response body.

Expression: $response.body_#/foo/bar_
Description: A portion of the request body specified by a JSON Pointer.

Expression: foo{$request.path.id}bar
Description: Enclose an expression into {} curly braces to embed it into a string.
```

TITLE: Define HTTP Status Codes and Ranges (OpenAPI YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates how to define various HTTP status codes (200, 400, 401, 404) and status code ranges (5XX) for API responses in OpenAPI 3.0, along with their descriptions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
responses:
  "200":
    description: OK
  "400":
    description: Bad request. User ID must be an integer and larger than 0.
  "401":
    description: Authorization information is missing or invalid.
  "404":
    description: A user with the specified ID was not found.
  "5XX":
    description: Unexpected error.
```

TITLE: Define Nested Objects Inline in OpenAPI YAML
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates defining a nested object directly within a parent object's schema in OpenAPI. The `contact_info` property is itself an object with its own properties like `email` and `phone`, illustrating direct embedding of complex structures within a schema.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_21

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    User:
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
        name:
          type: string
        contact_info:
          # The value of this property is an object
          type: object
          properties:
            email:
              type: string
              format: email
            phone:
              type: string
```

TITLE: Define Cookie Parameters in OpenAPI

CODE:

parameters:
  - in: cookie
    name: debug
    schema:
      type: integer
      enum: [0, 1]
      default: 0

    name: csrftoken
    schema:
      type: string

TITLE: OpenAPI Response Body Examples (Multiple)
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to provide multiple examples for a response body. The `examples` keyword is a child of the media type, allowing distinct examples like "Jessica" and "Ron" for a 200 OK response.

responses:
  "200":
    description: A user object.
    content:
      application/json:
        schema:
          $ref: "#/components/schemas/User" # Reference to an object
        examples:
          Jessica:
            value:
              id: 10
              name: Jessica Smith
          Ron:
            value:
              id: 20
              name: Ron Stewart
```

TITLE: Configure OpenAPI OAuth 2.0 Client Credentials Flow
DESCRIPTION: Provides an example of defining the OAuth 2.0 Client Credentials flow in an OpenAPI `securitySchemes` component. This flow uses `tokenUrl` and an optional `refreshUrl`, often without explicit scopes, as seen with Getty Images API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_11

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    oAuth2ClientCredentials:
      type: oauth2
      description: See http://developers.gettyimages.com/api/docs/v3/oauth2.html
      flows:
        clientCredentials:
          tokenUrl: https://api.gettyimages.com/oauth2/token/
          scopes: {} # Getty Images does not use scopes
```

TITLE: Applying Operation-Specific OAuth2 Scopes in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet advises against applying broad global scopes and instead demonstrates how to define specific OAuth2 scopes for individual operations. It shows how the `/users` `GET` operation requires `read` scope, and the `POST` operation requires `write` scope, ensuring granular access control.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
# Instead of this:
# security:
#   - OAuth2:
#       - read
#       - write

# Do this:
paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Get a list of users
      security:
        - OAuth2: [read]     # <------
      ...

    post:
      summary: Add a user
      security:
        - OAuth2: [write]    # <------
      ...
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Combining Security Schemes with Logical AND in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates the logical AND combination of security schemes in OpenAPI. When multiple security schemes are listed within the same hashmap item in the `security` array, all of them must be used simultaneously for authentication.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/authentication.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
security: # A AND B
  - A
    B
```

TITLE: Defining Common Parameters at the Path Level in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define parameters that are common to all operations (methods) of a specific path directly at the path level in OpenAPI. This promotes reusability and reduces redundancy. It also shows how operation-level parameters combine with or override path-level parameters.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_22

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /user/{id}:
    parameters:
      - in: path
        name: id
        schema:
          type: integer
        required: true
        description: The user ID
    get:
      summary: Gets a user by ID
      ...
    patch:
      summary: Updates an existing user with the specified ID
      ...
    delete:
      summary: Deletes the user with the specified ID
      ...
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{id}:
    parameters:
      - in: path
        name: id
        schema:
          type: integer
        required: true
        description: The user ID.

    # GET/users/{id}?metadata=true
    get:
      summary: Gets a user by ID
      # Note we only define the query parameter, because the {id} is defined at the path level.
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: metadata
          schema:
            type: boolean
          required: false
          description: If true, the endpoint returns only the user metadata.
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{id}:
    parameters:
      - in: path
        name: id
        schema:
          type: integer
        required: true
        description: The user ID.

    # DELETE /users/{id} - uses a single ID.
    # Reuses the {id} parameter definition from the path level.
    delete:
      summary: Deletes the user with the specified ID.
      responses:
        "204":
          description: User was deleted.

    # GET /users/id1,id2,id3 - uses one or more user IDs.
    # Overrides the path-level {id} parameter.
    get:
      summary: Gets one or more users by ID.
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: id
          required: true
          description: A comma-separated list of user IDs.
          schema:
            type: array
            items:
              type: integer
            minItems: 1
          explode: false
          style: simple
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Defining 401 Unauthorized Response for Basic Authentication in OpenAPI 3.0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /something:
    get:
      ...
      responses:
        ...
        '401':
            $ref: '#/components/responses/UnauthorizedError'
    post:
      ...
      responses:
        ...
        '401':
          $ref: '#/components/responses/UnauthorizedError'
...
components:
  responses:
    UnauthorizedError:
      description: Authentication information is missing or invalid
      headers:
        WWW_Authenticate:
          schema:
            type: string
```

TITLE: Specify Default Values for Optional Parameters in Swagger/OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to use the 'default' keyword for optional parameters, allowing the server to use a predefined value if the client doesn't provide one. It also shows how to define 'minimum' and 'maximum' constraints for numerical parameters.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
GET /users
GET /users?offset=30&limit=10
```

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: offset
    type: integer
    required: false
    default: 0
    minimum: 0
    description: The number of items to skip before starting to collect the result set.
  - in: query
    name: limit
    type: integer
    required: false
    default: 20
    minimum: 1
    maximum: 100
    description: The numbers of items to return.
```

TITLE: Define Default Error Response in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Explains and demonstrates the use of the `default` response in OpenAPI 3.0 to collectively describe all HTTP status codes not individually covered for an operation, typically for common error structures.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
responses:
  "200":
    description: Success
    content:
      application/json:
        schema:
          $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"

  # Definition of all error statuses
  default:
    description: Unexpected error
    content:
      application/json:
        schema:
          $ref: "#/components/schemas/Error"
```

CODE:
```
security: # (A AND B) OR (C AND D)
  - A
    B
  - C
    D
```

TITLE: Defining Global Cookie Authentication in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to define a cookie-based API key security scheme (`JSESSIONID`) in OpenAPI 3.0 and apply it globally to all API operations using the `security` key.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/cookie-authentication.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
---
# 1) Define the cookie name
components:
  securitySchemes:
    cookieAuth: # arbitrary name for the security scheme; will be used in the "security" key later
      type: apiKey
      in: cookie
      name: JSESSIONID # cookie name

# 2) Apply cookie auth globally to all operations
security:
  - cookieAuth: []
```

TITLE: Defining Multiple Media Types with Inline Schemas in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to specify different media types for a single response in an OpenAPI specification, each with its own inline schema definition for the response body. This allows for varied content representations based on the client's 'Accept' header.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /employees:
    get:
      summary: Returns a list of employees.
      responses:
        "200": # Response
          description: OK
          content: # Response body
            application/json: # One of media types
              schema:
                type: object
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                  name:
                    type: string
                  fullTime:
                    type: boolean
            application/xml: # Another media types
              schema:
                type: object
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                  name:
                    type: string
                  fullTime:
                    type: boolean
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Link Parameters with Runtime Expressions and Hard-coded Values
DESCRIPTION: This snippet provides an example of defining link parameters using a combination of runtime expressions and hard-coded values. It shows how to link a 'Get relative date ranges' operation to a 'Get report' operation, passing a selected date range from the response and setting other parameters to empty strings.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /date_ranges:
    get:
      summary: Get relative date ranges for the report.
      responses:
        '200':
          description: OK
          content:
            application/json:
              example: [Today, Yesterday, LastWeek, ThisMonth]
          links:
            ReportRelDate:
              operationId: getReport
              # Call "getReport" with the `rdate` parameter and with empty `start_date` and `end_date`
              parameters:
                rdate: '$response.body#/1'
                start_date: ''
                end_date: ''

  # GET /report?rdate=...
  # GET /report?start_date=...&end_date=...
  /report:
    get:
      operationId: getReport
      ...
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Keywords for Standard HTTP Headers
DESCRIPTION: This API documentation table outlines the specific OpenAPI keywords used to describe standard HTTP headers like 'Content-Type', 'Accept', and 'Authorization', which are not allowed to be defined as 'in: header' parameters. It provides references to relevant OpenAPI specification sections for more details on their proper usage.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Header | OpenAPI keywords | For more information, see...
-------|------------------|-----------------------------
Content-Type | Request content type: requestBody.content.<media-type>
Response content type: responses.<code>.content.<media-type> | Describing Request Body,
Describing Responses,
Media Types
Accept | responses.<code>.content.<media-type> | Describing Responses,
Media Types
Authorization | securitySchemes, security | Authentication
```

    externalDocs:

TITLE: Defining Reusable Common Parameters in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to define reusable API parameters, such as pagination controls (offset and limit), in the global `components` section of an OpenAPI specification. These common parameters can then be easily referenced and applied to multiple API paths, like /users and /teams, promoting consistency and reducing redundancy in API definitions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_23

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
components:
  parameters:
    offsetParam: # <-- Arbitrary name for the definition that will be used to refer to it.
      # Not necessarily the same as the parameter name.
      in: query
      name: offset
      required: false
      schema:
        type: integer
        minimum: 0
      description: The number of items to skip before starting to collect the result set.
    limitParam:
      in: query
      name: limit
      required: false
      schema:
        type: integer
        minimum: 1
        maximum: 50
        default: 20
      description: The numbers of items to return.

paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Gets a list of users.
      parameters:
        - $ref: "#/components/parameters/offsetParam"
        - $ref: "#/components/parameters/limitParam"
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
  /teams:
    get:
      summary: Gets a list of teams.
      parameters:
        - $ref: "#/components/parameters/offsetParam"
        - $ref: "#/components/parameters/limitParam"
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
```

LANGUAGE: YAML

```
components:
  schemas:
    AnyValue:

      description: Can be any value, including `null`.
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Link Parameters and Request Body Definition
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates how to define input parameters and request bodies for linked operations using `parameters` and `requestBody` keywords. It shows how to extract values from the original operation's response body using runtime expressions and pass them to the target operation's parameters or request body.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
links:
  # GET /users/{userId}
  GetUserByUserId:
    operationId: getUser
    parameters:
      userId: "$response.body#/id"

  # POST /users/{userId}/manager with the manager ID in the request body
  SetManagerId:
    operationId: setUserManager
    requestBody: "$response.body#/id"
```

TITLE: OpenAPI String Formats
DESCRIPTION: Explains the optional `format` modifier for string types in OpenAPI, providing hints about content and format. It lists built-in formats like `date`, `date-time`, `password`, `byte`, and `binary`, and also mentions custom formats like `email` and `uuid`. Tools can use these formats for validation or type mapping.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
OpenAPI Built-in String Formats:
- date: full-date notation (RFC 3339, section 5.6), e.g., 2017-07-21
- date-time: date-time notation (RFC 3339, section 5.6), e.g., 2017-07-21T17:32:28Z
- password: hint to UIs to mask the input
- byte: base64-encoded characters, e.g., U3dhZ2dlciByb2Nrcw==
- binary: binary data, used to describe files

Custom String Formats (Examples):
- email
- uuid
- uri
- hostname
- ipv4
- ipv6
```

TITLE: Create Custom Swagger UI Layout for Operations
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to define a custom React component, `OperationsLayout`, to serve as a Swagger UI layout that only displays API operations. It then shows how to create a plugin to provide this component to Swagger UI and configure Swagger UI to use it. This allows for highly customized views of the API documentation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/custom-layout.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
import React from "react"

// Create the layout component
class OperationsLayout extends React.Component {
  render() {
    const {
      getComponent
    } = this.props

    const Operations = getComponent("operations", true)

    return (
      <div className="swagger-ui">
        <Operations />
      </div>
    )
  }
}

// Create the plugin that provides our layout component
const OperationsLayoutPlugin = () => {
  return {
    components: {
      OperationsLayout: OperationsLayout
    }
  }
}

// Provide the plugin to Swagger-UI, and select OperationsLayout
// as the layout for Swagger-UI
SwaggerUI({
  url: "https://petstore.swagger.io/v2/swagger.json",
  plugins: [ OperationsLayoutPlugin ],
  layout: "OperationsLayout"
})
```

TITLE: Configure OpenAPI OAuth 2.0 Implicit Flow
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define the OAuth 2.0 Implicit flow in an OpenAPI `securitySchemes` component. This flow uses `authorizationUrl` to obtain the access token directly from the authorization server.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    oAuth2Implicit:
      type: oauth2
      description: For more information, see https://developers.getbase.com/docs/rest/articles/oauth2/requests
      flows:
        implicit:
          authorizationUrl: https://api.getbase.com/oauth2/authorize
          scopes:
            read: Grant read-only access to all your data except for the account and user info
            write: Grant write-only access to all your data except for the account and user info
            profile: Grant read-only access to the account and user info only
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Defining Object Request Body in OpenAPI 2.0
DESCRIPTION: Swagger 2.0 definition for a POST /users operation with an object (JSON) request body. It specifies the 'consumes' type, 'in: body' parameter, and a 'schema' detailing the object's properties and required fields directly within the parameter definition.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    post:
      summary: Creates a new user.
      consumes:
        - application/json
      parameters:
        - in: body
          name: user
          description: The user to create.
          schema:
            type: object
            required:
              - userName
            properties:
              userName:
                type: string
              firstName:
                type: string
              lastName:
                type: string
      responses:
        201:
          description: Created
```

TITLE: OpenAPI anyOf Keyword for Flexible Schema Validation
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates the `anyOf` keyword, which validates data if it matches one or more of the provided subschemas. This allows for flexible request body structures where multiple valid formats are acceptable.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/oneof-anyof-allof-not.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /pets:
    patch:
      requestBody:
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              anyOf:
                - $ref: "#/components/schemas/PetByAge"
                - $ref: "#/components/schemas/PetByType"
      responses:
        "200":
          description: Updated

components:
  schemas:
    PetByAge:
      type: object
      properties:
        age:
          type: integer
        nickname:
          type: string
      required:
        - age

    PetByType:
      type: object
      properties:
        pet_type:
          type: string
          enum: [Cat, Dog]
        hunts:
          type: boolean
      required:
        - pet_type
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Schema with Custom Content-Type for Multipart Part
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to specify a custom `Content-Type` for individual parts of a multipart request in OpenAPI 3.0. This is achieved using the `encoding` keyword at the same level as `schema`, allowing explicit control over the media type of a specific request part, such as an image.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/multipart-requests.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
requestBody:
  content:
    multipart/form-data:
      schema:
        type: object
        properties: # Request parts
          id:
            type: string
            format: uuid
          address:
            type: object
            properties:
              street:
                type: string
              city:
                type: string
          profileImage:
            type: string
            format: base64
      encoding: # The same level as schema
        profileImage: # Property name (see above)
          contentType: image/png, image/jpeg
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /something:
    get:
      security:
        - basicAuth: []
```

TITLE: Embed Swagger UI via unpkg CDN (Basic)

TITLE: Defining Object and Property Examples in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to specify example values for entire objects and individual properties within OpenAPI schemas using YAML. Shows both property-level and object-level example definitions for a 'User' schema.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    User: # Schema name
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
          format: int64
          example: 1 # Property example
        name:
          type: string
          example: New order # Property example
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    User: # Schema name
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
        name:
          type: string
      example: # Object-level example
        id: 1
        name: Jessica Smith
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Response Body Example (Single)
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to add a single example for a response body. The `example` keyword is a child of the media type (`application/json`) when the schema references an object. This example provides a sample user object for a 200 OK response.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
responses:
  "200":
    description: A user object.
    content:
      application/json:
        schema:
          $ref: "#/components/schemas/User" # Reference to an object
        example:
          # Properties of the referenced object
          id: 10
          name: Jessica Smith
```

TITLE: React Components and Swagger UI Plugin for Date Pickers
DESCRIPTION: Provides React components (`JsonSchema_string_date` and `JsonSchema_string_date_time`) that wrap `react-datepicker` to handle date and date-time inputs respectively. The `DateTimeSwaggerPlugin` registers these components with Swagger UI, enabling custom date picker functionality based on the schema's format.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plug-points.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
import React from "react";
import DatePicker from "react-datepicker";
import "react-datepicker/dist/react-datepicker.css";

const JsonSchema_string_date = (props) => {
  const dateNumber = Date.parse(props.value);
  const date = dateNumber
    ? new Date(dateNumber)
    : new Date();

  return (
    <DatePicker
      selected={date}
      onChange={d => props.onChange(d.toISOString().substring(0, 10))}
    />
  );
}

const JsonSchema_string_date_time = (props) => {
  const dateNumber = Date.parse(props.value);
  const date = dateNumber
    ? new Date(dateNumber)
    : new Date();

  return (
    <DatePicker
      selected={date}
      onChange={d => props.onChange(d.toISOString())}
      showTimeSelect
      timeFormat="p"
      dateFormat="Pp"
    />
  );
}


export const DateTimeSwaggerPlugin = {
  components: {
    JsonSchema_string_date: JsonSchema_string_date,
    "JsonSchema_string_date-time": JsonSchema_string_date_time
  }
};
```

TITLE: Specify Multiple Response Media Types (OpenAPI YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to define different media types (JSON, XML, plain text, image/png) for API responses using the 'content' keyword in OpenAPI 3.0. It includes examples for retrieving user lists and an image.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Get all users
      responses:
        "200":
          description: A list of users
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/ArrayOfUsers"
            application/xml:
              schema:
                $ref: "#/components/schemas/ArrayOfUsers"
            text/plain:
              schema:
                type: string

  # This operation returns image
  /logo:
    get:
      summary: Get the logo image
      responses:
        "200":
          description: Logo image in PNG format
          content:
            image/png:
              schema:
                type: string
                format: binary
```

TITLE: Defining Empty-Valued and Nullable Parameters in OpenAPI

TITLE: Compose Swagger UI React with Editor Plugins

The component is then rendered into a DOM element.

```
import React from 'react';

import EditorPreviewPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview';
import EditorPreviewSwaggerUIPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-swagger-ui';
import EditorPreviewAsyncAPIPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-asyncapi';

TITLE: Example HTTP Multipart/Form-Data Request

Content-Length: 428

--abcde12345

Content-Type: text/plain

123e4567-e89b-12d3-a456-426655440000
--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="address"
Content-Type: application/json

{
  "street": "3, Garden St",
  "city": "Hillsbery, UT"
}
--abcde12345

Content-Type: application/octet-stream

{…file content…}
--abcde12345--
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Definition for Callback Mechanism
DESCRIPTION: Extends the `/subscribe` operation with the `callbacks` keyword. This section defines a callback named `myEvent` with a dynamic URL derived from the initial request body (`{$request.body#/callbackUrl}`). It also specifies the `post` method for the callback, its `requestBody` schema (containing a `message`), and the expected `200` response from the callback receiver.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/callbacks.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /subscribe:
    post:
      summary: Subscribe to a webhook
      requestBody: …
      callbacks: # Callback definition
        myEvent: # Event name
          "{$request.body#/callbackUrl}": # The callback URL,
            # Refers to the passed URL
            post:
              requestBody: # Contents of the callback message
                required: true
                content:
                  application/json:
                    schema:
                      type: object
                      properties:
                        message:
                          type: string
                          example: Some event happened
                      required:
                        - message
              responses: # Expected responses to the callback message
                "200":
                  description: Your server returns this code if it accepts the callback
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define Default Values for Optional Parameters in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to use the `default` keyword in a parameter schema to specify a default value for an optional parameter. This value is used by the server if the client does not supply the parameter. The example defines `offset` and `limit` query parameters with their types, minimum/maximum values, and default settings.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_16

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: offset
    schema:
      type: integer
      minimum: 0
      default: 0
    required: false
    description: The number of items to skip before starting to collect the result set.
  - in: query
    name: limit
    schema:
      type: integer
      minimum: 1
      maximum: 100
      default: 20
    required: false
    description: The number of items to return.
```

TITLE: Server Templating for Regional API Endpoints
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to use a `region` variable to define regional API endpoints, allowing clients to select a specific geographical server with a default region.

TITLE: Assigning Unique Operation IDs in OpenAPI 2.0
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates the use of `operationId` in OpenAPI Specification v2.0. Each operation (a combination of path and HTTP method) can be assigned a unique `operationId`, which is often used by code generators to name corresponding methods in client SDKs or server stubs. Examples are provided for `GET /users`, `POST /users`, and `GET /user/{id}`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
/users:
    get:
      operationId: getUsers
      summary: Gets all users.
      ...
    post:
      operationId: addUser
      summary: Adds a new user.
      ...
  /user/{id}:
    get:
      operationId: getUserById
      summary: Gets a user by user ID.
      ...
```

TITLE: Using Relative URLs in OpenAPI Definitions
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates the use of relative URLs within an OpenAPI definition. Relative URLs in the `servers` array are resolved against the host serving the OpenAPI definition. Additionally, other URLs like `termsOfService`, `externalDocs`, and OAuth 2 flow endpoints can also be specified as relative paths, providing flexibility for on-premises installations.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/api-host-and-base-path.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
servers:
  - url: https://api.example.com
  - url: https://sandbox-api.example.com

# Relative URL to Terms of Service
info:
  version: 0.0.0
  title: test
  termsOfService: /terms-of-use

# Relative URL to external documentation
externalDocs:
  url: /docs
  description: Find more info here

# Relative URLs to OAuth2 authorization and token URLs
components:
  securitySchemes:
    oauth2:
      type: oauth2
      flows:
        authorizationCode:
          authorizationUrl: /oauth/dialog
          tokenUrl: /oauth/token
```

TITLE: Define a Dictionary Schema with Fixed and Additional Keys in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 schema shows how to define a dictionary that includes both fixed, explicitly defined properties (e.g., `default`) and additional, arbitrary key-value pairs. The `required` keyword ensures the fixed keys are present, while `additionalProperties` handles the dynamic part.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/dictionaries.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
type: object
properties:
  default:
    type: string
required:
  - default
additionalProperties:
  type: string
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Mapping Discriminator Values to Schema Names in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This YAML example demonstrates the use of the `discriminator/mapping` keyword within an OpenAPI schema. It shows how to define a `discriminator` on a `oneOf` composition, specifying `propertyName` as `objectType`. The `mapping` section then explicitly links custom property values (e.g., `obj1`, `obj2`, `system`) to their corresponding schema references, including schemas defined within the same spec and an external schema (`sysObject.json#/sysObject`). This allows for flexible type resolution where property values do not directly match schema names.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/inheritance-and-polymorphism.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
components:
  responses:
    sampleObjectResponse:
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            oneOf:
              - $ref: '#/components/schemas/Object1'
              - $ref: '#/components/schemas/Object2'
              - $ref: 'sysObject.json#/sysObject'
            discriminator:
              propertyName: objectType
              mapping:
                obj1: '#/components/schemas/Object1'
                obj2: '#/components/schemas/Object2'
                system: 'sysObject.json#/sysObject'
  …
  schemas:
    Object1:
      type: object
      required:
        - objectType
      properties:
        objectType:
          type: string
      …
    Object2:
      type: object
      required:
        - objectType
      properties:
        objectType:
          type: string
      …
```

TITLE: Run Swagger Generator Minimal Docker Image in CI Pipeline

GEN_IP=$(docker inspect --format '{{.NetworkSettings.IPAddress}}'  $CID)
```

TITLE: Basic Structure for Defining Links in OpenAPI Responses
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates the basic structure for including a `links` section within the `responses` object of an OpenAPI specification. It shows where the `links` keyword is placed for both successful (200) and error (400) responses, indicating that links can be defined for any response status code.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
responses:
  "200":
    description: Created
    content: ...
    links: # <----
      ...
  "400":
    description: Bad request
    content: ...
    links: # <----
      ...
```

TITLE: Define Request Body with Wildcard Media Type in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 YAML snippet illustrates how to use a wildcard media type (`image/*`) in a request body definition for a PUT operation on `/avatar`. It allows any image type (e.g., PNG, SVG, GIF) to be uploaded as binary data.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /avatar:
    put:
      summary: Upload an avatar
      requestBody:
        content:
          image/*: # Can be image/png, image/svg, image/gif, etc.
            schema:
              type: string
              format: binary
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define Multiple Error Responses with Same Schema in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to explicitly define multiple HTTP error responses (e.g., 400, 404) that share the same schema, before introducing the `default` response concept.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_11

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
responses:
  "200":
    description: Success
    content:
      application/json:
        schema:
          $ref: "#/components/schemas/User"

  # These two error responses have the same schema
  "400":
    description: Bad request
    content:
      application/json:
        schema:
          $ref: "#/components/schemas/Error"
  "404":
    description: Not found
    content:
      application/json:
        schema:
          $ref: "#/components/schemas/Error"
```

TITLE: Assigning Tags to OpenAPI Operations
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to associate `tags` with specific API operations (e.g., `get`, `post`) under the `paths` object in an OpenAPI 3.0 definition. Tags are crucial for grouping related endpoints, which tools like Swagger UI utilize for navigation and display purposes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/grouping-operations-with-tags.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /pet/findByStatus:
    get:
      summary: Finds pets by Status
      tags:
        - pets
      ...
  /pet:
    post:
      summary: Adds a new pet to the store
      tags:
        - pets
      ...
  /store/inventory:
    get:
      summary: Returns pet inventories
      tags:
        - store
      ...
```

TITLE: Applying API Keys to Specific Operations in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to apply an API key security scheme to a specific operation (e.g., a GET request to `/something`) within the `paths` section of an OpenAPI 3.0 definition, overriding global security settings.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/api-keys.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /something:
    get:
      # Operation-specific security:
      security:
        - ApiKeyAuth: []
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK (successfully authenticated)
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Callback URL Runtime Expression
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates the use of a runtime expression (`{$request.body#/callbackUrl}`) to dynamically specify the callback URL. This expression indicates that the callback URL will be extracted from the `callbackUrl` property of the initial `/subscribe` request's body.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/callbacks.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
callbacks:
  myEvent:
    "{$request.body#/callbackUrl}": # The callback URL, refers to the URL passed in the request body
```

TITLE: Define Query Parameter with Schema in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Explains how to use the `schema` keyword for simple parameter serialization, such as arrays and objects, which are serialized into a string. It demonstrates defining a query parameter `color` as an array of strings, with `form` style and `explode: false` for serialization.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: color
    schema:
      type: array
      items:
        type: string

    # Serialize as color=blue,black,brown (default)
    style: form
    explode: false
```

TITLE: Customize Generated SDK with Language-Specific Options
DESCRIPTION: This JSON payload illustrates how to include language-specific customization options when generating an SDK. By adding an `options` object with `additionalProperties`, users can enable features like `useRuntimeException` or `useRxJava` for the generated code. These options allow fine-tuning the output to meet specific project requirements.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/online-generators.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: json
CODE:
```
{
  "specURL" : "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/OAI/OpenAPI-Specification/master/examples/v3.0/petstore.yaml",
  "lang" : "java",
  "options" : {
    "additionalProperties" : {
    "useRuntimeException": true,
    "useRxJava" : true
    }
  },
  "type" : "CLIENT",
  "codegenVersion" : "V3"
}
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Path Uniqueness with Query Strings (Conceptual)
DESCRIPTION: Explains that OpenAPI considers a unique operation as a combination of a path and HTTP method. This means paths differing only by query strings are not considered unique operations by the specification.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
GET /users?firstName=value&lastName=value
GET /users?role=value
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Reference External OpenAPI Components with $ref
DESCRIPTION: This YAML example illustrates how to define components by referencing external files or URLs using the `$ref` keyword. This approach allows for modular API definitions, enabling the reuse of common components maintained in separate locations and providing local aliases for easier referencing.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/components.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    Pet:
      $ref: "../models/pet.yaml"
      # Can now use use '#/components/schemas/Pet' instead
    User:
      $ref: "https://api.example.com/v2/openapi.yaml#/components/schemas/User"
      # Can now use '#/components/schemas/User' instead

  responses:
    GenericError:
      $ref: "../template-api.yaml#/components/responses/GenericError"
      # Can now use '#/components/responses/GenericError' instead
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Reusable Enum Definition using Components and $ref in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to define a reusable enum, `Color`, within the `components/schemas` section of an OpenAPI 3.0 document. It then demonstrates referencing this reusable enum using `$ref` for a query parameter, promoting consistency and reducing redundancy across the API definition.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/enums.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /products:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: color
          required: true
          schema:
            $ref: "#/components/schemas/Color"
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
components:
  schemas:
    Color:
      type: string
      enum:
        - black
        - white
        - red
        - green
        - blue
```

TITLE: Defining OAuth 2.0 Security Scheme in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates how to configure an OAuth 2.0 security scheme within the `components/securitySchemes` section of an OpenAPI Specification 3.0 document. It specifically uses the implicit grant flow, defines the authorization URL, and specifies `read_pets` and `write_pets` scopes. The example also shows how to apply this defined security scheme globally using the `security` key.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
# Step 1 - define the security scheme
components:
  securitySchemes:
    oAuthSample:    # <---- arbitrary name
      type: oauth2
      description: This API uses OAuth 2 with the implicit grant flow. [More info](https://api.example.com/docs/auth)
      flows:
        implicit:   # <---- OAuth flow(authorizationCode, implicit, password or clientCredentials)
          authorizationUrl: https://api.example.com/oauth2/authorize
          scopes:
            read_pets: read your pets
            write_pets: modify pets in your account

# Step 2 - apply security globally...
security:
  - oAuthSample:
    - write_pets
    - read_pets
```

TITLE: Documenting Set-Cookie Header in OpenAPI Response
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to document the `Set-Cookie` header in an OpenAPI 3.0 response for a login operation, including its schema and an example value, for documentation purposes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/cookie-authentication.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /login:
    post:
      summary: Logs in and returns the authentication  cookie
      requestBody:
        required: true
        description: A JSON object containing the login and password.
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/LoginRequest"
      security: [] # no authentication
      responses:
        "200":
          description: >
            Successfully authenticated.
            The session ID is returned in a cookie named `JSESSIONID`. You need to include this cookie in subsequent requests.
          headers:
            Set-Cookie:
              schema:
                type: string
                example: JSESSIONID=abcde12345; Path=/; HttpOnly
```

TITLE: Embed Swagger UI via unpkg CDN with StandalonePreset
DESCRIPTION: This HTML example shows how to embed Swagger UI using unpkg, specifically incorporating the 'swagger-ui-standalone-preset.js'. This preset enables additional UI components like the TopBar and ValidatorBadge, providing a more feature-rich interface.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/installation.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: html
CODE:
```
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">
  <head>
    <meta charset="utf-8" />
    <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1" />
    <meta name="description" content="SwaggerUI" />
    <title>SwaggerUI</title>
    <link rel="stylesheet" href="https://unpkg.com/swagger-ui-dist@5.11.0/swagger-ui.css" />
  </head>
  <body>
  <div id="swagger-ui"></div>
  <script src="https://unpkg.com/swagger-ui-dist@5.11.0/swagger-ui-bundle.js" crossorigin></script>
  <script src="https://unpkg.com/swagger-ui-dist@5.11.0/swagger-ui-standalone-preset.js" crossorigin></script>
  <script>
    window.onload = () => {
      window.ui = SwaggerUIBundle({
        url: 'https://petstore3.swagger.io/api/v3/openapi.json',
        dom_id: '#swagger-ui',
        presets: [
          SwaggerUIBundle.presets.apis,
          SwaggerUIStandalonePreset
        ],
        layout: "StandaloneLayout",
      });
    };
  </script>
  </body>
</html>
```

TITLE: Ensure Discriminator Property is Required in OpenAPI 3.0 Schemas
DESCRIPTION: This snippet emphasizes that schemas referenced by a `discriminator` must include and require the property specified by the discriminator's `propertyName`. It ensures that `simpleObject` and `complexObject` both have the `objectType` property, which is crucial for the discriminator to function correctly.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/inheritance-and-polymorphism.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
schemas:
    simpleObject:
      type: object
      required:
        - objectType
      properties:
        objectType:
          type: string
      …
    complexObject:
      type: object
      required:
        - objectType
      properties:
        objectType:
          type: string
      …
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Boolean Type Definition
DESCRIPTION: Defines the `type: boolean` in OpenAPI, representing `true` and `false` values. It clarifies that truthy/falsy values like empty strings or zero are not considered boolean.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Boolean Type Definition:
  type: boolean
  Values: true, false
  Note: Truthy/falsy values (e.g., "", 0, null) are not considered boolean.
```
