TITLE: Swagger Runtime Expressions and Evaluation Results
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates various runtime expressions used in Swagger/OpenAPI, showing how they evaluate to specific values based on request and response data. Includes examples for accessing URL, method, status code, headers, and JSON body elements using JSON Pointer syntax.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Expression: $url
Result: http://api.example.com/users?limit=2&total=true
Comments: Accesses the full request URL.

Expression: $method
Result: GET
Comments: Retrieves the HTTP method of the request.

Expression: $request.query.total
Result: true
Comments: Accesses a specific query parameter. 'total' must be defined as a query parameter.

Expression: $statusCode
Result: 200
Comments: Retrieves the HTTP status code of the response.

Expression: $response.header.x-total-count
Result: 37
Comments: Accesses a specific response header. Assuming 'X-Total-Count' is defined as a response header. Header names are case-insensitive.

Expression: $response.body#/next_offset
Result: 2
Comments: Uses JSON Pointer to access a property within the response body.

Expression: $response.body#/users/0
Result: {"id": 1, "name": "Alice"}
Comments: Uses JSON Pointer with 0-based indexes to access array elements. No wildcard syntax (e.g., '$response.body#/users/*/id') is valid.

Expression: $response.body#/users/1
Result: {"id": 2, "name": "Bob"}
Comments: Accesses the second element of the 'users' array.

Expression: $response.body#/users/1/name
Result: Bob
Comments: Accesses a nested property within an array element.

Expression: ID_{$response.body#/users/1/id}
Result: ID_2
Comments: Demonstrates embedding an expression within a string.
```

TITLE: Using Relative URLs for OAuth 2.0 Endpoints in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define `authorizationUrl` and `tokenUrl` as relative paths within an OAuth 2.0 `authorizationCode` flow in OpenAPI 3.0, which are then resolved against the `servers` URL.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
servers:
  - url: https://api.example.com/v2

components:
  securitySchemes:
    oauth2sample:
      type: oauth2
      flows:
        authorizationCode:
          authorizationUrl: /oauth/authorize # <-----
          tokenUrl: /oauth/token # <-----
          scopes: ...
```

TITLE: Enum with Item Descriptions in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to provide detailed descriptions for individual enum values within the `description` field of a parameter in OpenAPI 3.0. It clarifies the meaning of `asc` and `desc` options for a `sort` query parameter.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/enums.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: sort
    schema:
      type: string
      enum: [asc, desc]
    description: >
      Sort order:
       * `asc` - Ascending, from A to Z
       * `desc` - Descending, from Z to A
```

TITLE: Define a Dictionary Schema with Referenced Values in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 example demonstrates defining a dictionary (`Messages`) where the values are references to another schema (`Message`). This promotes reusability and modularity by defining the structure of the dictionary values separately.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/dictionaries.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    Messages: # <---- dictionary
      type: object
      additionalProperties:
        $ref: "#/components/schemas/Message"

    Message:
      type: object
      properties:
        code:
          type: integer
        text:
          type: string
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Documenting Parameter Dependencies in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to document complex parameter dependencies in OpenAPI 3.0, which lacks native support for such features. It shows how to describe mutually exclusive parameters (e.g., `rdate` vs. `start_date` and `end_date` for a report endpoint) within parameter descriptions and define a `400 Bad Request` response to indicate required parameter combinations.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_24

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
paths:
  /report:
    get:
      parameters:
        - name: rdate
          in: query
          schema:
            type: string
          description: >
            A relative date range for the report, such as `Today` or `LastWeek`.
            For an exact range, use `start_date` and `end_date` instead.
        - name: start_date
          in: query
          schema:
            type: string
            format: date
          description: >
            The start date for the report. Must be used together with `end_date`.
            This parameter is incompatible with `rdate`.
        - name: end_date
          in: query
          schema:
            type: string
            format: date
          description: >
            The end date for the report. Must be used together with `start_date`.
            This parameter is incompatible with `rdate`.
      responses:
        "400":
          description: Either `rdate` or `start_date`+`end_date` are required.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Specifying Parameter Examples in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to provide single and multiple named examples for parameters in an OpenAPI specification. Examples help document expected input values and can be used by tools for mock data generation or testing.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_20

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: limit
    schema:
      type: integer
      minimum: 1
    example: 20
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: ids
    description: One or more IDs
    required: true
    schema:
      type: array
      items:
        type: integer
    style: form
    explode: false
    examples:
      oneId:
        summary: Example of a single ID
        value: [5] # ?ids=5
      multipleIds:
        summary: Example of multiple IDs
        value: [1, 5, 7] # ?ids=1,5,7
```

TITLE: OpenAPI OAuth 2.0 Flow FAQ
DESCRIPTION: Addresses common questions regarding the definition of `authorizationUrl` and `tokenUrl` in OpenAPI OAuth 2.0 security schemes, clarifying their role and parameter inclusion.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Question: Should I additionally define `authorizationUrl` and `tokenUrl` as API operations?
Answer:
  - `authorizationUrl` is not an API endpoint but a special web page that requires user input. It cannot be described using OpenAPI.
  - `tokenUrl` can be described if needed.

Question: Should `authorizationUrl` and `tokenUrl` include query string parameters, such as `grant_type`, `client_id` and others?
Answer:
  - The OpenAPI Specification does not state this, so it is up to you and the tools you use.
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Query Parameter Serialization Styles
DESCRIPTION: Documents the supported 'style' values for query parameters in OpenAPI, including 'form', 'spaceDelimited', 'pipeDelimited', and 'deepObject'. It illustrates how 'explode' affects array and object serialization and explains the 'allowReserved' keyword for special characters.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/serialization.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Query parameters support the following `style` values:

- **form** – (default) ampersand-separated values, also known as form-style query expansion. Corresponds to the `{?param_name}` URI template.
- **spaceDelimited** – space-separated array values. Same as `collectionFormat: ssv` in OpenAPI 2.0. Has effect only for non-exploded arrays (`explode: false`), that is, the space separates the array values if the array is a _single parameter_, as in `arr=a b c`.
- **pipeDelimited** – pipeline-separated array values. Same as `collectionFormat: pipes` in OpenAPI 2.0. Has effect only for non-exploded arrays (`explode: false`), that is, the pipe separates the array values if the array is a _single parameter_, as in `arr=a|b|c`.
- **deepObject** – simple non-nested objects are serialized as `paramName[prop1]=value1&paramName[prop2]=value2&...`. The behavior for nested objects and arrays is undefined.

The default serialization method is `style: form` and `explode: true`. This corresponds to `collectionFormat: multi` from OpenAPI 2.0. Given the path `/users` with a query parameter `id`, the query string is serialized as follows:

| style          | explode | URI template  | Primitive value id = 5 | Array id = [3, 4, 5]  | Object id = {"role": "admin", "firstName": "Alex"} |
| -------------- | ------- | ------------- | ---------------------- | --------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- |
| form *         | true *  | /users{?id*}  | /users?id=5            | /users?id=3&id=4&id=5 | /users?role=admin&firstName=Alex                   |
| form           | false   | /users{?id}   | /users?id=5            | /users?id=3,4,5       | /users?id=role,admin,firstName,Alex                |
| spaceDelimited | true    | /users{?id*}  | n/a                    | /users?id=3&id=4&id=5 | n/a                                                |
| spaceDelimited | false   | n/a           | n/a                    | /users?id=3%204%205   | n/a                                                |
| pipeDelimited  | true    | /users{?id*}  | n/a                    | /users?id=3&id=4&id=5 | n/a                                                |
| pipeDelimited  | false   | n/a           | n/a                    | /users?id=3\|4\|5     | n/a                                                |
| deepObject     | true    | n/a           | n/a                    | n/a                   | /users?id[role]=admin&id[firstName]=Alex           |

* Default serialization method

Additionally, the `allowReserved` keyword specifies whether the reserved characters `:/?#[]@!$&'()*+,;=` in parameter values are allowed to be sent as they are, or should be percent-encoded. By default, `allowReserved` is `false`, and reserved characters are percent-encoded. For example, `/` is encoded as `%2F` (or `%2f`), so that the parameter value `quotes/h2g2.txt` will be sent as `quotes%2Fh2g2.txt`.
```

TITLE: Initialize SwaggerUI in Standalone Mode with JavaScript
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript snippet demonstrates how to set up SwaggerUI in standalone mode. It imports necessary modules like `swagger-ui` and `swagger-ui-standalone-preset`, along with various `swagger-editor` plugins, to display an API definition from a URL with a `TopBar` for dynamic loading.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_25

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
import SwaggerUI from 'swagger-ui';
import SwaggerUIStandalonePreset from 'swagger-ui/dist/swagger-ui-standalone-preset';
import 'swagger-ui/dist/swagger-ui.css';
import 'swagger-editor/swagger-editor.css';
import EditorContentTypePlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-content-type';
import EditorPreviewAsyncAPIPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-asyncapi';
import EditorPreviewAPIDesignSystemsPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-api-design-systems';
import SwaggerUIAdapterPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/swagger-ui-adapter';

SwaggerUI({
  url: 'https://petstore.swagger.io/v2/swagger.json',
  dom_id: '#swagger-ui',
  presets: [SwaggerUI.presets.apis, SwaggerUIStandalonePreset],
  plugins: [
    EditorContentTypePlugin,
    EditorPreviewAsyncAPIPlugin,
    EditorPreviewAPIDesignSystemsPlugin,
    SwaggerUIAdapterPlugin,
    SwaggerUI.plugins.DownloadUrl,
  ],
  layout: 'StandaloneLayout',
});
```

TITLE: Define Custom Header Parameter in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0 YAML snippet defines a 'GET /ping' operation that requires an 'X-Request-ID' header. It specifies the header's type as string with UUID format and marks it as required, demonstrating how to document custom request headers in an API specification.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /ping:
    get:
      summary: Checks if the server is alive
      parameters:
        - in: header
          name: X-Request-ID
          schema:
            type: string
            format: uuid
          required: true
```

TITLE: Augment Default Swagger UI Layout with Custom Header
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to build upon the default `BaseLayout` in Swagger UI by creating a custom React component, `AugmentingLayout`. It demonstrates how to pull in and render the `BaseLayout` within a custom wrapper, adding elements like a custom header, and then configuring Swagger UI to use this augmented layout. This approach allows for adding custom UI elements while retaining the core Swagger UI functionality.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/custom-layout.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
import React from "react"

// Create the layout component
class AugmentingLayout extends React.Component {
  render() {
    const {
      getComponent
    } = this.props

    const BaseLayout = getComponent("BaseLayout", true)

    return (
      <div>
        <div className="myCustomHeader">
          <h1>I have a custom header above Swagger-UI!</h1>
        </div>
        <BaseLayout />
      </div>
    )
  }
}

// Create the plugin that provides our layout component
const AugmentingLayoutPlugin = () => {
  return {
    components: {
      AugmentingLayout: AugmentingLayout
    }
  }
}

// Provide the plugin to Swagger-UI, and select AugmentingLayout
// as the layout for Swagger-UI
SwaggerUI({
  url: "https://petstore.swagger.io/v2/swagger.json",
  plugins: [ AugmentingLayoutPlugin ],
  layout: "AugmentingLayout"
})
```

TITLE: Apply OpenID Connect Security Per Operation in OpenAPI 3.0

```
paths:
  /pets/{petId}:
    get:
      summary: Get a pet by ID
      security:
        - openId:
          - pets_read
      ...

    delete:
      summary: Delete a pet by ID
      security:
        - openId:
          - pets_write
      ...
```

TITLE: Define Alternate Response Schemas with oneOf/anyOf in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates using `oneOf` (or `anyOf`) to specify that a response body can conform to one of several predefined schemas, allowing for polymorphic responses.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
responses:
  "200":
    description: A JSON object containing pet information
    content:
      application/json:
        schema:
          oneOf:
            - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Cat"
            - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Dog"
            - $ref: "#/components/schemas/Hamster"
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Definition for Report Endpoint Parameter Dependencies
DESCRIPTION: Defines the `/report` GET endpoint in OpenAPI (YAML format), illustrating how to document mutually exclusive parameters (`rdate` vs `start_date`/`end_date`) using parameter descriptions and a 400 Bad Request response to indicate validation rules. This snippet addresses the lack of direct parameter dependency support in Swagger/OpenAPI by providing documentation guidelines.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_25

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
paths:
  /report:
    get:
      parameters:
        - name: rdate
          in: query
          type: string
          description: >
            A relative date range for the report, such as `Today` or `LastWeek`.
            For an exact range, use `start_date` and `end_date` instead.
        - name: start_date
          in: query
          type: string
          format: date
          description: >
            The start date for the report. Must be used together with `end_date`.
            This parameter is incompatible with `rdate`.
        - name: end_date
          in: query
          type: string
          format: date
          description: >
            The end date for the report. Must be used together with `start_date`.
            This parameter is incompatible with `rdate`.
      responses:
        400:
          description: Either `rdate` or `start_date`+`end_date` are required.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI Request Body Examples (Multiple with $ref)
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to provide multiple examples for a request body when the `schema` uses a `$ref`. Similar to single examples with `$ref`, the `examples` keyword is a child of the media type. It shows two distinct user examples, "Jessica" and "Ron".
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    post:
      summary: Adds a new user
      requestBody:
        content:
          application/json: # Media type
            schema: # Request body contents
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/User" # Reference to an object
            examples: # Child of media type
              Jessica: # Example 1
                value:
                  id: 10
                  name: Jessica Smith
              Ron: # Example 2
                value:
                  id: 11
                  name: Ron Stewart
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Configure Relative OpenID Connect Discovery URL in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define an `openIdConnect` security scheme with a relative `openIdConnectUrl` in OpenAPI 3.0, which will be resolved against the base server URL defined in the `servers` section.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/openid-connect-discovery.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    openId:
      type: openIdConnect
      openIdConnectUrl: /.well-known/openid-configuration
```

TITLE: Define Query Parameter with Content for Complex Serialization in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Explains using the `content` keyword for complex serialization scenarios not covered by `style` and `explode`, such as sending a JSON string in a query parameter. It shows how to wrap the parameter schema into `content/<media-type>` for a `filter` parameter with `application/json` media type.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_15

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: filter

    # Wrap 'schema' into 'content.<media-type>'
    content:
      application/json: # <---- media type indicates how to serialize / deserialize the parameter content
        schema:
          type: object
          properties:
            type:
              type: string
            color:
              type: string
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Error Schema Definition
DESCRIPTION: This API documentation snippet defines a reusable schema for generic error responses within an OpenAPI specification. It specifies that an error object will contain a 'code' (string) and a 'message' (string), both of which are required fields, ensuring consistent error reporting.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Error:
  type: object
  properties:
    code:
      type: string
    message:
      type: string
  required:
    - code
    - message
```

TITLE: Overriding Operation-Level Security in OpenAPI 2.0 (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates how to override global security settings for individual API operations within the `paths` section. It demonstrates applying a different OAuth2 scope for the `/billing_info` GET operation and explicitly disabling security for the `/ping` GET endpoint, showcasing fine-grained control over authentication requirements.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/authentication.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
/billing_info:
  get:
    summary: Gets the account billing info
    security:
      - OAuth2: [admin]   # Use OAuth with a different scope
    responses:
      200:
        description: OK
      401:
        description: Not authenticated
      403:
        description: Access token does not have the required scope

/ping:
  get:
    summary: Checks if the server is running
    security: []   # No security
    responses:
      200:
        description: Server is up and running
      default:
        description: Something is wrong
```

TITLE: Applying Global Security Requirements in OpenAPI 2.0 (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet shows how to apply previously defined security schemes globally to all API operations using the `security` keyword at the root level. It specifies that API calls can be authenticated using either an API key or OAuth 2 with 'read' and 'write' scopes, acting as a default for the entire API.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/authentication.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
security:
  - ApiKeyAuth: []
  - OAuth2: [read, write]
```

TITLE: Define Custom Response Headers in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define custom response headers within an OpenAPI 3.0 specification, including their schema and description, for a specific HTTP response code.

```
              schema:
                type: integer
              description: Request limit per hour.

              schema:
                type: integer
              description: The number of requests left for the time window.

              schema:
                type: string
                format: date-time
              description: The UTC date/time at which the current rate limit window resets.
```

TITLE: Define Custom Headers for Multipart Part in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI specification snippet demonstrates how to define custom headers for a specific part (e.g., `profileImage`) within a `multipart/form-data` request body. It utilizes the `encoding` field to specify `contentType` and `headers` for the `profileImage` property, including a `X-Custom-Header` with its description and schema.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/multipart-requests.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
requestBody:
  content:
    multipart/form-data:
      schema:
        type: object
        properties:
          id:
            type: string
            format: uuid
          profileImage:
            type: string
            format: binary
      encoding:
        profileImage: # Property name
          contentType: image/png, image/jpeg
          headers: # Custom headers
            X-Custom-Header:
              description: This is a custom header
              schema:
                type: string
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Use Wildcard Media Types in OpenAPI Responses
DESCRIPTION: This snippet shows how to use wildcard placeholders (e.g., `image/*`) to define a common data format for a range of media types in an OpenAPI response. This is useful when a server can return various specific types (like `image/png`, `image/jpeg`) that share the same underlying schema.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /info/logo:
    get:
      responses:
        "200": # Response
          description: OK
          content: # Response body
            image/*: # Media type
              schema:
                type: string
                format: binary
```

TITLE: Override Built-in Components with Wrap-Components Plugin (Functional)
DESCRIPTION: The `Wrap-Components` interface allows overriding registered components in the system. It uses a function factory signature `(OriginalComponent, system) => props => ReactElement` or `(OriginalComponent, system) => ReactClass`. This example demonstrates wrapping a built-in component (`info`) to add custom content above it.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_16

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const MyWrapBuiltinComponentPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    wrapComponents: {
      info: (Original, system) => (props) => {
        return <div>
          <h3>Hello world! I am above the Info component.</h3>
          <Original {...props} />
        </div>
      }
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Defining and Applying Paired API Keys (Logical AND)
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define two distinct API keys (`apiKey` and `appId`) and apply them together in the same array item within the `security` section. This configuration indicates that both keys are required for authentication (logical AND).
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/api-keys.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
securityDefinitions:
  apiKey:
    type: apiKey
    in: header
    name: X-API-KEY
  appId:
    type: apiKey
    in: header
    name: X-APP-ID
security:
  - apiKey: []
    appId: []
```

TITLE: Swagger 2.0 API Definition for Basic File Upload

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Schema for URL-Encoded Form Data
DESCRIPTION: Defines how `application/x-www-form-urlencoded` form fields are modeled in OpenAPI 3.0 using an `object` schema where properties correspond to form fields like 'name' and 'fav_number', with required fields specified.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /survey:
    post:
      requestBody:
        required: true
        content:
          application/x-www-form-urlencoded:
            schema:
              type: object
              properties:
                name: # <!--- form field name
                  type: string
                fav_number: # <!--- form field name
                  type: integer
              required:
                - name
                - email
```

TITLE: Define Common Path-Level Parameters in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to define parameters directly under a path. These parameters apply to all operations (GET, PATCH, DELETE) associated with that path, ensuring consistency for resources accessed via a path parameter like a user ID.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_20

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /user/{id}:
    parameters:
      - in: path
        name: id
        type: integer
        required: true
        description: The user ID.

    get:
      summary: Gets a user by ID.
      ...
    patch:
      summary: Updates an existing user with the specified ID.
      ...
    delete:
      summary: Deletes the user with the specified ID.
      ...
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Link Object Properties Reference
DESCRIPTION: This section details the key properties used within an OpenAPI Link Object, explaining their purpose and usage for defining relationships between API operations. It covers how to specify target operations, pass parameters, define server overrides, and add descriptive text to links.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Link Object Properties:
  operationId: string
    Description: Specifies the target operation by its operationId. Used for local links only, resolved within the current API specification.
  operationRef: string
    Description: Specifies the target operation by a relative or absolute URL. Can link to both local and external operations.
  parameters: object (map of string to string)
    Description: A map of parameter names to runtime expressions that extract values from the parent operation's response or request body to pass to the target operation.
    Example: userId: "$response.body#/id"
  requestBody: any
    Description: A literal value or a runtime expression that extracts a value from the parent operation's response or request body to be used as the request body of the target operation.
  server: Server Object
    Description: An alternative server object that the target operation should use, if different from the default servers.
  description: string
    Description: A verbose explanation of this link's purpose. Supports CommonMark syntax for rich text representation.
```

TITLE: Configure and Implement Custom Node.js Request Snippet Generator for SwaggerUI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to enable request snippets in SwaggerUI and provide a custom generator using the plugin API. It includes a configuration object (`snippetConfig`) to activate snippets and define a new 'node_native' generator, along with the `SnippedGeneratorNodeJsPlugin` which contains the `requestSnippetGenerator_node_native` function. This function takes an internal request object and transforms it into a Node.js native HTTP request code snippet, handling various request properties like method, URL, headers, and body. It also shows how to integrate this custom plugin into the `SwaggerUIBundle` initialization.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plug-points.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
// Add config to Request Snippets Configuration with an unique key like "node_native" 
const snippetConfig = {
  requestSnippetsEnabled: true,
  requestSnippets: {
    generators: {
      "node_native": {
        title: "NodeJs Native",
        syntax: "javascript"
      }
    }
  }
}

const SnippedGeneratorNodeJsPlugin = {
  fn: {
    // use `requestSnippetGenerator_` + key from config (node_native) for generator fn
    requestSnippetGenerator_node_native: (request) => {
      const url = new Url(request.get("url"))
      let isMultipartFormDataRequest = false
      const headers = request.get("headers")
      if(headers && headers.size) {
        request.get("headers").map((val, key) => {
          isMultipartFormDataRequest = isMultipartFormDataRequest || /^content-type$/i.test(key) && /^multipart\/form-data$/i.test(val)
        })
      }
      const packageStr = url.protocol === "https:" ? "https" : "http"
      let reqBody = request.get("body")
      if (request.get("body")) {
        if (isMultipartFormDataRequest && ["POST", "PUT", "PATCH"].includes(request.get("method"))) {
          return "throw new Error(\"Currently unsupported content-type: /^multipart\\/form-data$/i\");"
        } else {
          if (!Map.isMap(reqBody)) {
            if (typeof reqBody !== "string") {
              reqBody = JSON.stringify(reqBody)
            }
          } else {
            reqBody = getStringBodyOfMap(request)
          }
        }
      } else if (!request.get("body") && request.get("method") === "POST") {
        reqBody = ""
      }

      const stringBody = "`" + (reqBody || "")
          .replace(/\\n/g, "\n")
          .replace(/`/g, "\\`")
        + "`"

      return `const http = require("${packageStr}");
const options = {
  "method": "${request.get("method")}",
  "hostname": "${url.host}",
  "port": ${url.port || "null"},
  "path": "${url.pathname}"${headers && headers.size ? `,
  "headers": {
    ${request.get("headers").map((val, key) => `"${key}": "${val}"`).valueSeq().join(",\n    ")}
  }` : ""}
};
const req = http.request(options, function (res) {
  const chunks = [];
  res.on("data", function (chunk) {
    chunks.push(chunk);
  });
  res.on("end", function () {
    const body = Buffer.concat(chunks);
    console.log(body.toString());
  });
});
${reqBody ? `\nreq.write(${stringBody});` : ""}
req.end();`
    }
  }
}

const ui = SwaggerUIBundle({
  "dom_id": "#swagger-ui",
  deepLinking: true,
  presets: [
    SwaggerUIBundle.presets.apis,
    SwaggerUIStandalonePreset
  ],
  plugins: [
    SwaggerUIBundle.plugins.DownloadUrl,
    SnippedGeneratorNodeJsPlugin
  ],
  layout: "StandaloneLayout",
  validatorUrl: "https://validator.swagger.io/validator",
  url: "https://petstore.swagger.io/v2/swagger.json",
  ...snippetConfig,
})
```

TITLE: Referencing External Examples in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Details how to link to external example values using the `externalValue` keyword in OpenAPI, useful for examples that are not YAML or JSON conformant, such as binary files or large JSON objects hosted externally.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
content:
  application/json:
    schema:
      $ref: "#/components/schemas/MyObject"
    examples:
      jsonObject:
        summary: A sample object
        externalValue: "http://example.com/examples/object-example.json"
  application/pdf:
    schema:
      type: string
      format: binary
    examples:
      sampleFile:
        summary: A sample file
        externalValue: "http://example.com/examples/example.pdf"
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Header Parameter Serialization Styles
DESCRIPTION: Explains that header parameters always use the 'simple' style in OpenAPI. It demonstrates how the optional 'explode' keyword influences the serialization of object values in HTTP headers.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/serialization.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Header parameters always use the `simple` style, that is, comma-separated values. This corresponds to the `{param_name}` URI template. An optional `explode` keyword controls the object serialization. Given the request header named `X-MyHeader`, the header value is serialized as follows:

| style     | explode  | URI template | Primitive value X-MyHeader = 5 | Array X-MyHeader = [3, 4, 5] | Object X-MyHeader = {"role": "admin", "firstName": "Alex"} |
| --------- | -------- | ------------ | ------------------------------ | ---------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------- |
| simple *  | false *  | {id}         | X-MyHeader: 5                  | X-MyHeader: 3,4,5            | X-MyHeader: role,admin,firstName,Alex                      |
| simple    | true     | {id*}        | X-MyHeader: 5                  | X-MyHeader: 3,4,5            | X-MyHeader: role=admin,firstName=Alex                      |

- Default serialization method
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define and Reuse OpenAPI Links in YAML
DESCRIPTION: This YAML example illustrates how to define a reusable link, `GetUserByUserId`, in the `components/links` section. This link describes how to use the `id` from a response body (e.g., from `createUser` or `updateUser`) as the `userId` parameter for the `getUser` operation. The `post` and `patch` operations then reference this shared link definition using `$ref` to avoid duplicating the link logic, demonstrating efficient link management in OpenAPI.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    post:
      summary: Create a user
      operationId: createUser
      ...
      responses:
        '201':
          description: Created
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                type: object
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                    format: int64
                    description: ID of the created user.
          links:
            GetUserByUserId:
              $ref: '#/components/links/GetUserByUserId'    # <-------

  /user/{userId}:
    patch:
      summary: Update user
      operationId: updateUser
      ...
      responses:
        '200':
          description: The updated user object
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                $ref: '#/components/schemas/User'
          links:
            GetUserByUserId:
              $ref: '#/components/links/GetUserByUserId'    # <-------

    get:
      summary: Get a user by ID
      operationId: getUser
      ...

components:
  links:
    GetUserByUserId:   # <----- The $ref's above point here
      description: >
        The `id` value returned in the response can be used as
        the `userId` parameter in `GET /users/{userId}`.
      operationId: getUser
      parameters:
        userId: '$response.body#/id'
```

TITLE: Overriding SwaggerUI componentDidCatch for Custom Error Handling
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to create a new SwaggerUI plugin to override the default `componentDidCatch` behavior, allowing integration with custom error reporting services like Bugsnag for centralized error logging.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plug-points.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
const BugsnagErrorHandlerPlugin = () => {
  // init bugsnag

  return {
    fn: {
      componentDidCatch = (error, info) => {
        Bugsnag.notify(error);
        Bugsnag.notify(info);
      },
    },
  };
};
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Schema with `not` Keyword for Type Exclusion
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to use the `not` keyword within an OpenAPI schema to enforce that a property, `pet_type`, must *not* be an integer. This ensures that only non-integer values (e.g., strings, booleans, objects) are accepted for this field in the request body.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/oneof-anyof-allof-not.md#_snippet_11

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /pets:
    patch:
      requestBody:
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/PetByType"
      responses:
        "200":
          description: Updated

components:
  schemas:
    PetByType:
      type: object
      properties:
        pet_type:
          not:
            type: integer
      required:
        - pet_type
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Specification for Slack Incoming Webhook with Complex Form Data Serialization
DESCRIPTION: This OpenAPI 3.0.4 specification demonstrates how to define an API endpoint for a Slack incoming webhook, specifically addressing complex serialization where JSON data is sent within a form field (`payload`). It uses the `contentType: application/json` within the `encoding` object to specify the media type for the `payload` field, allowing both direct JSON and form-urlencoded JSON messages.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
openapi: 3.0.4
info:
  version: 1.0.0
  title: Slack Incoming Webhook
externalDocs:
  url: https://api.slack.com/incoming-webhooks

servers:
  - url: https://hooks.slack.com

paths:
  /services/T00000000/B00000000/XXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXXX:
    post:
      summary: Post a message to Slack
      requestBody:
        content:
          application/json:
            schema:
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/Message"

          application/x-www-form-urlencoded:
            schema:
              type: object
              properties:
                payload: # <--- form field that contains the JSON message
                  $ref: "#/components/schemas/Message"
            encoding:
              payload:
                contentType: application/json

      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK

components:
  schemas:
    Message:
      title: A Slack message
      type: object
      properties:
        text:
          type: string
          description: Message text
      required:
        - text
```

TITLE: Combine Path and Operation-Level Parameters in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how operation-level parameters are used in conjunction with path-level parameters. It shows how to add an additional query parameter ('metadata') to a GET operation, while the path parameter ('id') is inherited from the path definition.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_21

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{id}:
    parameters:
      - in: path
        name: id
        type: integer
        required: true
        description: The user ID.

    # GET/users/{id}?metadata=true
    get:
      summary: Gets a user by ID.
      # Note we only define the query parameter, because the {id} is defined at the path level.
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: metadata
          type: boolean
          required: false
          description: If true, the endpoint returns only the user metadata.
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:

```
type: string
enum:
  - asc
  - desc
description: >
  Sort order:
   * asc - Ascending, from A to Z.
   * desc - Descending, from Z to A.
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Runtime Expression Reference
DESCRIPTION: A comprehensive list of available runtime expressions in OpenAPI, detailing how to reference various parts of the request and response, such as URL, method, path, query parameters, headers, and body fields. Each expression includes an example and a description of its purpose.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/callbacks.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Runtime Expressions:
  {$url}:
    Example: /subscribe
    Description: The parent operation URL.
  {$method}:
    Example: POST
    Description: The method of the callback request.
  {$request.path.eventType}:
    Example: myEvent
    Description: The event name.
  {$request.query.param-name}:
    Example: query-param-value (the p1 query parameter)
    Description: The value of the specified query parameter.
  {$request.header.header-name}:
    Example: application/json (the Content-Type header)
    Description: The specified header of the “subscription” request.
  {$request.body#/field-name}:
    Example: callbackUrl
    Description: A field in the request body. If the field is an array, use the syntax like {$request.body#/arrayField/2}.
  {$response.header.header-name}:
    Example: http://my.example.com?id=123 (the Location header)
    Description: The value of the specified response header (the response to the “subscription” request).
```

TITLE: Define Ignore Rules with .swagger-codegen-ignore File
DESCRIPTION: This snippet provides examples of patterns used in a `.swagger-codegen-ignore` file, similar to `.gitignore`. This file allows users to specify individual files or directories to be excluded from generation or overwriting, offering more granular control than the `--skip-overwrite` flag. The file must reside in the root of the output directory.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/generation-selective.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
# Swagger Codegen Ignore
# Lines beginning with a # are comments

# This should match build.sh located anywhere.
build.sh

# Matches build.sh in the root
/build.sh

# Exclude all recursively
docs/**

# Explicitly allow files excluded by other rules
!docs/UserApi.md

# Recursively exclude directories named Api
# You can't negate files below this directory.
src/**/Api/

# When this file is nested under /Api (excluded above),
# this rule is ignored because parent directory is excluded by previous rule.
!src/**/PetApiTests.cs

# Exclude a single, nested file explicitly
src/IO.Swagger.Test/Model/AnimalFarmTests.cs
```

TITLE: Illustrating Logical Combinations for Security in OpenAPI 2.0 (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This conceptual YAML snippet explains the logical operators used within the `security` section of OpenAPI 2.0 for combining multiple authentication requirements. It clarifies that items within a hashmap are combined using logical AND (all must be met), while array items are combined using logical OR (any one can be used).
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/authentication.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
security:    # A OR B
  - A
  - B

security:    # A AND B
  - A
    B

security:    # (A AND B) OR (C AND D)
  - A
    B
  - C
    D
```

TITLE: Defining a 401 Unauthorized Response for API Keys

TITLE: OpenAPI Request Body Example (Media Type Child with $ref)
DESCRIPTION: Explains how to add a single example for a request body when the `schema` uses a `$ref` to an object defined in `components`. In this case, `example` must be a child of the media type (`application/json`) to avoid being overwritten by `$ref`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    post:
      summary: Adds a new user
      requestBody:
        content:
          application/json: # Media type
            schema: # Request body contents
              $ref: "#/components/schemas/User" # Reference to an object
            example: # Child of media type because we use $ref above
              # Properties of a referenced object
              id: 10
              name: Jessica Smith
      responses:
        "200":
          description: OK
```

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```

  - url: http://api.example.com
  - url: https://api.example.com
```

TITLE: Execute Logic After Plugin Registration with afterLoad
DESCRIPTION: The `afterLoad` plugin method provides a hook to execute logic after a plugin has been fully registered and its actions/selectors are bound into the system. This is useful for tasks requiring the plugin to be ready, such as fetching initial data or attaching bound actions as top-level methods for easier access.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_19

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const MyMethodProvidingPlugin = function() {
  return {
    afterLoad(system) {
      // at this point in time, your actions have been bound into the system
      // so you can do things with them
      this.rootInjects = this.rootInjects || {}
      this.rootInjects.myMethod = system.exampleActions.updateFavoriteColor
    },
    statePlugins: {
      example: {
        actions: {
          updateFavoriteColor: (str) => {
            return {
              type: "EXAMPLE_SET_FAV_COLOR",
              payload: str
            }
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Configure OpenAPI OAuth 2.0 Resource Owner Password Flow
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define the OAuth 2.0 Resource Owner Password flow within an OpenAPI `securitySchemes` component. This flow primarily uses `tokenUrl` and an optional `refreshUrl`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Authentication/oauth2.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    oAuth2Password:
      type: oauth2
      description: See https://developers.getbase.com/docs/rest/articles/oauth2/requests
      flows:
        password:
          tokenUrl: https://api.getbase.com/oauth2/token
          scopes:
            read: Grant read-only access to all your data except for the account and user info
            write: Grant write-only access to all your data except for the account and user info
            profile: Grant read-only access to the account and user info only
```

TITLE: Generate Specific Components with Swagger Codegen CLI

SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/generation-selective.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
# generate only models
java -Dmodels {opts}

# generate only apis
java -Dapis {opts}

# generate only supporting files
java -DsupportingFiles

# generate models and supporting files
java -Dmodels -DsupportingFiles
```

TITLE: HTML Example for SwaggerEditor UMD Bundle Usage
DESCRIPTION: This HTML snippet demonstrates how to integrate and initialize SwaggerEditor using its UMD bundle. It includes React and ReactDOM from CDNs and then mounts the SwaggerEditor component into a designated DOM element.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_19

LANGUAGE: HTML
CODE:
```
<!DOCTYPE html>
<html lang="en">

  <meta charset="utf-8" />
  <meta name="viewport" content="width=device-width, initial-scale=1" />
  <meta
    name="description"
    content="SwaggerEditor"
  />
  <title>SwaggerEditor</title>
  <link rel="stylesheet" href="./swagger-editor.css" />
</head>
<body>
  <div id="swagger-editor"></div>
  <script src="https://unpkg.com/react@18/umd/react.production.min.js" crossorigin></script>

  <script>
    const props = {
      url: 'https://raw.githubusercontent.com/asyncapi/spec/v2.2.0/examples/streetlights-kafka.yml',
    };
    const element = React.createElement(SwaggerEditor, props);

    ReactDOM.render(element, domContainer);
  </script>
</body>
</html>
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Exclusive Minimum and Maximum Keywords
DESCRIPTION: This API documentation explains the behavior of `exclusiveMinimum` and `exclusiveMaximum` keywords in OpenAPI. When set to `true`, the corresponding boundary value is excluded from the valid range.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/data-types.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
exclusiveMinimum: false or not included
  description: value ≥ minimum
exclusiveMinimum: true
  description: value > minimum
exclusiveMaximum: false or not included
  description: value ≤ maximum
exclusiveMaximum: true
  description: value < maximum
```

TITLE: Add XML Prefixes and Namespaces in OpenAPI Schema
DESCRIPTION: Explains how to define XML namespaces and prefixes for elements within an OpenAPI 3.0 schema using the `xml/prefix` and `xml/namespace` properties to avoid naming conflicts.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/representing-xml.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
xml:
  prefix: "smp"
  namespace: "http://example.com/schema"
```

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
book:
  type: object
  properties:
    id:
      type: integer
    title:
      type: string
    author:
      type: string
  xml:
    prefix: "smp"
    namespace: "http://example.com/schema"
```

LANGUAGE: XML
CODE:
```
<smp:book xmlns:smp="http://example.com/schema">
  <id>0</id>
  <title>string</title>
  <author>string</author>
</smp:book>
```

TITLE: Swagger UI JSON Schema Component Mapping
DESCRIPTION: Swagger UI internally maps OpenAPI Specification schema information to specific JSON Schema components for rendering inputs. This mapping follows a hierarchical lookup based on schema type and format, allowing for custom input components or overriding existing ones.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plug-points.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Mapping Logic:

1. If format defined:
   `JsonSchema_${type}_${format}`

2. Fallback if `JsonSchema_${type}_${format}` component does not exist or format not defined:
   `JsonSchema_${type}`

3. Default fallback:
   `JsonSchema_string`
```

TITLE: Defining Multiple Callbacks in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: An OpenAPI YAML definition demonstrating how to specify multiple distinct callbacks (e.g., for in-progress, failed, and success states) within a single `/subscribe` operation, each with its own dynamic URL derived from the request body.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/callbacks.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
/subscribe:
  post:
    requestBody:
      content:
        application/json:
          schema:
            type: object
            properties:
              inProgressUrl:
                type: string
              failedUrl:
                type: string
              successUrl:
                type: string
    responses:
      "200":
        description: OK
    callbacks:
      inProgress:
        "{$request.body#/inProgressUrl}":
          post:
            requestBody:
              $ref: "#/components/requestBodies/callbackMessage1"
            responses:
              "200":
                description: OK
        "{$request.body#/failedUrl}":
          post:
            requestBody:
              $ref: "#/components/requestBodies/callbackMessage2"
            responses:
              "200":
                description: OK
        "{$request.body#/successUrl}":
          post:
            requestBody:
              $ref: "#/components/requestBodies/callbackMessage3"
            responses:
              "200":
                description: OK
```

TITLE: Swagger Generator Docker Image Environment Variables and Configuration
DESCRIPTION: This section details the environment variables accepted by the `swaggerapi/swagger-generator-v3` Docker image, used for configuring Java memory, HTTP port, and options for hiding specific languages. It also explains how to add custom generators by mounting a volume.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/docker.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Swagger Generator Docker Image Configuration:
  Environment Variables:
    JAVA_MEM: string
      Description: Sets the Java memory allocation for the container.
      Example: "1024m"
    HTTP_PORT: string
      Description: Sets the HTTP port for the web application.
      Example: "8080"
    HIDDEN_OPTIONS_PATH: string
      Description: Path to a YAML file defining languages to hide. Useful for attaching a volume.
      Example: "/data/hiddenOptions.yaml"
    HIDDEN_OPTIONS: string
      Description: Defines languages to hide as an environment variable.
      Format: "{category}:{language},{language}|{category}:{language},{language}"
      Categories: "clients", "servers", "clientsV3", "serversV3"
      Example: "servers:foo,bar|clientsV3:wtf,isthis"
  Custom Generators:
    Description: Supports custom generators by mounting a volume containing generator JARs to `/jetty_home/lib/shared`.
    Note: Up to version 3.0.20, `-v /{WHATEVER_DIR}:/jetty_home/lib/shared` is required even without custom generators.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Swagger UI Network Configuration Parameters
DESCRIPTION: Details parameters for configuring network-related behavior in Swagger UI, including OAuth redirection, request/response interception, curl options, and validation settings.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/configuration.md#_snippet_15

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter: oauth2RedirectUrl
  Docker variable: OAUTH2_REDIRECT_URL
  Description: String. OAuth redirect URL.

Parameter: requestInterceptor
  Docker variable: Unavailable
  Description: Function=(a => a). MUST be a function. Function to intercept remote definition, "Try it out", and OAuth 2.0 requests. Accepts one argument requestInterceptor(request) and must return the modified request, or a Promise that resolves to the modified request.

Parameter: request.curlOptions
  Docker variable: Unavailable
  Description: Array. If set, MUST be an array of command line options available to the `curl` command. This can be set on the mutated request in the `requestInterceptor` function. For example `request.curlOptions = ["-g", "--limit-rate 20k"]`

Parameter: responseInterceptor
  Docker variable: Unavailable
  Description: Function=(a => a). MUST be a function. Function to intercept remote definition, "Try it out", and OAuth 2.0 responses. Accepts one argument responseInterceptor(response) and must return the modified response, or a Promise that resolves to the modified response.

Parameter: showMutatedRequest
  Docker variable: SHOW_MUTATED_REQUEST
  Description: Boolean=true. If set to `true`, uses the mutated request returned from a requestInterceptor to produce the curl command in the UI, otherwise the request before the requestInterceptor was applied is used.

Parameter: supportedSubmitMethods
  Docker variable: SUPPORTED_SUBMIT_METHODS
  Description: Array=["get", "put", "post", "delete", "options", "head", "patch", "trace"]. List of HTTP methods that have the "Try it out" feature enabled. An empty array disables "Try it out" for all operations. This does not filter the operations from the display.

Parameter: validatorUrl
  Docker variable: VALIDATOR_URL
  Description: String="https://validator.swagger.io/validator" OR null. By default, Swagger UI attempts to validate specs against swagger.io's online validator. You can use this parameter to set a different validator URL, for example for locally deployed validators (Validator Badge). Setting it to either `none`, `127.0.0.1` or `localhost` will disable validation.

Parameter: withCredentials
  Docker variable: WITH_CREDENTIALS
  Description: Boolean=false. If set to `true`, enables passing credentials, as defined in the Fetch standard, in CORS requests that are sent by the browser. Note that Swagger UI cannot currently set cookies cross-domain (see swagger-js#1163) - as a result, you will have to rely on browser-supplied cookies (which this setting enables sending) that Swagger UI cannot control.
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Configure File Overwriting with .swagger-codegen-ignore Examples
DESCRIPTION: This snippet provides examples of patterns used in a `.swagger-codegen-ignore` file, which functions similarly to `.gitignore`. It allows users to specify individual files or directories to be excluded from or explicitly included in the code generation process, offering granular control over output.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v2/generators.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: text
CODE:
```
# Swagger Codegen Ignore
# Lines beginning with a # are comments

# This should match build.sh located anywhere.
build.sh

# Matches build.sh in the root
/build.sh

# Exclude all recursively
docs/**

# Explicitly allow files excluded by other rules
!docs/UserApi.md

# Recursively exclude directories named Api
# You can't negate files below this directory.
src/**/Api/

# When this file is nested under /Api (excluded above),
# this rule is ignored because parent directory is excluded by previous rule.
!src/**/PetApiTests.cs

# Exclude a single, nested file explicitly
src/IO.Swagger.Test/Model/AnimalFarmTests.cs
```

TITLE: Customize Swagger UI Operations Filter Function
DESCRIPTION: Override the default `fn.opsFilter` function in Swagger UI to implement custom filtering logic for tag names, such as a multiple-phrase filter. This allows for more flexible and advanced filtering beyond the standard behavior.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plug-points.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
const MultiplePhraseFilterPlugin = function() {
  return {
    fn: {
      opsFilter: (taggedOps, phrase) => {
        const phrases = phrase.split(", ")

        return taggedOps.filter((val, key) => {
          return phrases.some(item => key.indexOf(item) > -1)
        })
      }
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Defining API Key Security in OpenAPI 2.0
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define API key security schemes in the `securityDefinitions` section of an OpenAPI Specification v2 document. It specifies whether the key is passed `in: header` or `in: query` and defines its `name`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/api-keys.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
securityDefinitions:
  # X-API-Key: abcdef12345
  APIKeyHeader:
    type: apiKey
    in: header
    name: X-API-Key
  # /path?api_key=abcdef12345
  APIKeyQueryParam:
    type: apiKey
    in: query
    name: api_key
```

TITLE: Configure Multiple Model Import Mappings (Separate Arguments)
DESCRIPTION: This command-line argument shows an alternative way to specify multiple model import mappings by repeating the --import-mappings flag for each mapping. This method can improve readability for a large number of mappings.

TITLE: Correct Query Parameter Definition in Swagger/OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates the correct method for defining query parameters in Swagger/OpenAPI. Parameters should be specified within the 'parameters' section of an operation, with 'in: query' to indicate their type.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: role
          type: string
          enum: [user, poweruser, admin]
          required: false
```

TITLE: Customize Wrapped XML Array and Item Names in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to use `xml/wrapped` along with `xml/name` for both the array and its items to define distinct names for the wrapping element and the individual array items in the generated XML.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/representing-xml.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
books:
  type: array
  items:
    type: string
    xml:
      name: "item"
  xml:
    wrapped: true
    name: books-array
  example:
    - "one"
    - "two"
    - "three"
```

LANGUAGE: XML
CODE:
```
<books-array>
  <item>one</item>
  <item>two</item>
  <item>three</item>
</books-array>
```

TITLE: Generate Code via HTTP POST Request with Curl
DESCRIPTION: This `curl` command sends a POST request to a local Swagger Codegen API endpoint to generate server-side code (JAX-RS Jersey) from a specified OpenAPI specification URL. The generated code, packaged as a zip file, is saved to `result.zip`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/docker.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
curl -X POST \
           http://localhost:8080/api/generate \
           -H 'content-type: application/json' \
           -d '{
           "specURL" : "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/OAI/OpenAPI-Specification/master/examples/v3.0/petstore.yaml",
           "lang" : "jaxrs-jersey",
           "type" : "SERVER",
           "codegenVersion" : "V3"
         }' > result.zip
```

TITLE: Using Media Type Placeholders in OpenAPI Responses
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define a response body using a media type placeholder like 'image/*' in OpenAPI. This indicates that the server will use the same data structure for all matching media types, simplifying documentation for broad content categories.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/media-types.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /info/logo:
    get:
      responses:
        "200": # Response
          description: OK
          content: # Response body
            image/*: # Media type
              schema:
                type: string
                format: binary
```

TITLE: Swagger Codegen CLI `generate` Command API Reference
DESCRIPTION: Comprehensive API documentation for the `swagger-codegen-cli generate` command, detailing its syntax, available options, and their purposes for customizing code generation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v2/about.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
NAME
        swagger-codegen-cli generate - Generate code with chosen lang

SYNOPSIS
        swagger-codegen-cli generate
                [(-a <authorization> | --auth <authorization>)]
                [--additional-properties <additional properties>...]
                [--api-package <api package>] [--artifact-id <artifact id>]
                [--artifact-version <artifact version>]
                [(-c <configuration file> | --config <configuration file>)]
                [-D <system properties>...] [--git-repo-id <git repo id>]
                [--git-user-id <git user id>] [--group-id <group id>]
                [--http-user-agent <http user agent>]
                (-i <spec file> | --input-spec <spec file>)
                [--ignore-file-override <ignore file override location>]
                [--import-mappings <import mappings>...]
                [--instantiation-types <instantiation types>...]
                [--invoker-package <invoker package>]
                (-l <language> | --lang <language>)
                [--language-specific-primitives <language specific primitives>...]
                [--library <library>] [--model-name-prefix <model name prefix>]
                [--model-name-suffix <model name suffix>]
                [--model-package <model package>]
                [(-o <output directory> | --output <output directory>)]
                [--release-note <release note>] [--remove-operation-id-prefix]
                [--reserved-words-mappings <reserved word mappings>...]
                [(-s | --skip-overwrite)]
                [(-t <template directory> | --template-dir <template directory>)]
                [--type-mappings <type mappings>...] [(-v | --verbose)]

OPTIONS
        -a <authorization>, --auth <authorization>
            adds authorization headers when fetching the swagger definitions
            remotely. Pass in a URL-encoded string of name:header with a comma
            separating multiple values

...... (results omitted)

        -v, --verbose
            verbose mode
```

```
    -l go -o /gen/out/go-petstore -DpackageName=petstore # generates go client, outputs locally to ./out/go-petstore
```

TITLE: Wrap Custom Components with Functional and Class-based Approaches
DESCRIPTION: This example illustrates how to wrap a custom component (`NumberDisplay`) using both functional and class-based approaches with the `Wrap-Components` interface. It shows how to conditionally render additional UI based on component props, demonstrating the flexibility of component wrapping.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_17

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
/////  Overriding a component from a plugin

// Here's our normal, unmodified component.
const MyNumberDisplayPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    components: {
      NumberDisplay: ({ number }) => <span>{number}</span>
    }
  }
}

// Here's a component wrapper defined as a function.
const MyWrapComponentPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    wrapComponents: {
      NumberDisplay: (Original, system) => (props) => {
        if(props.number > 10) {
          return <div>
            <h3>Warning! Big number ahead.</h3>
            <Original {...props} />
          </div>
        } else {
          return <Original {...props} />
        }
      }
    }
  }
}

// Alternatively, here's the same component wrapper defined as a class.
const MyWrapComponentPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    wrapComponents: {
      NumberDisplay: (Original, system) => class WrappedNumberDisplay extends React.component {
        render() {
          if(props.number > 10) {
            return <div>
              <h3>Warning! Big number ahead.</h3>
              <Original {...props} />
            </div>
          } else {
            return <Original {...props} />
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Configure npm Overrides for Older React Versions with Swagger Editor
DESCRIPTION: Example `package.json` configuration using npm `overrides` to force `swagger-editor@4` to use a specific older version of React (e.g., React 17) and a compatible `react-redux` version. This ensures dependency resolution aligns with your application's React version.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor.md#_snippet_12

LANGUAGE: json
CODE:
```
{
  "dependencies": {
    "react": "=17.0.2",
    "react-dom": "=17.0.2"
  },
  "overrides": {
    "swagger-editor": {
      "react": "$react",
      "react": "$react-dom",
      "react-redux": "^8"
    }
  }
}
```

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import leftPad from "left-pad"

const MyFnPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    fn: {
      leftPad: leftPad
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Defining Amazon API Gateway Custom Authorizer with OpenAPI Extensions
DESCRIPTION: This YAML example illustrates how to integrate Amazon API Gateway custom authorizer details into an OpenAPI 3.0 specification using vendor extensions. It defines an `apiKey` security scheme named `APIGatewayAuthorizer` in the `components.securitySchemes` section, utilizing `x-amazon-apigateway-authtype` for the authorizer type and `x-amazon-apigateway-authorizer` to configure the token-based authorizer's URI, credentials, identity validation, and result TTL.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/openapi-extensions.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  securitySchemes:
    APIGatewayAuthorizer:
      type: apiKey
      name: Authorization
      in: header
      x-amazon-apigateway-authtype: oauth2
      x-amazon-apigateway-authorizer:
        type: token
        authorizerUri: arn:aws:apigateway:us-east-1:lambda:path/2015-03-31/functions/arn:aws:lambda:us-east-1:account-id:function:function-name/invocations
        authorizerCredentials: arn:aws:iam::account-id:role
        identityValidationExpression: "^x-[a-z]+"
        authorizerResultTtlInSeconds: 60
```

TITLE: Defining HTTP Status Codes for API Responses in OpenAPI 2
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define multiple HTTP status codes for an API response, including successful (200) and various error codes (400, 401, 404), each with a descriptive message. Markdown can be used for rich text.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
responses:
  200:
    description: OK
  400:
    description: Bad request. User ID must be an integer and bigger than 0.
  401:
    description: Authorization information is missing or invalid.
  404:
    description: A user with the specified ID was not found.
```

TITLE: Download Swagger Codegen CLI (v2 and v3) and Display Help
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to download the stable 2.x.x and 3.x.x branches of the Swagger Codegen CLI JAR files from Maven.org using `wget`. It also shows how to execute the downloaded JARs to display their respective help messages, requiring a Java 8 runtime or higher.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v2/prerequisites.md#_snippet_0

```
# Download current stable 2.x.x branch (Swagger and OpenAPI version 2)
wget https://repo1.maven.org/maven2/io/swagger/swagger-codegen-cli/2.4.44/swagger-codegen-cli-2.4.44.jar -O swagger-codegen-cli.jar

java -jar swagger-codegen-cli.jar help

# Download current stable 3.x.x branch (OpenAPI version 3)
wget https://repo1.maven.org/maven2/io/swagger/codegen/v3/swagger-codegen-cli/3.0.65/swagger-codegen-cli-3.0.65.jar -O swagger-codegen-cli.jar
```

TITLE: HTTP Request Example for File Upload with Additional Form Data
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates the HTTP `POST` request payload for uploading a file along with other form fields, demonstrating multiple parts in the `multipart/form-data` body.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/file-upload.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: HTTP
CODE:
```
POST /upload
Host: example.com
Content-Type: multipart/form-data; boundary=abcde12345
Content-Length: 332

--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="upfile"; filename="example.txt"
Content-Type: text/plain

File contents go here.
--abcde12345
Content-Disposition: form-data; name="note"

Uploading a file named "example.txt"
--abcde12345--
```

TITLE: Implement a Wrap-Action to Override/Listen to Core Actions
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to create a wrap-action to override or listen to the behavior of an existing action in the Swagger UI system. It's crucial to call `oriAction` to ensure the original action fires, allowing for conditional execution or side effects.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
// this plugin allows you to watch changes to the spec that is in memory
const MyWrapActionPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    statePlugins: {
      spec: {
        wrapActions: {
          updateSpec: (oriAction, system) => (str) => {
            // here, you can hand the value to some function that exists outside of Swagger UI
            console.log("Here is my API definition", str)
            return oriAction(str) // don't forget! otherwise, Swagger UI won't update
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

```
package com.mycompany.swagger.codegen;

    }
}
```

TITLE: Defining 401 Unauthorized Response in OpenAPI Specification 2
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define a reusable 401 'Unauthorized' response in OpenAPI Specification version 2, including referencing it from multiple operations and specifying the `WWW-Authenticate` header in the global `responses` section.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/basic-authentication.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /something:
    get:
      ...
      responses:
        ...
        401:
            $ref: '#/responses/UnauthorizedError'
    post:
      ...
      responses:
        ...
        401:
          $ref: '#/responses/UnauthorizedError'
responses:
  UnauthorizedError:
    description: Authentication information is missing or invalid
    headers:
      WWW_Authenticate:
        type: string
```

TITLE: Swagger UI Instance Methods for Authorization
DESCRIPTION: Documents methods available for programmatic control over authorization schemes in Swagger UI, including OAuth initialization and pre-authorization for Basic and API Key schemes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/configuration.md#_snippet_18

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Method: initOAuth
  Docker variable: See oauth2.md
  Description: (configObj) => void. Provide Swagger UI with information about your OAuth server - see the OAuth 2.0 documentation for more information.

Method: preauthorizeBasic
  Docker variable: Unavailable
  Description: (authDefinitionKey, username, password) => action. Programmatically set values for a Basic authorization scheme.

Method: preauthorizeApiKey
  Docker variable: Unavailable
  Description: (authDefinitionKey, apiKeyValue) => action. Programmatically set values for an API key or Bearer authorization scheme. In case of OpenAPI 3.0 Bearer scheme, `apiKeyValue` must contain just the token itself without the `Bearer` prefix.
```

```
123e4567-e89b-12d3-a456-426655440000
--abcde12345

{…file content…}
```

TITLE: Control Documentation and Test Generation in Swagger Codegen
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates how to disable the generation of documentation and tests for APIs and models using specific system properties (e.g., `-DapiTests=false`, `-DmodelDocs=false`). These options default to true and provide independent control over test and documentation output without affecting component generation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/generation-selective.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
# generate only models (with tests and documentation)
java -Dmodels {opts}

# generate only models (with tests but no documentation)
java -Dmodels -DmodelDocs=false {opts}

# generate only User and Pet models (no tests and no documentation)
java -Dmodels=User,Pet -DmodelTests=false {opts}

# generate only apis (without tests)
java -Dapis -DapiTests=false {opts}

# generate only apis (modelTests option is ignored)
java -Dapis -DmodelTests=false {opts}
```
