TITLE: Define Constant Parameters in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Explains how to define a constant parameter as a required parameter with only one possible value using the `enum` keyword. This ensures the client always sends a specific value. The example demonstrates a `rel_date` query parameter that must always be 'now'.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_18

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
parameters:
  - in: query
    name: rel_date
    required: true
    schema:
      type: string
      enum:
        - now
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI Specification v2 Parameter Types Overview
DESCRIPTION: Documents the different types of parameters supported by OpenAPI Specification v2 (Swagger), categorized by their location (`in` key). Includes query, path, header, body, and form parameters with their characteristics.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Parameter Types (OpenAPI Specification v2):
  - Query Parameters:
      Location: in: query
      Example: /users?role=admin
      Description: Appear at the end of the request URL after a question mark (?), with name=value pairs separated by ampersands (&). Can be required or optional. Support primitive types or arrays of primitive types.
  - Path Parameters:
      Location: in: path
      Example: /users/{id}
      Description: Components of a URL path that can vary, typically used to point to a specific resource. Denoted with curly braces {}. Always required.
  - Header Parameters:
      Location: in: header
      Example: X-MyHeader: Value
      Description: Passed in the request header.
  - Body Parameters:
      Location: (implied by request body)
      Description: Describe the body of POST, PUT, and PATCH requests.
  - Form Parameters:
      Location: (implied by Content-Type)
      Description: A variety of body parameters used for requests with Content-Type of application/x-www-form-urlencoded and multipart/form-data (e.g., file uploads).
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Define Global API MIME Types in OpenAPI (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to define global `consumes` and `produces` MIME types at the root level of an OpenAPI Specification. These types are inherited by all API operations unless explicitly overridden at the operation level.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/mime-types.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
consumes:
  - application/json
  - application/xml
produces:
  - application/json
  - application/xml
```

TITLE: Extend Swagger UI Plugin Functionality with System Reference
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript snippet illustrates how a plugin receives the `system` object as an argument, enabling it to access and extend functionality from other plugins. It shows an `ExtendingPlugin` calling `system.normalActions.doStuff`, highlighting the importance of loading dependent plugins after their dependencies.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const ExtendingPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    statePlugins: {
      extending: {
        actions: {
          doExtendedThings: function(...args) {
            // you can do other things in here if you want
            return system.normalActions.doStuff(...args)
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

```
        swagger-codegen-cli generate - Generate code with chosen lang
```

TITLE: Specifying XML and HTML Examples in OpenAPI

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:

```
content:
  application/xml:
    schema:
      $ref: "#/components/schemas/xml"
    examples:
      xml:
        summary: A sample XML response
        value: "<objects><object><id>1</id><name>new</name></object><object><id>2</id></object></objects>"
  text/html:
    schema:
      type: string
    examples:
      html:
        summary: A list containing two items
        value: "<html><body><ul><li>item 1</li><li>item 2</li></ul></body></html>"
```

TITLE: Display Language-Specific Configuration Options for PHP

TITLE: Define Reusable Data Models with `definitions` (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet shows how to define a reusable `User` data model within the global `definitions` section of an OpenAPI specification. It specifies `id` (integer) and `name` (string) properties and marks them as required. This model can then be referenced throughout the API for consistency.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/basic-structure.md#_snippet_9

CODE:

```
  User:
    properties:
      id:
        type: integer
      name:
        type: string
    # Both properties are required
    required:
      - id
      - name
```

TITLE: OpenAPI 2.0 Authentication Keywords Reference (APIDOC)
DESCRIPTION: This API documentation entry details the structure and usage of the `securityDefinitions` and `security` keywords in OpenAPI Specification v2.0. It outlines the properties for defining various security schemes (basic, apiKey, oauth2) and explains how to apply them globally or per operation, including the logical rules for combining multiple authentication requirements.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/authentication.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
OpenAPI 2.0 Authentication Keywords:
  securityDefinitions:
    Purpose: Defines all security schemes supported by the API.
    Type: Map (name -> SecuritySchemeObject)
    Properties of SecuritySchemeObject:
      type: string (required)
        Values: "basic", "apiKey", "oauth2"
      in: string (required for apiKey)
        Values: "header", "query"
        Description: The location of the API key.
      name: string (required for apiKey)
        Description: The name of the header or query parameter to be used.
      flow: string (required for oauth2)
        Values: "implicit", "password", "application", "accessCode"
        Description: The OAuth2 flow.
      authorizationUrl: string (required for oauth2, if flow is implicit or accessCode)
        Description: The URL of the authorization endpoint.
      tokenUrl: string (required for oauth2, if flow is password, application or accessCode)
        Description: The URL of the token endpoint.
      scopes: object (optional for oauth2)
        Description: A map of scope name to description.

  security:
    Purpose: Applies defined security schemes to the whole API or individual operations.
    Type: Array of HashMaps
    Logic:
      - Items within a hashmap are combined using logical AND (all must be met).
      - Array items are combined using logical OR (any one can be used).
    Example Structure:
      - SchemeA: [scope1, scope2]
        SchemeB: []
      - SchemeC: []
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Override Path Parameters at Operation Level in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how a path-level parameter can be overridden by an operation-specific definition. While the 'delete' operation reuses the path-level 'id', the 'get' operation overrides it to accept a comma-separated list of IDs, showcasing flexibility in parameter definitions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_22

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{id}:
    parameters:
      - in: path
        name: id
        type: integer
        required: true
        description: The user ID.

    # DELETE /users/{id} - uses a single ID.
    # Reuses the {id} parameter definition from the path level.
    delete:
      summary: Deletes the user with the specified ID.
      responses:
        204:
          description: User was deleted.

    # GET /users/id1,id2,id3 - uses one or more user IDs.
    # Overrides the path-level {id} parameter.
    get:
      summary: Gets one or more users by ID.
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: id
          required: true
          description: A comma-separated list of user IDs.
          type: array
          items:
            type: integer
          collectionFormat: csv
          minItems: 1
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Swagger Server Override Configuration for Links
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to override the default server URL for a specific operation within Swagger/OpenAPI links. This allows an operation to target a different API endpoint than the globally defined servers.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/links.md#_snippet_13

CODE:
```
servers:
  - url: https://api.example.com
---
links:

    operationId: getUser
    parameters:
      userId: "$response.body#/id"
    server:
      url: https://new-api.example.com/v2
```

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 `allowReserved` for URL-Encoded Form Data
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to use the `allowReserved: true` keyword within the `encoding` section of an OpenAPI 3.0 schema to prevent percent-encoding of reserved characters in specific form field values ('bar', 'baz').
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Describing Request Body/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
requestBody:
  content:
    application/x-www-form-urlencoded:
      schema:
        type: object
        properties:
          foo:
            type: string
          bar:
            type: string
          baz:
            type: string
      encoding:
        # Don't percent-encode reserved characters in the values of "bar" and "baz" fields
        bar:
          allowReserved: true
        baz:
          allowReserved: true
```

TITLE: Defining and Applying Basic Authentication in OpenAPI Specification 2
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to define Basic authentication using `securityDefinitions` with `type: basic` and apply it globally to an entire API or to specific operations within `paths` in OpenAPI Specification version 2.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/basic-authentication.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
securityDefinitions:
  basicAuth:
    type: basic

# To apply Basic auth to the whole API:
security:
  - basicAuth: []

paths:
  /something:
    get:
      # To apply Basic auth to an individual operation:
      security:
        - basicAuth: []
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK (successfully authenticated)
```

TITLE: Define API Responses with Status Codes and Schemas (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to define API responses for a GET operation on a `/users/{userId}` endpoint. It includes various HTTP status codes (200, 400, 404, default) with descriptions and a detailed schema for the 200 OK response, including properties and examples. This shows how to specify the structure of successful and error responses.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/basic-structure.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{userId}:
    get:
      summary: Returns a user by ID.
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: userId
          required: true
          type: integer
          minimum: 1
          description: The ID of the user to return.
      responses:
        200:
          description: A User object.
          schema:
            type: object
            properties:
              id:
                type: integer
                example: 4
              name:
                type: string
                example: Arthur Dent
        400:
          description: The specified user ID is invalid (e.g. not a number).
        404:
          description: A user with the specified ID was not found.
        default:
          description: Unexpected error
```

TITLE: Swagger UI requestSnippets Configuration
DESCRIPTION: Defines the configuration for the requestSnippets plugin, including available code generators and display settings.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/configuration.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
requestSnippets:
  type: Object
  description: Default configuration section for the requestSnippets plugin.
  properties:
    generators: Object - Defines available code snippet generators.
      curl_bash: Object - Configuration for cURL (bash).
        title: String - Display title (e.g., "cURL (bash)").
        syntax: String - Syntax highlighting language (e.g., "bash").
      curl_powershell: Object - Configuration for cURL (PowerShell).
        title: String - Display title (e.g., "cURL (PowerShell)").
        syntax: String - Syntax highlighting language (e.g., "powershell").
      curl_cmd: Object - Configuration for cURL (CMD).
        title: String - Display title (e.g., "cURL (CMD)").
        syntax: String - Syntax highlighting language (e.g., "bash").
    defaultExpanded: Boolean - Whether the section is expanded by default.
    languages: Array<String> | null - List of specific generators to show (e.g., ["curl_bash"]). Null shows all.
```

TITLE: Applying API Key Security Globally and Per Operation
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to apply defined API key security schemes at the global level (affecting all operations) or at the operation level for specific endpoints within an OpenAPI Specification v2 document. This allows for flexible security application.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/api-keys.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
# Global security (applies to all operations):
security:
  - APIKeyHeader: []
paths:
  /something:
    get:
      # Operation-specific security:
      security:
        - APIKeyQueryParam: []
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK (successfully authenticated)
```

TITLE: Defining Security Schemes in OpenAPI 2.0 (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to define various authentication methods using the `securityDefinitions` keyword in OpenAPI Specification v2.0. It maps arbitrary names to security scheme definitions, specifying their type (basic, apiKey, oauth2) along with relevant properties like `in`, `name`, `flow`, `authorizationUrl`, `tokenUrl`, and `scopes`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/authentication.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
securityDefinitions:
  BasicAuth:
    type: basic
  ApiKeyAuth:
    type: apiKey
    in: header
    name: X-API-Key
  OAuth2:
    type: oauth2
    flow: accessCode
    authorizationUrl: https://example.com/oauth/authorize
    tokenUrl: https://example.com/oauth/token
    scopes:
      read: Grants read access
      write: Grants write access
      admin: Grants read and write access to administrative information
```

TITLE: Customize XML Property Element Name in OpenAPI Schema
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to rename a specific property's XML element using the `xml/name` property within the property definition in OpenAPI 3.0, affecting only that property's representation.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/representing-xml.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
components:
  schemas:
    book:
      type: object
      properties:
        id:
          type: integer
        title:
          type: string
          xml:
            name: "xml-title"
        author:
          type: string
```

LANGUAGE: XML
CODE:
```
<book>
  <id>0</id>
  <xml-title>string</xml-title>
  <author>string</author>
</book>
```

TITLE: Convert OpenAPI Schema Property to XML Attribute

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI Cookie Parameter Serialization Styles
DESCRIPTION: Details that cookie parameters consistently use the 'form' style in OpenAPI. It illustrates how the 'explode' keyword can be used to control the serialization of array and object values within cookies.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/serialization.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Cookie parameters always use the `form` style. An optional `explode` keyword controls the array and object serialization. Given the cookie named `id`, the cookie value is serialized as follows:

| style   | explode | URI template | Primitive value id = 5 | Array id = [3, 4, 5] | Object id = {"role": "admin", "firstName": "Alex"} |
| ------- | ------- | ------------ | ---------------------- | -------------------- | -------------------------------------------------- |
| form *  | true *  |              | Cookie: id=5           |                      |                                                    |
| form    | false   | id={id}      | Cookie: id=5           | Cookie: id=3,4,5     | Cookie: id=role,admin,firstName,Alex               |

- Default serialization method
```

TITLE: Generate Specific Files within Components
DESCRIPTION: To further refine generation, pass a comma-separated list of desired file names to the system properties. This allows for generating only specific models (e.g., User, Pet) or individual supporting files (e.g., StringUtil.java) instead of all files within a component type.

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
# generate the User and Pet models only
-Dmodels=User,Pet

# generate the User model and the supportingFile `StringUtil.java`:
-Dmodels=User -DsupportingFiles=StringUtil.java
```

TITLE: Embed Base64-Encoded File in JSON Response in OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to embed a base64-encoded file, like an avatar image, within a JSON response body. The file content is represented as `type: string` with `format: byte`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/me:
    get:
      summary: Returns user information
      responses:
        "200":
          description: A JSON object containing user name and avatar
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                type: object
                properties:
                  username:
                    type: string
                  avatar: # <-- image embedded into JSON
                    type: string
                    format: byte
                    description: Base64-encoded contents of the avatar image
```

```
- additionalItems
- const
- contains
- dependencies
- id
- $id
- patternProperties
- propertyNames
```

TITLE: Define Form Parameters in Swagger/OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Describes how to use 'in: formData' for requests with 'application/x-www-form-urlencoded' or 'multipart/form-data' content types. It clarifies that form parameters cannot coexist with 'in: body' and provides an HTML form example along with its Swagger YAML definition.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: html
CODE:
```
<form action="http://example.com/survey" method="post">
  <input type="text" name="name" />
  <input type="number" name="fav_number" />
  <input type="submit" />
</form>
```

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
POST /survey HTTP/1.1
Host: example.com
Content-Type: application/x-www-form-urlencoded
Content-Length: 29

name=Amy+Smith&fav_number=321
```

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /survey:
    post:
      summary: A sample survey.
      consumes:
        - application/x-www-form-urlencoded
      parameters:
        - in: formData
          name: name
          type: string
          description: A person's name.
        - in: formData
          name: fav_number
          type: number
          description: A person's favorite number.
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Initialize SwaggerUI with SwaggerEditor Preview Plugins
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript code snippet demonstrates how to initialize SwaggerUI and integrate preview plugins from `swagger-editor` such as `EditorContentTypePlugin`, `EditorPreviewAsyncAPIPlugin`, and `EditorPreviewAPIDesignSystemsPlugin`. The `SwaggerUIAdapterPlugin` is crucial for adapting SwaggerEditor plugins for direct use with SwaggerUI.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_24

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import SwaggerUI from 'swagger-ui';
import SwaggerUIStandalonePreset from 'swagger-ui/dist/swagger-ui-standalone-preset';
import 'swagger-editor/swagger-editor.css';
import EditorContentTypePlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-content-type';
import EditorPreviewAsyncAPIPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-asyncapi';
import EditorPreviewAPIDesignSystemsPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/editor-preview-api-design-systems';
import SwaggerUIAdapterPlugin from 'swagger-editor/plugins/swagger-ui-adapter';

SwaggerUI({
  url: 'https://petstore.swagger.io/v2/swagger.json',
  dom_id: '#swagger-ui',
  presets: [SwaggerUI.presets.apis, SwaggerUIStandalonePreset],
  plugins: [
    EditorContentTypePlugin,
    EditorPreviewAsyncAPIPlugin,
    EditorPreviewAPIDesignSystemsPlugin,
    SwaggerUIAdapterPlugin,
    SwaggerUI.plugins.DownloadUrl,
  ],
});
```

TITLE: Generate Code with Swagger Generator Docker Image
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to use the `swaggerapi/swagger-generator` Docker image as a self-hosted web application to generate client code. It demonstrates starting the container, retrieving its IP, making an HTTP POST request to generate JavaScript client code from a Swagger URL, downloading the resulting zip file, and cleaning up the container. This example assumes `jq` is installed for JSON processing.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v2/docker.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
CID=$(docker run -d swaggerapi/swagger-generator)
sleep 5
GEN_IP=$(docker inspect --format '{{.NetworkSettings.IPAddress}}'  $CID)
RESULT=$(curl -X POST --header 'Content-Type: application/json' --header 'Accept: application/json' -d '{
  "swaggerUrl": "https://petstore.swagger.io/v2/swagger.json"
}' 'http://localhost:8188/api/gen/clients/javascript' | jq '.link' | tr -d '"')
curl $RESULT > result.zip
docker stop $CID && docker rm $CID
```

TITLE: Define Memoized Selector with Reselect in Swagger UI Plugin
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to use the Reselect library to create a memoized selector. Memoization is recommended for heavily used selectors to improve performance by caching results, preventing unnecessary re-calculations.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import { createSelector } from "reselect"

const MySelectorPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    statePlugins: {
      example: {
        selectors: {
          // this selector will be memoized after it is run once for a
          // value of `state`
          myFavoriteColor: createSelector((state) => state.get("favColor"))
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Python Client Generation Options Schema (APIDOC)
DESCRIPTION: Details the configurable options for Python client generation, including 'packageName', 'packageVersion', and 'sortParamsByRequiredFlag'. Each option specifies its type, description, and default value, guiding users on available customizations.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v2/online-generators.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
packageName:
  opt: packageName
  description: python package name (convention: snake_case).
  type: string
  default: swagger_client
packageVersion:
  opt: packageVersion
  description: python package version.
  type: string
  default: 1.0.0
sortParamsByRequiredFlag:
  opt: sortParamsByRequiredFlag
  description: Sort method arguments to place required parameters before optional parameters.
  type: boolean
  default: true
```

TITLE: Implementing Combined OR and AND Logic for Authentication in OpenAPI 2.0 (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates a complex combination of logical OR and AND for authentication requirements. It allows API requests to be authenticated either via OAuth 2 with specific scopes OR by providing a pair of API keys ('apiKey1' and 'apiKey2') simultaneously, offering advanced security options.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/authentication.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
security:
  - oauth2: [scope1, scope2]
  - apiKey1: []
    apiKey2: []
```

TITLE: Build and Run Unprivileged SwaggerEditor Docker Image Locally
DESCRIPTION: These shell commands outline the process to build an unprivileged Docker image for SwaggerEditor from local source and run it. SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_33

CODE:
```
$ npm run build:app
 $ docker build . -f Dockerfile.unprivileged -t swaggerapi/swagger-editor:next-v5-unprivileged
 $ docker run -d -p 8080:8080 swaggerapi/swagger-editor:next-v5-unprivileged
```

TITLE: Configure Webpack 5 with Pre-built SwaggerEditor Workers
DESCRIPTION: This alternative Webpack 5 configuration simplifies the build process by directly using pre-built Web Worker fragments from the `swagger-editor` npm package. It utilizes `copy-webpack-plugin` to move these fragments into the output directory and includes similar `resolve.fallback` and `alias` settings for browser compatibility and dependency management.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
const path = require('path');
const webpack = require('webpack');
const CopyWebpackPlugin = require('copy-webpack-plugin');

module.exports = {
  mode: 'production',
  entry: {
    app: './index.js',
  },
  output: {
    globalObject: 'self',
    filename: 'static/js/[name].js',
    path: path.resolve(__dirname, 'dist')
  },
  resolve: {
    fallback: {
      path: false,
      fs: false,
      http: require.resolve('stream-http'), // required for asyncapi parser
      https: require.resolve('https-browserify'), // required for asyncapi parser
      stream: require.resolve('stream-browserify'),
      util: require.resolve('util'),
      url: require.resolve('url'),
      zlib: false,
    },
    alias: {
      // This alias make sure we don't pull two different versions of monaco-editor
      'monaco-editor': '/node_modules/monaco-editor',
      // This alias makes sure we're avoiding a runtime error related to this package

```

TITLE: Wrap XML Arrays with a Parent Element in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to add a wrapping element around array items in XML output by setting the `xml/wrapped` property to `true` in the OpenAPI 3.0 schema definition for the array.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/representing-xml.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
books:
  type: array
  items:
    type: string
  xml:
    wrapped: true
  example:
    - "one"
    - "two"
    - "three"
```

LANGUAGE: XML
CODE:
```
<books>
  <books>one</books>
  <books>two</books>
  <books>three</books>
</books>
```

TITLE: Detailed OpenAPI 2.0 GET Operation with Parameters and Response Schema
DESCRIPTION: This comprehensive YAML snippet demonstrates a detailed `GET` operation for retrieving a user by ID in OpenAPI Specification v2.0. It includes a summary, multi-line description with Markdown support, `operationId`, `tags`, `produces` media types, and defines a required `path` parameter `id`. The snippet also specifies a `200 OK` response with a `$ref` to a `User` definition, which is provided separately, and includes `externalDocs` for additional information.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{id}:
    get:
      summary: Gets a user by ID.
      description: >
        A detailed description of the operation.
        GitHub Flavored Markdown can be used for rich text representation,
        such as **bold**, *italic* and [links](https://swagger.io).
      operationId: getUsers
      tags:
        - users
      produces:
        - application/json
        - application/xml
      parameters:
        - name: id
          in: path
          description: User ID
          type: integer
          required: true
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
          schema:
            $ref: "#/definitions/User"
      externalDocs:
        url: http://api.example.com/docs/user-operations/
        description: Learn more about User operations provided by this API.
definitions:
  User:
    type: object
    properties:
      id:
        type: integer
      name:
        type: string
    required:
      - id
      - name
```

TITLE: Examples of Standard and Vendor-Specific MIME Types (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This snippet provides a list of common standard and vendor-specific MIME types compliant with RFC 6838, which can be used in OpenAPI `consumes` and `produces` definitions to specify data formats.

```
application/xml

multipart/form-data

application/vnd.github-issue.text+json

image/vnd.djvu
```

TITLE: Defining Inline Object Examples in OpenAPI 2.0
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to provide complex inline examples for properties of type 'object' within an OpenAPI 2.0 schema. The example structure must comply with the object's schema definition.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
definitions:
  CatalogItem:
    type: object
    properties:
      id:
        type: integer
        example: 38
      title:
        type: string
        example: T-shirt
      image:
        type: object
        properties:
          url:
            type: string
          width:
            type: integer
          height:
            type: integer
        required:
          - url
        example:   # <-----
          url: images/38.png
          width: 100
          height: 100
    required:
      - id
      - title
```

TITLE: Defining Reusable Enums with YAML Anchors in OpenAPI 2
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define and reuse enum values across an OpenAPI 2 specification using YAML anchors (`&`) and references (`*`), allowing for efficient content duplication and consistency.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/enums.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
definitions:
  Colors:
    type: string
    enum: &COLORS
      - black
      - white
      - red
      - green
      - blue
    # OR:
    # enum: &COLORS [black, white, red, green, blue]

paths:
  /products:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: color
          required: true
          type: string
          enum: *COLORS
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Configure Yarn Resolutions for Older React Versions with Swagger Editor
DESCRIPTION: Example `package.json` configuration using yarn `resolutions` to force `swagger-editor@4` to use a specific older version of React (e.g., React 17) and a compatible `react-redux` version. Unlike npm, yarn requires exact versions for resolutions and does not support aliasing.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor.md#_snippet_13

LANGUAGE: json
CODE:
```
{
  "dependencies": {
    "react": "17.0.2",
    "react-dom": "17.0.2"
  },
  "resolutions": {
    "swagger-editor/react": "17.0.2",
    "swagger-editor/react-dom": "17.0.2",
    "swagger-editor/react-redux": "^8"
  }
}
```

TITLE: Swagger UI Deep Link URL Fragment Formats
DESCRIPTION: Swagger UI supports two primary URL fragment formats for deep linking: one for focusing on a specific tag and another for a specific operation within a tag. The `operationId` can be explicit or implicitly generated by combining the operation's path and method.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/deep-linking.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Fragment Formats:
  #/{tagName}
  #/{tagName}/{operationId}

operationId:
  Explicitly provided in the spec, or
  Implicitly generated by combining operation's path and method (non-alphanumeric characters escaped).
```

```
export PATH=${JAVA_HOME}/bin:$PATH
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI 3.0 Supported JSON Schema Keywords (Minor Differences)
DESCRIPTION: These keywords are supported in OpenAPI 3.0 but have slight variations in their usage or interpretation compared to standard JSON Schema.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/Data Models/keywords.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Keywords supported with minor differences:
- type: The value must be a single type, not an array. 'null' is not supported as a type; use 'nullable: true' instead.
- format: OpenAPI uses its own predefined formats and allows custom formats.
- description: Supports CommonMark syntax for rich text.
- items: Must be present if 'type' is 'array'. The item schema must be an OpenAPI schema.
- properties: Individual property definitions must follow OpenAPI schema rules.
- additionalProperties: Value can be boolean (true/false) or an OpenAPI schema.
- default: The default value must conform to the specified schema.
- allOf: Subschemas must be OpenAPI schemas.
- oneOf: Subschemas must be OpenAPI schemas.
- anyOf: Subschemas must be OpenAPI schemas.
- not: The subschema must be an OpenAPI schema.
```

```
  type: String

```

TITLE: OpenAPI Example Precedence Rules
DESCRIPTION: Describes the order of precedence for examples defined at different levels within an OpenAPI specification. Higher-level examples override lower-level ones, ensuring clarity on which example is applied by tools processing the spec.

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:

```
Example Precedence Order:
1. Response example
2. Schema example
3. Object and array property examples
4. Atomic property examples and array item examples
```

TITLE: OpenAPI 2.0 Example Limitations with $ref
DESCRIPTION: Explains that OpenAPI 2.0's `example` and `examples` keywords require inline examples and do not support `$ref` for referencing external examples. Referencing examples is only supported in OpenAPI 3.0.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/adding-examples.md#_snippet_11

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
OpenAPI 2.0 Example and Examples Keywords:
- Require inline examples.
- Do not support $ref.
- $ref would be displayed as an object property named $ref.
Referencing examples is supported in OpenAPI 3.0.
```

TITLE: OpenAPI Paths Before Component Refactoring
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates an OpenAPI specification where common data structures, such as the 'User' object, are defined inline and duplicated across different API paths, leading to redundancy.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/components.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{userId}:
    get:
      summary: Get a user by ID
      parameters: ...
      responses:
        "200":
          description: A single user.
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                type: object
                properties:
                  id:
                    type: integer
                  name:
                    type: string
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Get all users
      responses:
        "200":
          description: A list of users.
          content:
            application/json:
              schema:
                type: array
                items:
                  type: object
                  properties:
                    id:
                      type: integer
                    name:
                      type: string
```

TITLE: OpenAPI `collectionFormat` Options for Array Parameters
DESCRIPTION: Details the `collectionFormat` options available in OpenAPI/Swagger for array parameters, specifying how multiple values are serialized and transmitted. Includes examples for `csv`, `ssv`, `tsv`, `pipes`, and `multi` formats.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_14

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
collectionFormat:
  csv (default):
    Description: Comma-separated values.
    Example: foo,bar,baz
  ssv:
    Description: Space-separated values.
    Example: foo bar baz
  tsv:
    Description: Tab-separated values.
    Example: "foo\tbar\tbaz"
  pipes:
    Description: Pipe-separated values.
    Example: foo|bar|baz
  multi:
    Description: Multiple parameter instances rather than multiple values. This is only supported for the in: query and in: formData parameters.
    Example: foo=value&foo=another_value
```

TITLE: Using Default Response for Collective Error Handling in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet demonstrates how to use the 'default' response keyword in OpenAPI to describe all HTTP status codes not explicitly covered for an operation. This is particularly useful for consolidating the documentation of various error responses that share a common structure, simplifying the API specification.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
responses:
  200:
    description: Success
    schema:
      $ref: "#/definitions/User"
  # Definition of all error statuses
  default:
    description: Unexpected error
    schema:
      $ref: "#/definitions/Error"
```

TITLE: Complete Sample Swagger 2.0 API Definition
DESCRIPTION: This comprehensive YAML snippet presents a foundational Swagger 2.0 API definition, showcasing the integration of version, API information, host, base path, schemes, and a basic path with a GET operation. It serves as a complete structural example for an OpenAPI Specification.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/basic-structure.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:

```
swagger: "2.0"
info:
  title: Sample API
  description: API description in Markdown.
  version: 1.0.0

host: api.example.com
basePath: /v1
schemes:
  - https

paths:
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Returns a list of users.
      description: Optional extended description in Markdown.
      produces:
        - application/json
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Control Generation of Tests and Documentation
DESCRIPTION: Control the generation of tests and documentation for APIs and models by setting specific system properties to 'false'. Options like -DapiTests=false, -DapiDocs=false, -DmodelTests=false, and -DmodelDocs=false can be used to disable these outputs, which are true by default. These options do not limit the generation of the core features like -Dapis.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v2/generation-selective.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
# generate only models (with tests and documentation)
java -Dmodels {opts}

# generate only models (with tests but no documentation)
java -Dmodels -DmodelDocs=false {opts}

# generate only User and Pet models (no tests and no documentation)
java -Dmodels=User,Pet -DmodelTests=false {opts}

# generate only apis (without tests)
java -Dapis -DapiTests=false {opts}

# generate only apis (modelTests option is ignored)
java -Dapis -DmodelTests=false {opts}
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Override System Selectors with Wrap-Selectors Plugin
DESCRIPTION: The `Wrap-Selectors` interface allows overriding the behavior of existing selectors in the system. It uses a function factory signature `(oriSelector, system) => (state, ...args) => result` to control data flow into components. This is useful for modifying or disabling selector behavior based on conditions, such as API definition versions.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_15

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
import { createSelector } from 'reselect'

// FYI: in an actual Swagger UI, the `url` spec selector is already defined
// it's just here for clarity on what's behind the scenes
const MySpecPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    statePlugins: {
      spec: {
        selectors: {
          url: createSelector(
            state => state.get("url")
          )
        }
      }
    }
  }
}

const MyWrapSelectorsPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    statePlugins: {
      spec: {
        wrapSelectors: {
          url: (oriSelector, system) => (state, ...args) => {
            console.log('someone asked for the spec url!!! it is', state.get('url'))
            // you can return other values here...
            // but let's just enable the default behavior
            return oriSelector(state, ...args)
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Defining Enum for Query Parameter in OpenAPI 2
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to use the `enum` keyword to restrict possible values for a query parameter (e.g., 'sort') within an OpenAPI 2 specification, ensuring only 'asc' or 'desc' are accepted.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/enums.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /items:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: sort
          description: Sort order
          type: string
          enum: [asc, desc]
```

TITLE: Swagger UI tagsSorter Configuration
DESCRIPTION: Configures how API tags are sorted in Swagger UI. Can be 'alpha' for alphanumeric sorting or a custom JavaScript Array.prototype.sort() function.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/configuration.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
tagsSorter:
  type: Function | String
  default: (a => a) (Swagger UI default order)
  description: Applies a sort to the tag list of each API. Accepts 'alpha' or a custom sort function (Array.prototype.sort()). Two tag name strings are passed to the sorter.
  function_signature: (tagA: string, tagB: string) => number
```

TITLE: Map OpenAPI 2.0 Component References to OpenAPI 3.0
DESCRIPTION: This snippet highlights the changes in component organization and referencing between OpenAPI 2.0 and OpenAPI 3.0. It shows how `definitions`, `parameters`, and `responses` sections from OpenAPI 2.0 are consolidated under the `components` object in OpenAPI 3.0, with `definitions` renamed to `schemas` and `securityDefinitions` to `securitySchemes`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v3_0/components.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
OpenAPI 2.0                    OpenAPI 3.0
'#/definitions/User'         → '#/components/schemas/User'
'#/parameters/offsetParam'   → '#/components/parameters/offsetParam'
'#/responses/ErrorResponse'  → '#/components/responses/ErrorResponse'
```

TITLE: Special Swagger Keywords for Common HTTP Headers
DESCRIPTION: Documents specific HTTP headers (Content-Type, Accept, Authorization) and their corresponding keywords in the Swagger specification (consumes, produces, securityDefinitions, security).
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Header Keywords:
  Content-Type:
    Keywords: consumes (request content type), produces (response content type)
    More Info: MIME Types
  Accept:
    Keywords: produces
    More Info: MIME Types
  Authorization:
    Keywords: securityDefinitions, security
    More Info: Authentication
```

TITLE: Defining Custom Response Headers in OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to define custom response headers within an OpenAPI specification for a specific HTTP status code. It shows the syntax for specifying header names, types, and descriptions, providing additional context for API consumers.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
paths:
  /ping:
    get:
      summary: Checks if the server is alive.
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
          headers:
            X-RateLimit-Limit:
              type: integer
              description: Request limit per hour.
            X-RateLimit-Remaining:
              type: integer
              description: The number of requests left for the time window.
            X-RateLimit-Reset:
              type: string
              format: date-time
              description: The UTC date/time at which the current rate limit window resets.
```

TITLE: Specifying Response Media Types in OpenAPI 2
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to define global and operation-specific 'produces' media types for API responses. It shows overriding the global 'application/json' with 'image/png', 'image/gif', and 'image/jpeg' for a specific endpoint.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
produces:
  - application/json

paths:
  # This operation returns JSON - as defined globally above
  /users:
    get:
      summary: Gets a list of users.
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
  # Here, we override the "produces" array to specify other media types
  /logo:
    get:
      summary: Gets the logo image.
      produces:
        - image/png
        - image/gif
        - image/jpeg
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Override Operation-Specific MIME Types in OpenAPI (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This example shows how to override global `produces` definitions at the operation level for a specific path, such as returning an image for a GET request. Operation-level definitions take precedence over global ones, allowing for fine-grained control over accepted and returned data formats.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/mime-types.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /logo:
    get:
      summary: Returns the logo image
      produces:
        - image/png
        - image/gif
        - image/jpeg
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
          schema:
            type: file
```

TITLE: YAML Syntax for Security Scopes in Swagger/OpenAPI
DESCRIPTION: This snippet illustrates the YAML syntax for defining security requirements in Swagger/OpenAPI specifications. It shows how to specify required scopes for OAuth 2 security schemes and how to use an empty array `[]` for security schemes like BasicAuth and ApiKeyAuth where scopes are not applicable, adhering to the specification's requirement for a list of scopes.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/Authentication/authentication.md#_snippet_8

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
security:
  - securityA: [scopeA1, scopeA2]
  - securityB: [scopeB1, scopeB2]
```

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
security:
  - oauth2: [scope1, scope2]
  - BasicAuth: []
  - ApiKeyAuth: []
```

TITLE: Reusing Enum Definitions with YAML Merge Keys in OpenAPI 2
DESCRIPTION: Shows an advanced YAML technique using merge keys (`<<`) to reference both the type and enum values from a reusable definition, provided the YAML parser supports this feature.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/enums.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
definitions:
  Colors: &COLORS
    type: string
    enum: [black, white, red, green, blue]
paths:
  /products:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: query
          name: color
          required: true
          <<: *COLORS
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Reference Reusable Data Models in API Paths (YAML)
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet demonstrates how to reference a globally defined `User` data model (`#/definitions/User`) in both response schemas and request body schemas for API paths. It shows a GET operation returning a `User` object and a POST operation accepting a `User` object in the request body, promoting schema reuse and consistency.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/basic-structure.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{userId}:
    get:
      summary: Returns a user by ID.
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: userId
          required: true
          type: integer
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
          schema:
            $ref: "#/definitions/User"
  /users:
    post:
      summary: Creates a new user.
      parameters:
        - in: body
          name: user
          schema:
            $ref: "#/definitions/User"
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
```

TITLE: Referencing Reusable Response Body Schemas in OpenAPI 2
DESCRIPTION: Shows how to define a reusable schema at the root level ('definitions') and reference it within a response using '$ref'. This promotes reusability for common data structures like a User object.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
      responses:
        200:
          description: A User object
          schema:
            $ref: '#/definitions/User'
definitions:
  User:
    type: object
    properties:
      id:
        type: integer
        description: The user ID.
      username:
        type: string
        description: The user name.
```

TITLE: Defining Object Request Body with Reusable Schema in OpenAPI 2.0
DESCRIPTION: Swagger 2.0 definition demonstrating how to use a reusable schema ('#/definitions/User') for an object request body, promoting modularity and reusability in API definitions by referencing a globally defined schema.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-request-body.md#_snippet_2

LANGUAGE: yaml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users:
    post:
      summary: Creates a new user.
      consumes:
        - application/json
      parameters:
        - in: body
          name: user
          description: The user to create.
          schema:
            $ref: "#/definitions/User" # <----------
      responses:
        200:
          description: OK
definitions:
  User: # <----------
    type: object
    required:
      - userName
    properties:
      userName:
        type: string
      firstName:
        type: string
      lastName:
        type: string
```

TITLE: Extend Swagger Codegen Language Class in Java

```
    }
}
```

TITLE: Default Implementation of SwaggerUI Fallback Component
DESCRIPTION: This snippet presents the default React component for `Fallback`, which is displayed when an error boundary catches an error, providing a basic message and indicating the failed component.

```
import React from "react"
import PropTypes from "prop-types"

  <div className="fallback">
    😱 <i>Could not render { name === "t" ? "this component" : name }, see the console.</i>
  </div>
)
Fallback.propTypes = {
  name: PropTypes.string.isRequired,
}
export default Fallback
```

TITLE: Define Custom Redux Action in Swagger UI Plugin
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript example demonstrates how to define a new Redux action creator within a Swagger UI plugin. The `updateFavoriteColor` action is created under the `example` state namespace and returns a Flux Standard Action, which will be processed by a corresponding reducer.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const MyActionPlugin = () => {
  return {
    statePlugins: {
      example: {
        actions: {
          updateFavoriteColor: (str) => {
            return {
              type: "EXAMPLE_SET_FAV_COLOR",
              payload: str
            }
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Define Custom Reducer in Swagger UI Plugin
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript example illustrates how to define a reducer within a Swagger UI plugin. Reducers handle specific action types (e.g., `EXAMPLE_SET_FAV_COLOR`), take an Immutable.js map state and an action, and return a new state, operating only on their designated namespace.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
const MyReducerPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    statePlugins: {
      example: {
        reducers: {
          "EXAMPLE_SET_FAV_COLOR": (state, action) => {
            // you're only working with the state under the namespace, in this case "example".
            // So you can do what you want, without worrying about /other/ namespaces
            return state.set("favColor", action.payload)
          }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Documenting Multiple Error Responses with Same Structure
DESCRIPTION: This example shows how an API operation might return different HTTP error status codes (e.g., 400, 404) that, despite their distinct codes, share the same underlying response schema. This approach can lead to repetitive schema references in the OpenAPI definition.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-responses.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
responses:
  200:
    description: Success
    schema:
      $ref: "#/definitions/User"
  400:
    description: Bad request
    schema:
      $ref: "#/definitions/Error"
  404:
    description: Not found
    schema:
      $ref: "#/definitions/Error"
```

TITLE: Define Class and Stateless Components in Swagger UI Plugin
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to provide both class-based React components and functional (stateless) components to the Swagger UI plugin system. Components are integrated into the system via a map, allowing for flexible UI customization.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plugin-api.md#_snippet_9

LANGUAGE: javascript
CODE:
```
class HelloWorldClass extends React.Component {
  render() {
    return <h1>Hello World!</h1>
  }
}

const MyComponentPlugin = function(system) {
  return {
    components: {
      HelloWorldClass: HelloWorldClass,
      // components can just be functions, these are called "stateless components"
      HelloWorldStateless: () => <h1>Hello World!</h1>
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Example: Amazon API Gateway Custom Authorizer Extension in OpenAPI v2
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to define a custom authorizer for Amazon API Gateway within an OpenAPI Specification v2 using `x-amazon-apigateway-authtype` and `x-amazon-apigateway-authorizer` extensions under `securityDefinitions`.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/swagger-extensions.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
securityDefinitions:
  APIGatewayAuthorizer:
    type: apiKey
    name: Authorization
    in: header
    x-amazon-apigateway-authtype: oauth2
    x-amazon-apigateway-authorizer:
      type: token
      authorizerUri: arn:aws:apigateway:us-east-1:lambda:path/2015-03-31/functions/arn:aws:lambda:us-east-1:account-id:function:function-name/invocations
      authorizerCredentials: arn:aws:iam::account-id:role
      identityValidationExpression: "^x-[a-z]+"
      authorizerResultTtlInSeconds: 60
```

TITLE: Swagger Extensions (OpenAPI v2) Definition
DESCRIPTION: Defines the concept and usage of vendor extensions in OpenAPI Specification v2, detailing their prefix, supported locations within the API definition, and acceptable value types.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/swagger-extensions.md#_snippet_0

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
Swagger Extensions (Vendor Extensions):
  Prefix: x-
  Purpose: Describe extra functionality not covered by standard Swagger specification.
  Supported Locations:
    - Root level of the API spec
    - info section
    - paths section, individual paths and operations
    - operation parameters
    - responses
    - tags
    - security schemes
  Value Types:
    - Primitive (string, number, boolean)
    - Array
    - Object
    - null
  Object/Array Property Names: Do not need to start with x-
```

TITLE: Configure Webpack 5 for SwaggerEditor with Worker Bundling
DESCRIPTION: This Webpack 5 configuration bundles the main application along with `apidom.worker.js` and `editor.worker.js` as separate entry points. It includes `resolve.fallback` for browser compatibility, `alias` for `monaco-editor` and `@stoplight/ordered-object-literal`, and a rule for handling WASM files, ensuring all necessary components are correctly processed.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_4

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
const path = require('path');
const webpack = require('webpack');

module.exports = {
  mode: 'production',
  entry: {
    app: './index.js',
    'apidom.worker': 'swagger-editor/apidom.worker',
    'editor.worker': 'swagger-editor/editor.worker',
  },
  output: {
    globalObject: 'self',
    filename: '[name].js',
    path: path.resolve(__dirname, 'dist')
  },
  resolve: {
    fallback: {
      path: false,
      fs: false,
      http: require.resolve('stream-http'), // required for asyncapi parser
      https: require.resolve('https-browserify'), // required for asyncapi parser
      stream: require.resolve('stream-browserify'),
      util: require.resolve('util'),
      url: require.resolve('url'),
      zlib: false,
    },
    alias: {
      // This alias make sure we don't pull two different versions of monaco-editor
      'monaco-editor': '/node_modules/monaco-editor',
      // This alias makes sure we're avoiding a runtime error related to this package
      '@stoplight/ordered-object-literal$': '/node_modules/@stoplight/ordered-object-literal/src/index.mjs',
    },
  },
  plugins: [
    new webpack.ProvidePlugin({
      Buffer: ['buffer', 'Buffer'],
    }),
  ],
  module: {
    rules: [
      {
        test: /\.css$/,
        use: ['style-loader', 'css-loader']
      },
      /**
       * The default way in which webpack loads wasm files won’t work in a worker,
       * so we will have to disable webpack’s default handling of wasm files and
       * then fetch the wasm file by using the file path that we get using file-loader.
       *
       * Resource: https://pspdfkit.com/blog/2020/webassembly-in-a-web-worker/
       *
       * Alternatively, WASM file can be bundled directly into JavaScript bundle as data URLs.
       * This configuration reduces the complexity of WASM file loading
       * but increases the overal bundle size:
       *
       * {
       *   test: /\.wasm$/,
       *   type: 'asset/inline',
       * }
       */
      {
        test: /\.wasm$/,
        loader: 'file-loader',
        type: 'javascript/auto', // this disables webpacks default handling of wasm
      },
    ]
  }
};
```

TITLE: Define Specific Path Parameter for User ID in OpenAPI YAML
DESCRIPTION: Demonstrates how to define a specific `id` path parameter for a GET `/users/{id}` operation in OpenAPI Specification (Swagger) YAML, including its type, minimum value, and requirement. Emphasizes that the parameter name must match the path.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/describing-parameters.md#_snippet_5

LANGUAGE: yml
CODE:
```
paths:
  /users/{id}:
    get:
      parameters:
        - in: path
          name: id   # Note the name is the same as in the path
          required: true
          type: integer
          minimum: 1
          description: The user ID.
        responses:
          200:
            description: OK
```

TITLE: Configuring SwaggerUI Safe-Render Plugin to Protect Custom Components
DESCRIPTION: This example demonstrates how to configure the `safe-render` plugin with `fullOverride` and `componentList` options to protect additional custom components within a SwaggerUI instance, useful for integrators with custom plugins.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Customization/plug-points.md#_snippet_10

LANGUAGE: js
CODE:
```
const swaggerUI = SwaggerUI({
  url: "https://petstore.swagger.io/v2/swagger.json",
  dom_id: '#swagger-ui',
  plugins: [
    () => ({
      components: {
        MyCustomComponent1: () => 'my custom component',
      },
    }),
    SwaggerUI.plugins.SafeRender({
      fullOverride: true, // only the component list defined here will apply (not the default list)
      componentList: [
        "MyCustomComponent1",
      ],
    }),
  ],
});
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: OpenAPI 2.0 Path Templating Syntax
DESCRIPTION: This YAML snippet illustrates the syntax for path templating in OpenAPI Specification v2.0. Curly braces `{}` are used to define path parameters, allowing for dynamic parts in the URL. Examples include single parameters like `{id}` and multiple parameters like `{orgId}/{memberId}`, as well as format specifiers like `{format}`. API clients must provide values for these parameters.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/specification/v2_0/paths-and-operations.md#_snippet_1

LANGUAGE: YAML
CODE:
```
/users/{id}
/organizations/{orgId}/members/{memberId}
/report.{format}
```

DESCRIPTION: This shell command stops a running Docker container identified by `$CID` and then removes it. This is typically used for cleaning up temporary or background Swagger Codegen generator instances.

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```

```

TITLE: SwaggerEditor Package.json Build Artifact Mapping
DESCRIPTION: This JSON snippet from `package.json` illustrates how SwaggerEditor maps its various build artifacts to different fields (`unpkg`, `module`, `browser`, `jsnext:main`, `exports`). This configuration guides module bundlers and environments on which file to use for different consumption scenarios.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_21

LANGUAGE: JSON
CODE:
```
"unpkg": "./dist/umd/swagger-editor.js",
"module": "./dist/esm/swagger-editor.js",
"browser": "./dist/esm/swagger-editor.js",
"jsnext:main": "./dist/esm/swagger-editor.js",
"exports": {
  "./package.json": "./package.json",
  "./swagger-editor.css": "./dist/swagger-editor.css",
  ".": {
    "browser": "./dist/esm/swagger-editor.js"
  },
  "./plugins/*": {
    "browser": "./dist/esm/plugins/*/index.js"
  },
  "./presets/*": {
    "browser": "./dist/esm/presets/*/index.js"
  },
  "./apidom.worker": {
    "browser": "./dist/esm/apidom.worker.js"
  },
  "./editor.worker": {
    "browser": "./dist/esm/editor.worker.js"
  }
}
```

TITLE: Set JAVA_HOME and PATH for Java 11 (macOS)
DESCRIPTION: Illustrates how to correctly set the `JAVA_HOME` environment variable to point to Java 11 and update the system's `PATH` on macOS. This is crucial for building Swagger Codegen from source or ensuring the correct Java version is used.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger Codegen/Codegen v3/prerequisites.md#_snippet_3

LANGUAGE: sh
CODE:
```
export JAVA_HOME=`/usr/libexec/java_home -v 11`
export PATH=${JAVA_HOME}/bin:$PATH
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Webpack Configuration for SwaggerEditor
DESCRIPTION: This JavaScript configuration defines how Webpack processes and bundles the SwaggerEditor project. It includes providing Buffer, copying worker files (apidom.worker.js, editor.worker.js) to the static/js directory, and handling CSS files using style-loader and css-loader.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_7

LANGUAGE: JavaScript
CODE:
```
{
  '@stoplight/ordered-object-literal$': '/node_modules/@stoplight/ordered-object-literal/src/index.mjs',
  }
},
plugins: [
  new webpack.ProvidePlugin({
    Buffer: ['buffer', 'Buffer'],
  }),
  new CopyWebpackPlugin({
    patterns: [
      {
        from: 'node_modules/swagger-editor/dist/umd/apidom.worker.js',
        to: 'static/js',
      },
      {
        from: 'node_modules/swagger-editor/dist/umd/editor.worker.js',
        to: 'static/js',
      }
    ]
  }),
],
module: {
  rules: [
    {
      test: /\.css$/,
      use: ['style-loader', 'css-loader']
    },
  ]
}
};
```

----------------------------------------

TITLE: Configure npm Overrides for SwaggerEditor with React 17
DESCRIPTION: This JSON configuration demonstrates how to use npm overrides to force `swagger-editor@5` to use React 17.0.2 and react-dom 17.0.2. It also specifies `react-redux@8` as `react-redux@9` requires React 18.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/swagger-editor-next.md#_snippet_22

LANGUAGE: json
CODE:
```
{
  "dependencies": {
    "react": "=17.0.2",
    "react-dom": "=17.0.2"
  },
  "overrides": {
    "swagger-editor": {
      "react": "$react",
      "react": "$react-dom",
      "react-redux": "^8"
    }
  }
}
```

TITLE: Swagger UI useUnsafeMarkdown Configuration
DESCRIPTION: Controls whether the sanitizer leaves style, class, and data-* attributes untouched in HTML elements within markdown strings. This parameter is deprecated.
SOURCE: https://github.com/swagger-api/swagger.io-docs/blob/main/src/content/docs/open-source-tools/Swagger UI/Usage/configuration.md#_snippet_6

LANGUAGE: APIDOC
CODE:
```
useUnsafeMarkdown:
  type: Boolean
  default: false
  description: When enabled, sanitizer leaves 'style', 'class', and 'data-*' attributes untouched on HTML Elements in markdown. Deprecated; will be removed in 4.0.0.
```
